صاحب کتاب نے تیسری صورت بیان کی ہے کہ اگر عورت کے ساتھ دخول ہو گیا اور مہر مقتل ہے تو امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک یہی حکم ہے۔ یعنی عورت کو حق منع حاصل ہے۔ اور صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ دخول کے بعد عورت کو حق منع حاصل نہیں ہوگا۔ یہ بات یادر ہے کہ امام صاحب اور صاحبین کا اختلاف اس صورت میں ہے جبکہ دخول عورت کی رضا مندی سے ہوا ہو۔ چنانچہ اگر عورت سے زبردستی کی گئی یا وہ بچی ہے یا دیوانی تو بالاتفاق اس کا حق جبس ساقط نہیں ہوگا۔ یہی اختلاف اس وقت ہے جب عورت کی رضامندی سے اس کے ساتھ خلوت پائی۔ اسی اختلاف پر استحقاق نفقہ مبنی ہے۔ چنانچہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک مدت منع میں عورت مستحق نفقہ ہوگی کیونکہ یہ منع بق ہے اور منع سبق کی وجہ سے یہ عورت ناشزہ اور نا فرمان نہیں کہلائے گی ۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک مستحق نفقہ نہیں ہوگی۔ اسلئے کہ ان کے نزدیک یہ عورت ناشزہ ہے اور ناشزہ کیلئے نفقہ وغیرہ واجب نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ بہر حال دخول یا خلوت کے بعد صاحبین کے نزدیک عورت کیلئے حق منع نہیں ہے۔ اور امام صاحب کے نزدیک عورت کیلئے حق منع حاصل ہے۔ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جب شوہر نے عورت کے ساتھ ایک مرتبہ ولی کی یا خلوت صحیحہ کی تو عورت کی جانب سے شوہر کی طرف پورا معقود علیہ سپرد کر دیا یہی وجہ ہے کہ ایک ولی یا خلوت سے پورا مہر واجب ہو جاتا ہے۔ چنانچہ دوسری ولی کے مقابلہ میں بھی اگر مہر ہوتا تو ایک ولی سے کل مہر واجب نہ ہوتا۔ پس جب عورت نے معقود علیہ . سپرد کر دیا تو اب اس کیلئے اپنے آپ کو روکنے کا حق نہیں ہوگا۔ اور یہ بالکل ایسا ہے جیسا کہ بائع نے شمن پر قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے مشتری کی جانب مبیع کو سپرد کر دیا تو بائع کو شمن کی وجہ سے جس مبیع کا حق حاصل نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل بطور مناقضہ کے یہ ہوگی کہ ہمیں یہ بات تسلیم نہیں کہ ایک وطی سے پورا معقود علیہ یعنی بضع شوہر کے حوالہ کر دیا گیا۔ کیونکہ عورت نے شوہر سے ایسی چیز کو روکا ہے جس کے مقابلے میں بدل ہے۔ اسلئے کہ ہر ولی بضع محترم میں تصرف ہے۔ لہذا ہر وطی کے مقابلہ میں بدل یعنی مہر ہوگا۔ اور جب ہر ولی بضع محترم
The author of the book (al-Hidayah) mentioned a third scenario: if consummation has taken place and the mahr is prompt, according to Imam Abu Hanifa the same ruling applies, i.e., the woman has the right to refuse. The two (Sahibayn) say that after consummation the woman does not have the right to refuse. It should be noted that this difference of opinion is when consummation occurred with the woman's consent. If she was forced, or she is a minor or insane, then by consensus her right of habs is not forfeited. The same difference applies to valid seclusion (khalwat sahihah) with her consent. Upon this difference also depends the entitlement to nafaqah: according to Imam, during the period of refusal she is entitled to nafaqah because she is not nashiz; according to Sahibayn she is not entitled to nafaqah because she is nashiz. In any case, after consummation or valid seclusion, according to Sahibayn the right to refuse is gone; according to Imam it remains. Their proof: when the husband has consummated once or had valid seclusion, the entire object of contract (al-bad') is surrendered from the wife's side to the husband, just as the entire mahr becomes due by one act of seclusion. So after surrender, the wife cannot withhold. This is like a seller who delivers the goods before payment: he loses the right to withhold. Imam Abu Hanifa's rebuttal: we do not accept that one act of consummation surrenders the entire object of contract, because the wife withholds something that is subject to exchange. Each act of consummation in a protected vagina is a disposition requiring compensation, so each act deserves a portion of mahr.
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage presents the intra-Hanafi dispute after consummation has taken place with the wife's consent. Imam Abu Hanifa maintains that the wife still has the right to withhold the remaining acts of seclusion until the full prompt mahr is paid, because each act of sexual intercourse is a separate disposition that deserves compensation. The wife has only surrendered the benefit of that one act, not all future acts. Therefore, she can still withhold herself. Sahibayn argue that once the husband has consummated once or had valid seclusion, the entire subject of the contract (the woman's person for marital relations) is deemed surrendered to the husband, similar to how the entire mahr becomes due by that one act. Therefore, the wife loses her right to withhold. The practical consequence is on nafaqah: according to Imam, since she is not nashiz, she is entitled to nafaqah; according to Sahibayn, she is nashiz and not entitled to nafaqah. The relied-upon position in the school is the view of Sahibayn after consummation.

Key Terms
دخول (dukhul): Sexual intercourse between the spouses.
خلوت صحیحہ (khalwat sahihah): Valid seclusion between a married couple without any legal barrier to intercourse, even if intercourse does not occur.
ناشزہ (nashizah): A disobedient wife who refuses marital relations without a valid legal right.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Sahibayn, what happens to the wife's right to withhold after she voluntarily allows consummation once?
A) She retains the right for future acts until mahr is paid
B) She loses the right entirely
C) She retains the right only if mahr is less than the dower
D) The right is transferred to the husband

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that the wife loses her right to withhold after a single voluntary consummation or valid seclusion, even if the prompt mahr is unpaid.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
8 min
Wife's Right to Prevent Intercourse When Mahr is Deferred: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on haqq al-man' after consummation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on the wife's right to haqq al-man' after consummation with deferred mahr, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf regarding maintenance.

Core Idea
After consummation, Imam Abu Hanifa grants the wife the right to withhold intercourse if mahr is deferred; the Sahibayn deny it.

The marriage contract establishes mutual rights: the husband gains access to his wife's companionship, and the wife is entitled to her dower (mahr). What happens when the mahr is deferred and the husband has already consummated the marriage? Can the wife refuse further intimacy until her mahr is paid? This lesson unpacks a key intra-Hanafi dispute on this question, tracing the reasoning of the founding Imams and its practical consequence on maintenance.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) regarding the wife's right to prevent intercourse after consummation when the mahr is fully deferred.
The dispute only applies when consummation was with her consent; otherwise, the right remains by consensus.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
The opposing position is held by the Sahibayn. State their view: after consummation, the wife loses the right to prevent intercourse.
The Sahibayn include both Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Sahibayn use qiyas: analogizing marriage to a sale. Explain how the analogy works—once the subject matter (badd) is surrendered, the right to withhold is lost.
The asl is a seller who delivers goods before receiving payment.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Imam Abu Hanifa responds by rejecting the analogy. Explain his reasoning: each act of intercourse is a separate valuable act, so the wife has not surrendered the entire badd in one act.
He also uses a counter-analogy to a creditor withholding a pledge.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: maintenance (nafaqah). According to Abu Hanifa, the wife is entitled to maintenance during the period of prevention because she is not rebellious (nashizah). According to the Sahibayn, she is not entitled.
This affects financial obligations between spouses.

كتاب النكاح
کرنے سے منع کرے اور اپنے گھر سے نکلنے سے۔ اور عورت کے گھر والوں کی زیارت کرنے سے منع کرے یہاں تک کہ شوہر اس کو پورا مہر معجل ادا کر دے۔ دلیل یہ کہ شوہر کو حق حبس اس لئے حاصل تھا کہ وہ اپنا حق یعنی منافع بضع وصول کر سکے اور شوہر اداء مہر سے پہلے اپنا حق وصول کرنے کا مجاز نہیں ہے۔ لہذا شو ہر کیلئے عورت کو سفر وغیرہ سے روکنے کا اختیار بھی نہیں ہوگا۔ دوسری صورت کہ مہر پورے کا پورا مؤجل ہو اسکی بھی دو صورتیں ہیں۔ کیونکہ شوہر نے عورت کے ساتھ دخول کیا ہے یا نہیں ۔ اگر دخول نہیں کیا ہے تو عورت کو حق منع حاصل ہے یا نہیں۔ اس بارے میں اختلاف ہے۔ طرفین کے نزدیک عورت کو حق منع حاصل نہیں ہے۔ یعنی عورت کو یہ اختیار نہیں ہے کہ وہ شوہر کو وطی پر قدرت نہ دے۔ اور امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک عورت کو حق منع حاصل ہے۔ یعنی عورت کو یہ اختیار ہے کہ وہ شوہر کو وطی کرنے سے منع کر دے اور اس کو قدرت علی الوطی نہ دے۔ امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اطلاق کے وقت موجب نکاح تسلیم مہر ہے۔ مہر عین ہو یا دین۔ پس جس وقت شوہر نے موجب نکاح کو جاننے کے باوجود اجل کو قبول کیا۔ یعنی یہ مان لیا کہ مہر بعد میں ادا کر دیا جائے گا۔ تو گویا شوہر اس بات پر راضی ہو گیا کہ اس کا حق ادائیگی مہر تک کیلئے مؤخر کر دیا جائے ۔ اور جب شوہر اپنے حق کو مؤخر کرنے پر راضی ہو گیا تو عورت کو بھی اس وقت تک حق منع حاصل رہے گا جب تک کہ شوہر مہر ادا نہ کر دے۔ طرفین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ عورت نے مہر مؤجل کر دینے کی وجہ سے اپنا حق طلب ساقط کر دیا ہے اور جب عورت خود ہی اپنا حق طلب ساقط کر چکی تو اب اسکو شوہر کا حق مستحق یعنی بضع روکنے کا حق نہیں ہو گا جیسا کہ بیع میں یعنی بائع اگر ثمن مؤجل کر دے تو بائع کو مبیع روکنے کا حق نہیں ہے۔ اسی طرح اگر مہر مؤجل ہے تو عورت کو حق منع حاصل نہیں ہوگا۔
صاحب کتاب نے تیسری صورت بیان کی ہے کہ اگر عورت کے ساتھ دخول ہو گیا اور مہر مؤجل ہے تو امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک یہی حکم ہے۔ یعنی عورت کو حق منع حاصل ہے۔ اور صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ دخول کے بعد عورت کو حق منع کی وجہ سے یہ عورت ناشزہ اور نا فرمان نہیں کہلائے گی ۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک مستحق نفقہ نہیں ہوگی۔ اسلئے کہ ان کے نزدیک یہ عورت ناشزہ ہے اور ناشزہ کیلئے نفقہ وغیرہ واجب نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ بہر حال دخول یا خلوت کے بعد صاحبین کے نزدیک عورت کیلئے حق منع نہیں ہے۔ اور امام صاحب کے نزدیک عورت کیلئے حق منع حاصل ہے۔ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جب شوہر نے عورت کے ساتھ ایک مرتبہ وطی کی یا خلوت صحیحہ کی تو عورت کی جانب سے شوہر کی طرف پورا معقود علیہ سپرد کر دیا یہی وجہ ہے کہ ایک وطی یا خلوت سے پورا مہر واجب ہو جاتا ہے۔ چنانچہ دوسری وطی کے مقابلہ میں بھی اگر مہر ہوتا تو ایک وطی سے کل مہر واجب نہ ہوتا۔ پس جب عورت نے معقود علیہ سپرد کر دیا تو اب اس کیلئے اپنے آپ کو روکنے کا حق نہیں ہوگا۔ اور یہ بالکل ایسا ہے جیسا کہ بائع نے ثمن پر قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے مشتری کی جانب مبیع کو سپرد کر دیا تو بائع کو ثمن کی وجہ سے مبیع کا حق حاصل نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل بطور مناقضہ کے یہ ہوگی کہ ہمیں یہ بات تسلیم نہیں کہ ایک وطی سے پورا معقود علیہ یعنی بضع شوہر کے حوالہ کر دیا گیا۔ کیونکہ عورت نے شوہر سے ایسی چیز کو روکا ہے جس کے مقابلے میں بدل ہے۔ اسلئے کہ ہر وطی بضع محترم میں تصرف ہے۔ لہذا ہر وطی کے مقابلہ میں بدل یعنی مہر ہوگا۔ اور جب ہر وطی بضع محترم میں تصرف ہے تو ایک وطی سے کل بضع یعنی پورے معقود علیہ کا سپرد کرنا تحقیق نہیں ہو گا۔ اور اسی دلیل کو معارضہ کے طور پر کہیں تو تقریر یہ ہوگی کہ عورت نے شوہر سے اسی چیز کو روکا ہے۔ جس کے مقابلہ میں بدل ہے۔ اسلئے کہ ہر وطی بضع محترم میں تصرف کرنا ہے اور تصرف فی البضع خالی عن العوض نہیں ہوتا ہے اور اس چیز سے روکنا جس کے مقابلے میں بدل ہے صحیح ہے لہذا عورت کو ایک وطی کے بعد بھی حق منع حاصل رہے گا۔
والتاكد بالوحدة ... الخ سے صاحبین کی دلیل کا جواب ہے۔ جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ ایک وطی سے کل مہر اسلئے ثابت ہو گیا تھا کہ اس وطی کے علاوہ دوسری وطیات مجہول ہیں۔ اور مجہول معلوم کا مزاحم نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ اسلئے پورا مہر ایک وطی سے مؤکد ہو جاتا ہے۔ چنانچہ اگر ایک وطی کے بعد دوسری اور تیسری وطی بھی پائی گئی تو یہ دوسری اور تیسری وطی بھی معلوم ہوگی اور ایک معلوم وطی دوسری معلوم وطی کا مزاحم بن سکتی ہے۔ تو اس صورت میں مہر صرف ایک وطی کا مقابل نہیں ہو گا۔ بلکہ جس قدر وطیات پائی گئیں سب کا مقابل ہوگا۔ اسکی مثال ایسی ہے کہ ایک غلام نے جنایت کی تو مولیٰ پر واجب ہے کہ وہ بدل جنایت ادا کرے یا غلام سپرد کر دے۔ پس اگر پورا غلام ایک ہی بدل جنایت میں دے دیا گیا۔ پھر غلام نے دوسری اور تیسری جنایت کی تو تمام جنایتوں کا بدل یہی ایک غلام ہو گا اس سے زائد مولی پر کچھ واجب نہیں ہوگا۔ اور اگر کچھ مہر معجل ہے اور کچھ مؤجل تو مہر معجل ادا کرنے سے پہلے عورت کو حق منع حاصل ہوگا اور اگر مہر معجل عورت کو سپرد کر دیا تو عورت کو حق منع حاصل نہیں ہوگا۔
لیکن اگر آپ اشکال کریں کہ اگر مہر اور تا جیل دونوں سے سکوت کیا گیا ہے تو اس کا کیا حکم ہے۔ جواب ابو یوسف کی دلیل کے تحت میں ہم نے ذکر کیا ہے کہ اطلاق کے وقت موجب نکاح تسلیم مہر حالا ہے۔ لہذا سکوت کے وقت پورا مہر معجل ہی شمار ہوگا۔
This passage is already in Urdu and does not require translation. It discusses the rules of the wife's right to prevent intercourse (haqq al-man') in various scenarios of dower (mahr).
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the wife's right to prevent intercourse when mahr is deferred. It begins with the ruling when mahr is fully prompt: the wife can prevent intercourse and can also prevent the husband from taking her out or traveling until the prompt mahr is paid. Then it discusses when mahr is fully deferred before consummation: there is disagreement between Imam Abu Yusuf (who says she retains the right to prevent) and the other two (Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad, who say she does not). The evidence for each side is given, using analogies to a sale. Then the third scenario is after consummation with deferred mahr: Imam Abu Hanifa says she still has the right to prevent, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say she does not. This only applies when consummation was with her consent; if forced, or if she is a minor or insane, the right remains by consensus. The dispute also affects entitlement to maintenance (nafaqah): according to Imam Abu Hanifa, she is entitled because she is not rebellious (nashizah); according to the Sahibayn, she is not entitled. Then the reasoning of each side is elaborated with analogies, and a rebuttal regarding the concept of 'tawakid bil-wahdah' (confirmation by unity) is provided. Finally, it addresses the case where mahr is partly prompt and partly deferred: she has the right to prevent until the prompt portion is paid. If nothing is specified, the entire mahr is considered prompt by default.

Key Terms
حق حبس (haqq al-habs): The right to detain or withhold something, here the right of the wife to withhold herself from the husband's sexual access until payment of prompt dower.
حق منع (haqq al-man'): The right to prevent; synonym for haqq al-habs in this context.
بضع (badd'): The female genitalia; legally used to refer to the sexual function as the object of the marriage contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what is the ruling on the wife's right to prevent intercourse after consummation when the mahr is fully deferred?
A) She does not have the right because consummation transfers full ownership.
B) She retains the right because each act of intercourse is a separate exchange.
C) She loses the right only if the mahr is prompt.
D) She has the right only before consummation.

Key Takeaway
The intra-Hanafi dispute over the wife's right to prevent intercourse after consummation with deferred mahr hinges on whether the vulva is surrendered in one act; Abu Hanifa says no, the Sahibayn say yes, with direct impact on maintenance entitlement.

Husband's Right to Move Wife After Full Mahr
Intra-Hanafi dispute on moving wife after mahr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on moving one's wife after full mahr payment and explain the intra-madhhab dispute between Faqih Abu al-Layth and al-Marghinani.

Core Idea
After full dower payment, the husband may move his wife, but harm to the wife restricts this right.

This passage addresses a key marital right: relocation. After the husband pays the full mahr, he gains authority to move his wife. However, later Hanafi scholars debated whether this extends to another city, balancing the general Quranic command with the prohibition of harm. The passage presents both sides and a compromise solution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling
State the ruling: after payment of the full mahr, the husband has the right to move his wife to any location of his choosing.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the Quranic proof: Surah al-Talaq 65:6, 'House them where you live according to your means, and do not harm them.' This general command supports the husband's authority.
3
Note the ikhtilaf
Faqih Abu al-Layth restricts moving to another city because it causes harm (dharar), citing the same verse's prohibition. Al-Marghinani upholds the general permission.
4
Analyze the responses
Both scholars use the same verse: al-Marghinani emphasizes 'house them where you live' as general, while Abu al-Layth emphasizes 'do not harm them.' The passage provides a response on behalf of Abu al-Layth that leaving one's homeland is inherently harmful.
5
Identify the compromise
Moving to a nearby village within less than travel distance is permissible because it does not constitute exile (pardes).
Travel distance is considered to be the distance at which one becomes a traveler (musafir).

This passage is in Urdu. It states that when the husband gives her the full dower, he has the option to move her wherever he wishes, citing the Quranic verse: 'House them where you live according to your means, and do not harm them.' Faqih Abu al-Layth says he should not move her to another city because it is a foreign land and will cause her distress. Zahir al-Din al-Marghinani says adopting the general meaning of the Quran is preferable, so the husband may move her. However, a response can be given that Faqih Abu al-Layth also follows the Quran as the verse continues 'and do not harm them', and leaving her homeland causes harm. It is allowed to move her to nearby villages that are less than a travel distance away, as that does not constitute exile.
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling and a subsequent dispute among later Hanafi scholars. The base ruling is that after the husband pays the full dower, he has the right to move his wife to any location he chooses. The evidence is the Quranic verse (Surah al-Talaq 65:6) which instructs husbands to house wives where they live. Some scholars, like Faqih Abu al-Layth, restrict this to the same city because moving to another city would cause harm (dharar) and violate the verse's prohibition on harming wives. Others, like al-Marghinani, uphold the general permissibility. A middle position allows moving to nearby villages within less than travel distance, as that does not constitute exile. The passage highlights the methodology of balancing general Quranic commands with the principle of avoiding harm.

Key Terms
پردیس (pardes): A foreign land away from one's hometown; considered a place of hardship for the wife.
مضرت (mazarrat): Harm, detriment, or injury. In this context, the distress caused to the wife by moving to a foreign land.

Key Takeaway
The husband's right to move his wife after full mahr is balanced by the principle of avoiding harm, leading to a legitimate intra-Hanafi dispute with a compromise for nearby relocations.

Mahr Dispute: Evidentiary Preference
Ruling on evidentiary preference in mahr disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule of evidentiary preference in mahr disputes by distinguishing the wife's accepted claim up to mahr al-mithl and the husband's claim for any excess.

Core Idea
In a mahr dispute, the wife's word prevails up to the customary dower; the husband's word prevails for any excess.

This passage from al-Hidayah provides a clear procedural rule for when spouses disagree on the mahr amount after marriage. The rule balances fairness and practicality by using the customary dower (mahr al-mithl) as a benchmark: the wife's claim is trusted up to that amount, and the husband's claim is trusted for any amount above it. This prevents either party from exploiting the lack of evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute scenario
Recognize that the rule applies when a husband and wife disagree on the specific mahr amount agreed upon at the time of marriage, and no clear evidence exists.
The dispute must be after the marriage contract is valid.
2
Apply the wife's claim up to mahr al-mithl
Accept the wife's statement regarding the mahr amount, but only up to the mahr al-mithl (customary dower for women of her status). Any amount she claims beyond that requires proof.
Mahr al-mithl is determined by factors like age, beauty, wealth, lineage, and locality.
3
Apply the husband's claim for excess
If the husband claims a higher amount than what the wife claims, his statement is accepted for the excess amount. For example, if wife claims 500 and husband claims 700, the husband's word is accepted for the extra 200.
This prevents the wife from claiming an exorbitant amount without proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ایک عورت سے نکاح کیا، پھر مہر میں اختلاف ہو گیا تو کس کا قول معتبر ہے؟
قال ومن تزوج امرأة ثم اختلفا فى المهر فالقول قول المرأة الى تمام مهر مثلها والقول قول الزوج فيما زاد
A man married a woman, then they disagreed on the dower. Whose statement is accepted? He said: Whoever marries a woman and then they disagree on the dower, the woman's statement is accepted up to the full dower of her peers (mahr al-mithl), and the husband's statement is accepted as to any excess beyond that.
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This is a concise matn (ruling) from the original text of al-Hidayah. It addresses a common dispute: after marriage, the husband and wife disagree on the amount of dower agreed upon. The rule provides a practical solution: if no evidence is available, the wife's claim is accepted as true, but only up to the amount that is customary for women of her status (mahr al-mithl). Any amount she claims beyond that is not accepted unless she can prove it. Conversely, if the husband claims the dower is less than the mithl, his word is not accepted; but if he claims it is more than what the wife claims, his word is accepted for the excess. In essence, the mahr al-mithl serves as a default upper limit for the wife's claim and a lower limit for the husband's claim.

Key Terms
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The standard dower for a woman of similar status (age, beauty, wealth, lineage, etc.) in her family and community.
قول المرأة (qawl al-mar'ah): The wife's statement is given evidentiary preference (considered truthful) up to mahr al-mithl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The husband's word is always accepted.
B) The wife's word is accepted entirely.
C) The wife's word is accepted up to mahr al-mithl; the husband's word for any excess.
D) The matter is settled by arbitration.

Key Takeaway
In mahr disputes, the wife's claim is trusted up to the customary dower, and the husband's claim is trusted for any excess above that.

Ruling on Mahr Dispute Between Spouses: Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Explains the Hanafi ruling when spouses dispute over mahr amount with imam differences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mahr disputes between spouses and compare the positions of Abu Hanifa/Muhammad with Abu Yusuf, explaining the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
When spouses dispute mahr, the apparent circumstance (zahir) of mahr al-mithl tilts the scales, not simply who is claiming or denying.

Marriage contracts often involve a specified mahr, but what if the spouses later disagree on the amount? This passage delves into an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on whose word is accepted. Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad anchor the ruling in the customary mahr (mahr al-mithl), while Abu Yusuf prioritizes the general rule of accepting the denier's oath. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to apply usul al-fiqh principles—especially the role of al-zahir—to practical family law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
Recognize that the spouses differ on the mahr amount. The core question: whose statement (qawl) is given evidentiary weight?
2
State the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad
During marriage: wife's word accepted up to mahr al-mithl; husband's word for any excess. After divorce before consummation: husband's word accepted for half the mahr.
This is the zahir al-riwayah position from al-Asl and al-Jami' al-Saghir.
3
State the position of Abu Yusuf
Husband's word is always accepted (before and after divorce) unless he claims an unreasonably low amount that contradicts custom.
Abu Yusuf relies on the default rule that the denier's word with oath is accepted.
4
Analyze the proofs
Abu Hanifa/Muhammad invoke al-zahir (apparent circumstance) supporting mahr al-mithl as the original obligation, drawing an analogy to the dyer and garment owner. Abu Yusuf counters with the general principle of accepting the denial and the necessity of valuing conjugal benefits.
The difference stems from conflicting usul principles: al-zahir vs. al-asl fi al-da'awa.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
Under the majority view, the wife is assured at least mahr al-mithl; under Abu Yusuf, the husband's denial can reduce the amount unless it is implausibly low. Practical outcomes depend on the relationship between the claimed amounts and the custom.
The mufta bihi position adopts the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ایک عورت سے نکاح کیا، پھر مہر میں اختلاف ہو گیا تو کس کا قول معتبر ہے؟
قال ومن تزوج امرأة ثم اختلفا فى المهر فالقول قول المرأة الى تمام مهر مثلها والقول قول الزوج فيما زاد على مهر المثل وان طلقها قبل الدخول بها فالقول قوله فى نصف المهر وهذا عند ابي حنيفة ومحمد وقال ابويوسف القول قوله بعد الطلاق وقبله الا ان ياتي بشيء قليل ومعناه ما لا يتعارف مهر الهاهو الصحيح لابي يوسف ان المرأة تدعى الزيادة والزوج ينكر و القول قول المنكر مع يمينه الا ان ياتي بشيء يكدبه الظاهر فيه وهذا لان تقوم منافع البضع ضروری فمتى امکن ایجاب شيء من المسمى لا يصار اليه ولهما ان القول في الدعاوى قول من يشهدله الظاهر والظاهر شاهد لمن يشهد له مهر المثل لانه هو الموجب الاصلي في باب النكاح وصار كالصباغ مع رب الثوب اذا اختلفافى مقدار الاجريحكم فيه قيمة الصبغ ثم ذكر ههنا ان بعد الطلاق قبل الدخول القول قوله في نصف المهر وهذا رواية الجامع الصغير والاصل وذكر في الجامع الكبيـرانـه يـحـكـم متعة مثلها وهو قياس قولهما لان المتعة موجبة بعد الطلاق كمهر المثل قبله فتحكم كهوووجه التوفيق أنه وضع المسألة في الأصل فى الالف والالفين والمتعة لا تبلغ هذا المبلغ في العادة فلايفيد تحكيمها ووضعها فى الجامع الكبير فى المائة والعشرة ومتعة مثلها عشرون فيفيد تحكيمها والمذكور في الجامع الصغير ساكت عن ذكر المقدار فيحمل على ماهو المذكور فى الأصل وشرح قولهما فيما اذا اختلفافي حال قيام النكاح ان الزوج اذا ادعى الالف والمرأة الالفين فان كان مهر مثلها الفا او اقل فالقول قوله وانكان الفين او اكثر فالقول قولها وايهما اقام البيئة فى الوجهين تقبل وان اقاما البيئة في الوجه الاول تقبل بينتها لانها تثبت الزيادة وفى الوجه الثانى بينته لانها تثبت الحط وان كان مهر مثلها الفاو خمس مائة تحالفا واذا حلفا تجب الف وخمس مائة هذا تخريج الرازي وقال الكرخي يتحالفان في الفصول الثلثة ثم يحكم مهر المثل بعد ذلك
ترجمہ اور جس شخص نے کسی عورت سے نکاح کیا پھر دونوں نے مہر میں اختلاف کیا تو عورت کا قول ( معتبر ) ہوگا۔ اسکے تمام مہر مثل تک اور شوہر کا قول معتبر ہو گا اس مقدار میں جو مہرشل پر زائد ہے۔ اور اگر اس کو طلاق قبل الدخول دی تو شوہر کا قول ( معتبر ہو گا نصف مہر میں ۔ اور یہ ابو حنیفہ اور امام محمد کے نزدیک ہے۔ اور ابو یوسف نے فرمایا کہ شوہر کا قول (معتبر ) ہوگا۔ طلاق کے بعد بھی اور طلاق سے پہلے بھی ۔مگر یہ کہ شوہر تھوڑی سی چیز لا دے اورشی قلیل کی مراد وہ ہے کہ عورت کیلئے وہ مہر متعارف نہ ہو یہی صحیح ہے۔ ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے عورت دعوی کرتی ہے زیادتی کا۔ اور شو ہر منکر ہے اور منکر کا قول مع الیمین (معتبر ) ہوتا ہے۔ مگر یہ کہ شوہر ایسی چیز بیان کرے۔ جس کی ظاہر حال تکذیب کرتا ہے۔ اور یہ اسلئے کہ منافع بضع کا متقوم ہونا ضرورۃ ہے۔ پس جب تک مسمی میں سے کسی چیز کا واجب کرنا ممکن ہو تو مہر مثل کی طرف رجوع نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ اور طرفین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ دعووں میں اس کا قول ( معتبر ) ہوتا ہے جس کے واسطے ظاہر حال شاہد ہو اور ظاہر حال اس کے واسطے شاہد ہے، جس کے واسطے مہر مثل شاہد ہو۔ کیونکہ باب نکاح میں مہر مشکل ہی موجب اصلی ہے۔ اور یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسا کہ رنگریز کا ( مخاصمہ) کپڑے کے مالک کے ساتھ جبکہ اجرت کی مقدار میں اختلاف کیا ہو تو اس میں رنگ کی قیمت کو حکم بنایا جائے گا۔ پھر صاحب قدوری نے یہاں ذکر کیا کہ طلاق قبل الدخول کے بعد نصف مہر میں شوہر کا قول ( معتبر ) ہوگا۔ اور یہ روایت ہے جامع صغیر اور مبسوط کی۔ اور جامع کبیر میں ذکر کیا کہ عورت کے معہ مثل کو حکم بنایا جائے گا۔ اور یہی قیاس ہے طرفین کے قول کا۔ اسلئے کہ متعہ موجب ہے طلاق کے بعد ۔ جیسا کہ مہر مثل موجب ہے طلاق سے پہلے ۔ پس متعہ کو حکم بنایا جائے گا۔ جیسا کہ مہر مثل کو ۔ اور توفیق کی
A man married a woman, then they differed over the mahr. The woman's statement is accepted up to the full mahr al-mithl, and the husband's statement is accepted for what exceeds mahr al-mithl. If he divorced her before consummation, his statement is accepted regarding half the mahr. This is according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said: The husband's statement is accepted both after divorce and before it, unless he brings something insignificant, meaning something not recognized as mahr for such a woman. This is the correct view of Abu Yusuf: the woman claims increase and the husband denies, and the statement of the denier with his oath is accepted, unless he brings something that the apparent circumstance belies. This is because the benefits of the vulva are valuable out of necessity, so whenever it is possible to make something from the named mahr obligatory, one does not resort to mahr al-mithl. The two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) argued: In claims, the statement of the one whom the apparent circumstance supports is accepted, and the apparent circumstance supports mahr al-mithl because it is the original obligatory amount in nikah. It is like the dyer with the owner of the garment when they differ over the amount of wages; the value of the dye is judged. Then (the author) mentioned here that after divorce before consummation, his statement is accepted regarding half the mahr. This is the narration of al-Jami' al-Saghir and al-Asl. And in al-Jami' al-Kabir, it is mentioned that she is judged mut'ah mithlihah, which is the qiyas of their (the two's) saying, because mut'ah is obligatory after divorce as mahr al-mithl is before it, so it is judged similarly. The reconciliation is that he placed the issue in al-Asl regarding one thousand and two thousand, and mut'ah does not reach that amount customarily, so its judgment is not beneficial. And he placed it in al-Jami' al-Kabir regarding one hundred and ten, and her mut'ah mithlihah is twenty, so its judgment is beneficial. What is mentioned in al-Jami' al-Saghir is silent about the amount, so it is carried upon what is mentioned in al-Asl. And the explanation of their (the two's) statement when they differ during the existence of marriage: if the husband claims one thousand and the woman claims two thousand, then if her mahr al-mithl is one thousand or less, his statement is accepted; if it is two thousand or more, her statement is accepted. Whichever of them produces evidence in both cases is accepted. If they both produce evidence, in the first case her evidence is accepted because it proves increase, and in the second case his evidence is accepted because it proves reduction. If her mahr al-mithl is one thousand five hundred, they take oaths; when they take oaths, one thousand five hundred becomes obligatory. This is the deduction of al-Razi. Al-Karkhi said: They take oaths in all three cases, then mahr al-mithl is judged after that.
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage presents a detailed Hanafi ruling on how to resolve a dispute between spouses over the amount of mahr (dower). The core rule, according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad, is that the wife's word is accepted for the mahr amount up to the value of her mahr al-mithl (the customary mahr for a woman of her status). The husband's word is accepted for any amount above that. This is based on the principle that the apparent circumstance (al-zahir) supports the wife's claim up to what is customary. The passage then addresses the case of divorce before consummation: the husband's word is accepted regarding half the mahr, again per Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Imam Abu Yusuf differs: he holds that the husband's word is always accepted (both before and after divorce) unless he claims an amount that is unreasonably low and contrary to custom. Abu Yusuf's reasoning is that when a claimant (the wife) demands more and the defendant (the husband) denies, the default rule is to accept the denial with an oath, unless the claim is so weak that the apparent circumstances belie it. He also argues that since intercourse is valuable by necessity, if any named mahr can be established, one should not revert to mahr al-mithl. The two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) respond that the apparent circumstance supports mahr al-mithl as the original obligation in marriage, similar to the dyer analogy: if a dyer and garment owner dispute the wage, the value of the dye (which is customarily known) is judged. The passage then explains a variance in narrations: in al-Jami' al-Saghir and al-Asl, the husband's word is accepted for half after divorce, but in al-Jami' al-Kabir, the wife is judged mut'ah mithlihah (a consolatory gift equal to her mahr al-mithl). The commentator reconciles this by noting that the amounts involved are different. Finally, the passage elaborates on scenarios during marriage: if the husband claims 1000 and the wife claims 2000, the decision depends on mahr al-mithl. If it is 1000 or less, the husband's word stands; if 2000 or more, the wife's word stands. If both produce evidence, the evidence of the one who proves a change (increase or decrease) is accepted. If mahr al-mithl is 1500, they take oaths and then 1500 is due. Al-Karkhi holds that oaths are taken in all three cases and then mahr al-mithl is decreed.

Key Terms
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The customary dower for a woman of similar status (family, beauty, virginity, etc.) in her community.
قول (qawl): The statement or claim of a party; in disputes, whose statement is given evidentiary weight.
ظاهر (zahir): Apparent circumstance or external evidence that supports one party's claim over the other.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, if a husband claims the mahr is 1000 and the wife claims it is 2000, and the mahr al-mithl is 1500, what is the outcome?
A) The husband's word is accepted, so the mahr is 1000.
B) The wife's word is accepted up to mahr al-mithl, so the mahr is 1500.
C) They must take oaths and then the mahr is 1500.
D) The husband's word is accepted for half and the wife's for the other half.

Key Takeaway
In mahr disputes, the customary mahr (mahr al-mithl) serves as the default benchmark and the wife's word is accepted up to that amount, reflecting the Hanafi usul principle that al-zahir (apparent circumstance) plus the original obligation outweigh the default rule of accepting the denier's oath.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
12 min
The Ruling on Mahr Disputes: Two Companions vs. Abu Yusuf
Intra-Hanafi dispute on mahr dispute resolution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on whose statement is accepted when spouses dispute the mahr amount, and compare the positions of the two companions and Imam Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
When spouses dispute mahr, the one whose claim matches mahr al-mithl is believed — not always the husband.

In marriage, the mahr is often specified, but disputes can arise about the agreed amount. The Hanafi school has a detailed framework: the two companions (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) base the decision on the customary mahr al-mithl, while Imam Abu Yusuf gives presumptive weight to the husband's claim. Understanding this dispute sharpens your appreciation of how Hanafi imams balance principles and exceptions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Determine the context of the dispute: before/after divorce, before/after consummation, or after death. The ruling varies.
The text outlines multiple forms: dispute during marriage, after divorce (before or after consummation), or among heirs.
2
State the two companions' rule
For disputes after consummation, the wife's statement is accepted up to mahr al-mithl, and the husband's statement for any excess. For divorce before consummation, only the husband's statement on half the mahr is accepted.
This is based on the idea that the original cause in marriage is mahr al-mithl.
3
State Abu Yusuf's rule
Abu Yusuf holds that the husband's statement is accepted in all cases, unless he claims a trifling amount (shay' qalil) that contradicts apparent circumstances.
Abu Yusuf considers the husband as the denier of increase, and thus his statement with oath is accepted.
4
Compare the proofs
The two companions argue that the defendant is whose statement agrees with the apparent circumstances (mahr al-mithl). Abu Yusuf argues that the usufruct of the vulva is not property; mahr is made property by necessity, so the named mahr (original) takes precedence.
Both use the principle that the claimant must provide evidence, but they differ on what constitutes the 'apparent circumstances'.
5
Determine the thamarah
If mahr al-mithl is known, the two companions accept wife's statement up to that amount; Abu Yusuf accepts the husband's claim unless it is trifling. This can lead to different mahr outcomes in practice.
The author of al-Hidayah leans towards the two companions' view as the mufta bihi.

تشریح اس مسئلہ کی چند صورتیں ہیں۔ اسلئے کہ زوجین کا اختلاف حالت حیات میں ہے یا دونوں کی موت کے بعد ان کے ورثہ نے اختلاف کیا یا احد الزوجین کی موت کے بعد پس اگر حالت حیات میں زوجین نے اختلاف کیا تو پھر طرفین کی دلیل کا حاصل یہ ہے مدعی کے پاس اگر بینہ موجود نہ ہو ت مدعی علیہ کا قول مع الیمین معتبر ہوتا ہے اور مدعی علیہ وہ شخص کہلاتا ہے جس کا قول ظاہر حال کے موافق ہو۔ اور چونکہ نکاح میں موجب اصلی مہر مثل ہے۔ لہذا جس کا قول مہر مثل کے موافق ہو گا اس کا قول ظاہر حال کے موافق کہلائے گا۔
خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ طرفین کے نزدیک مہر مثل حکم ہے۔ چنانچہ اگر مہر مثل ایک ہزار یا اس سے کم ہے تو شوہر کا قول معتبر ہوگا۔ اور اگر مبر مثل دو ہزار یا اس سے زائد ہے تو عورت کا قول معتبر ہوگا اور اگر مہر مثل ایک ہزار اور دو ہزار کے درمیان ہے تو مہر مثل واجب ہو گا۔ اسکی مثال ایسی ہے کہ انگریز اور صاحب ثوب کے درمیان اجرت کی مقدار میں اختلاف ہوا مثلاً صاحب ثوب کہتا ہے کہ رنگنے کی اجرت ایک درہم ہے اور انگریز کہتا ہے کہ اجرت دو درہم ہیں تو اس صورت میں رنگ کی قیمت کو حکم بنایا جائے گا۔ اس کی صورت یہ ہوگی کہ پہلے بغیر رنگے کپڑے کی قیمت معلوم کرے۔ پھر رنگے ہوئے کی قیمت معلوم کرے۔ مثلاً بغیر رنگے کپڑے کی قیمت ہے دس درہم اور رنگے ہوئے کپڑے کی قیمت بارہ درہم ہیں۔ پس رنگ کی وجہ سے دو درہم کا اضافہ ہوا ہے تو یہ دو درہم رنگ کی قیمت ہوں گے ۔ لہذا اس قیمت کو حکم بنایا جائے گا۔ چنانچہ رنگریز کا قول اس قیمت کے موافق ہے تو صاحب ثوب کا قول معتبر ہوگا۔
ثم ذكر ههنا الح سے صاحب ہدایہ نے امام محمد کے اقوال میں تعارض بیان فرمایا ہے تعارض یہ ہے کہ امام محمد نے جامع صغیر اور مبسوط میں ذکر فرمایا کہ طلاق قبل الدخول کے بعد اگر مقدار مہر میں زوجین نے اختلاف کیا تو نصف مہر میں شوہر کا قول معتبر مانا جائے گا۔ اور متعہ مثل کو حکم نہیں بنایا جائے گا۔ اور جامع کبیر میں ذکر کیا ہے کہ متعہ مثل کو حکم بنایا جائے گا۔ متعہ مثل زوجین میں سے جس کے قول کے موافق ہو گا نصف مہر میں اس کا قول معتبر ہو گا۔ جامع کبیر کی روایت طرفین کے قول کے مطابق ہے۔ کیونکہ جس طرح طلاق سے پہلے مہر مثل موجب نکاح ہے اسی طرح طلاق قبل الدخول کے بعد متعہ موجب نکاح ہے۔ پس جس طرح مہر مثل حکم تھا۔ اسی طرح متعہ مثل بھی حکم ہونا چاہئے ۔ طرفین کا ذکر خاص طور سے اسلئے کیا گیا ہے کہ ابو یوسف کے نزدیک تمام صورتوں میں شوہر کا قول معتبر ہے۔ وجه التوفیق سے صاحب ہدایہ اس تعارض کو دور فرما رہے ہیں۔ فرماتے ہیں کہ مبسوط میں مسئلہ کی وضع ایک ہزار اور دو ہزار میں تھی ۔ یعنی شوہر مدعی تھا ایک ہزار کا اور عورت دعوی کر رہی ہے دو ہزار کا۔ اور متعہ بالعموم پانچ سوروپیہ کی مقدار کو نہیں پہنچتا ہے۔ اس وجہ سے متعہ کوحکم بنانے میں کوئی فائدہ نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ شوہر نصف مسمی یعنی پانچ سو کا پہلے ہی سے معترف ہے لہذا عورت کو پانچ سو درہم دے دیئے جائیں گے متعہ کو حکم بنانے کی چنداں ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ اور جامع کبیر میں مسئلہ وضع سو اور دس درہم میں ہے ۔ یعنی شوہر کا دعویٰ ہے کہ مہر دس درہم ہیں اور عورت کا دعوی ہے کہ مہر سو درہم ہیں۔ اور متعد مثل بالعموم ہیں درہم کا ہوتا ہے۔ پس اب متعہ کو حکم بنانا مفید ہوگا۔ چنانچہ اس صورت میں متعہ عورت کی جانب کیلئے مؤید ہے اور جامع صغیر میں مقدار مہر کا ذکر نہیں کیا گیا۔ بلکہ اس سلسلہ میں جامع صغیر ساکت ہے۔ لہذا جامع صغیر کی روایت کو اس پر محمول کیا جائے گا جو مبسوط میں مذکور ہے۔ کیونکہ امام محمد کی تمام کتابوں میں مبسوط ہی اصل ہے۔ اور بعض لوگ یہ بھی کہتے ہیں کہ مبسوط پہلے تصنیف کی گئی۔ اسکے بعد جامع صغیر تصنیف کی گئی ہے لہذا مبسوط میں جو مذکور ہو گا وہ متعارف کے مانند ہے۔ وشرح قولھما سے طرفین کے قول کی تشریح فرمارہے ہیں۔ تشریح یہ ہے کہ جب زوجین نے مقدار مبر قبل الطلاق میں اختلاف
The reason is that Imam Muhammad in al-Mabsut hypothesized the case with one thousand and two thousand, and mut'ah customarily does not reach that amount. So making mut'ah the governing factor would be useless. In al-Jami' al-Kabir, the case was set with one hundred and ten. And that woman's mut'ah al-mithl is not like that. So making mut'ah the governing factor would be useful. What is mentioned in al-Jami' al-Saghir is silent about the amount. Therefore, it will be carried on the amount mentioned in al-Mabsut. Explanation of the statement of the two (companions) in this case: when the dispute occurs at the time of the marriage contract, if the husband claims one thousand and the wife claims two thousand, then if the wife's mahr al-mithl is one thousand or less, the husband's statement (is accepted). If the mahr al-mithl is two thousand or more, the wife's statement (is accepted). If either establishes clear evidence, it will be accepted in both cases. If both present evidence, in the first case the wife's evidence is accepted because it proves the increase, and in the second case the husband's evidence because he proves the decrease. If the mahr al-mithl is one thousand five hundred, both take oaths, and when both have taken oaths, one thousand five hundred becomes obligatory. This is the derivation of Imam Abu Bakr al-Jassas al-Razi. Imam al-Karkhi said: Both take oaths in all three cases, then after that mahr al-mithl is made the governing factor. Explanation: This issue has several forms: the dispute between the spouses occurs during their lifetimes, or after both deaths their heirs dispute, or after the death of one spouse. If during their lifetimes they dispute, then there are two forms: this dispute occurs after divorce or before divorce. Then each of those has two forms: the dispute is about the original or about the named amount. The author first described the case where the spouses dispute about the amount of the dower at the time of the marriage contract, or after separation after consummation, or after the death of one spouse. For example, the husband claims the mahr is one thousand and the wife says two thousand. Regarding this, the school of the two (companions) is that the wife's statement is accepted up to the amount of mahr al-mithl, and the husband's statement is accepted for the excess over mahr al-mithl. If divorce occurred before consummation, regarding half the mahr only the husband's statement is accepted, not the wife's. Imam Abu Yusuf's school is that whether the dispute occurs after divorce or before divorce, in both cases the husband's statement is accepted, unless the husband mentions a trifling thing, then his statement is not accepted. There is disagreement among jurists about the meaning of a trifling thing. Some jurists hold that a trifling thing means less than ten dirhams. Summary: if the husband claims less than ten dirhams, his statement is not accepted; from ten dirhams and above, Abu Yusuf holds the husband's statement is accepted. The author of al-Hidayah says that the correct position is that in Abu Yusuf's view, a trifling thing means an unfamiliar mahr, meaning the husband mentions such a small amount that a woman of her like would not normally marry for that amount. Abu Yusuf's proof is that the wife is the claimant of the increase and the husband is the denier of the increase, and the rule is that in the absence of evidence from the claimant, the statement of the denier with an oath is accepted. Therefore, the husband, who denies the increase, his statement with an oath is accepted. But if the husband mentions such a trifling amount that apparent circumstances belie it, then his statement in that trifling amount is not accepted. The gist of Abu Yusuf's mentioned proof is that the usufruct of the vulva is not considered property, because the vulva is not wealth. However, to manifest the greatness of the vulva or for the purpose of procreation, the usufruct of the vulva is made considered property by necessity. So as long as it is possible to make the named mahr (which is the original) obligatory, one does not resort to mahr al-mithl (which is established by necessity). Therefore, Abu Yusuf says that regarding the named mahr, the husband's statement is accepted; mahr al-mithl will not be made the governing factor. The gist of the proof of the two (companions) is that if the claimant has no evidence, the statement of the defendant with an oath is accepted, and the defendant is the person whose statement agrees with the apparent circumstances. Since in marriage the original cause is mahr al-mithl, therefore the one whose statement agrees with mahr al-mithl, his statement will be called agreeing with the apparent circumstances. Summary: According to the two (companions), mahr al-mithl is the governing factor. So if mahr al-mithl is one thousand or less, the husband's statement is accepted. If mahr al-mithl is two thousand or more, the wife's statement is accepted. If mahr al-mithl is between one thousand and two thousand, mahr al-mithl becomes obligatory. An example: a dyer and a cloth-owner dispute the amount of wages. The cloth-owner says the dyeing wage is one dirham, the dyer says two dirhams. In this case, the value of the dyeing is made the governing factor. The method: first determine the value of the un-dyed cloth, then the value of the dyed cloth. For instance, the un-dyed cloth value is ten dirhams, the dyed cloth value is twelve dirhams. Thus the increase due to dyeing is two dirhams, which is the value of the dyeing. So that value is made the governing factor. Accordingly, if the dyer's statement agrees with this value, the cloth-owner's statement is accepted. Then, here, the author of al-Hidayah stated a contradiction in Imam Muhammad's statements. The contradiction is that Imam Muhammad in al-Jami' al-Saghir and al-Mabsut stated that after divorce before consummation, if the spouses dispute the amount of mahr, the husband's statement is accepted regarding half the mahr, and mut'ah al-mithl is not made the governing factor. But in al-Jami' al-Kabir, he stated that mut'ah al-mithl is made the governing factor, and whichever of the spouses has a statement agreeing with mut'ah al-mithl, his statement regarding half the mahr is accepted. The narration of al-Jami' al-Kabir agrees with the statement of the two (companions). Because just as before divorce mahr al-mithl is the cause of marriage, similarly after divorce before consummation mut'ah is the cause of marriage. So as mahr al-mithl was the governing factor, similarly mut'ah al-mithl should be the governing factor. The two (companions) are mentioned specifically because according to Abu Yusuf the husband's statement is accepted in all cases. The author of al-Hidayah removes this contradiction through reconciliation. He says: In al-Mabsut the case was set with one thousand and two thousand, meaning the husband claimed one thousand and the wife claimed two thousand, and mut'ah generally does not reach the amount of five hundred. Therefore, making mut'ah the governing factor is not beneficial because the husband already admits half the named mahr, i.e., five hundred, so the wife will be given five hundred dirhams; there is no need to make mut'ah the governing factor. In al-Jami' al-Kabir the case was set with one hundred and ten dirhams, meaning the husband claims the mahr is ten dirhams and the wife claims one hundred dirhams, and mut'ah al-mithl is generally ten dirhams. So here making mut'ah the governing factor is beneficial. In that case, mut'ah supports the wife's side. In al-Jami' al-Saghir the amount of mahr is not mentioned; rather, it is silent on this matter. Therefore, the narration of al-Jami' al-Saghir is carried on what is mentioned in al-Mabsut, because among all Imam Muhammad's books, al-Mabsut is the original. Some also say that al-Mabsut was composed first; then al-Jami' al-Saghir was composed later, so what is mentioned in al-Mabsut is like the customary. And the explanation of the statement of the two (companions): He (the author) is explaining the statement of the two (companions). The explanation is that when the spouses dispute the amount of mahr before divorce...
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute resolution and ruling statement from the Urdu sharh of al-Hidayah. It addresses the scenario where spouses disagree on the amount of mahr (dower), either during marriage or after divorce (before or after consummation). The text first explains the apparent contradiction in Imam Muhammad's statements across his works (al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir) regarding whether mut'ah al-mithl (the dower of the like for divorce before consummation) should be used as a governing factor. The reconciliation is based on different hypothetical amounts: in al-Mabsut, the amounts are large (1000 and 2000) where mut'ah al-mithl is less than half of the smaller claim, so it is not needed; in al-Jami' al-Kabir, the amounts are small (10 and 100) where mut'ah al-mithl is comparable, so it becomes relevant. The author then presents the ruling of the two companions (Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad, though contextually 'al-tarafayn' here likely refers to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad as opposed to Abu Yusuf) that the statement of the spouse whose claimed amount matches the mahr al-mithl (or mut'ah al-mithl) is accepted. Specifically, the wife's statement is accepted up to mahr al-mithl, and the husband's statement is accepted for any excess. For divorce before consummation, only the husband's statement is accepted regarding half the mahr. Imam Abu Yusuf's separate opinion is also detailed: he holds the husband's statement is always accepted unless he claims a trifling amount (shay' qalil), which is defined as an amount so low that a woman of her status would not normally marry for it. Abu Yusuf's reasoning is that the usufruct of the vulva is not inherently valuable, but by necessity it becomes considered property; therefore, the named mahr (original) takes precedence over mahr al-mithl. The passage concludes with a qiyas (analogy) to a dispute between a dyer and a cloth-owner to illustrate how mahr al-mithl is determined. This is a thorough explanation of the Hanafi positions on mahr disputes.

Key Terms
مهر مثل (mahr al-mithl): The dower of the like: the mahr that is customary for a woman of similar status.
متعہ مثل (mut'ah al-mithl): The gift of consolation for a divorced woman before consummation, measured by the mahr al-mithl.
شی قلیل (shay' qalil): A trifling amount of mahr that is so low that a woman of her status would not normally marry for it.
مهر سمی (mahr musamma): The mahr explicitly named in the marriage contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the two companions (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), if after consummation the husband claims mahr = 500 and wife claims mahr = 1500, and mahr al-mithl = 1000, what is the outcome?
A) Husband's statement is accepted; mahr = 500.
B) Wife's statement is accepted; mahr = 1500.
C) Both statements are accepted partially; wife gets 1000, husband's claim of 500 is disregarded.
D) Wife's statement is accepted up to 1000, and husband's statement is accepted for the excess; thus mahr = 1000.

Key Takeaway
In mahr disputes after consummation, the spouse whose claim matches the customary mahr (mahr al-mithl) is believed, not automatically the husband.

Nikah — Marriage
advanced
8 min
Reconciling Imam Muhammad's Narrations on Mut'ah al-Mithl
Reconciliation of internal contradiction in Imam Muhammad's works

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the apparent contradiction in Imam Muhammad's statements on mut'ah al-mithl and the reconciliation presented in al-Hidayah.

Core Idea
Imam Muhammad's rulings vary by context — al-Marghinani resolves them using the specific amounts assumed in each narration.

Imam Muhammad's works sometimes show different rulings on whether mut'ah al-mithl should govern after divorce before consummation. Al-Marghinani demonstrates that the apparent contradiction is resolved by noting the different hypothetical mahr amounts assumed in each text. This illustrates a key method in Hanafi jurisprudence: reconciling conflicting riwayat by contextual analysis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contradiction
In al-Mabsut and al-Jami' al-Saghir, after divorce before consummation, the husband's statement is accepted regarding half the mahr without referring to mut'ah al-mithl. In al-Jami' al-Kabir, mut'ah al-mithl is made the governing factor.
This is an apparent contradiction within the same imam.
2
Note the amounts
In al-Mabsut, the disputed amounts are large (1000 vs 2000 dirhams), so mut'ah al-mithl (typically less than half of the smaller claim, e.g., 500) is not useful. In al-Jami' al-Kabir, the amounts are small (10 vs 100), and mut'ah al-mithl (10) is comparable. In al-Jami' al-Saghir, no amount is given.
The usefulness of mut'ah al-mithl depends on the magnitude of the dispute.
3
Apply the reconciliation principle
When mut'ah al-mithl is less than the half claimed by the wife, it is not beneficial to make it the governing factor; when it is comparable, it is beneficial and thus used.
The author of al-Hidayah uses this principle to show there is no real contradiction.
4
Understand the epistemological weight
Al-Mabsut is the earliest and most authoritative of Imam Muhammad's works. Silent narrations (al-Jami' al-Saghir) are carried on what is mentioned in al-Mabsut.
This hierarchy resolves any residual ambiguity.
5
Connect to the broader dispute
This reconciliation supports the two companions' position that the governing factor in marriage is mahr al-mithl (or mut'ah al-mithl). It also shows how later Hanafi scholars harmonize apparent conflicts.
The reconciliation reinforces the mufta bihi position.

طرفین کی دلیل کا حاصل یہ ہے مدعی کے پاس اگر بینہ موجود نہ ہو ت مدعی علیہ کا قول مع الیمین معتبر ہوتا ہے اور مدعی علیہ وہ شخص کہلاتا ہے جس کا قول ظاہر حال کے موافق ہو۔ اور چونکہ نکاح میں موجب اصلی مہر مثل ہے۔ لہذا جس کا قول مہر مثل کے موافق ہو گا اس کا قول ظاہر حال کے موافق کہلائے گا۔
خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ طرفین کے نزدیک مہر مثل حکم ہے۔ چنانچہ اگر مہر مثل ایک ہزار یا اس سے کم ہے تو شوہر کا قول معتبر ہوگا۔ اور اگر مبر مثل دو ہزار یا اس سے زائد ہے تو عورت کا قول معتبر ہوگا اور اگر مہر مثل ایک ہزار اور دو ہزار کے درمیان ہے تو مہر مثل واجب ہو گا۔ اسکی مثال ایسی ہے کہ انگریز اور صاحب ثوب کے درمیان اجرت کی مقدار میں اختلاف ہوا مثلاً صاحب ثوب کہتا ہے کہ رنگنے کی اجرت ایک درہم ہے اور انگریز کہتا ہے کہ اجرت دو درہم ہیں تو اس صورت میں رنگ کی قیمت کو حکم بنایا جائے گا۔ اس کی صورت یہ ہوگی کہ پہلے بغیر رنگے کپڑے کی قیمت معلوم کرے۔ پھر رنگے ہوئے کی قیمت معلوم کرے۔ مثلاً بغیر رنگے کپڑے کی قیمت ہے دس درہم اور رنگے ہوئے کپڑے کی قیمت بارہ درہم ہیں۔ پس رنگ کی وجہ سے دو درہم کا اضافہ ہوا ہے تو یہ دو درہم رنگ کی قیمت ہوں گے ۔ لہذا اس قیمت کو حکم بنایا جائے گا۔ چنانچہ رنگریز کا قول اس قیمت کے موافق ہے تو صاحب ثوب کا قول معتبر ہوگا۔
ثم ذكر ههنا الح سے صاحب ہدایہ نے امام محمد کے اقوال میں تعارض بیان فرمایا ہے تعارض یہ ہے کہ امام محمد نے جامع صغیر اور مبسوط میں ذکر فرمایا کہ طلاق قبل الدخول کے بعد اگر مقدار مہر میں زوجین نے اختلاف کیا تو نصف مہر میں شوہر کا قول معتبر مانا جائے گا۔ اور متعہ مثل کو حکم نہیں بنایا جائے گا۔ اور جامع کبیر میں ذکر کیا ہے کہ متعہ مثل کو حکم بنایا جائے گا۔ متعہ مثل زوجین میں سے جس کے قول کے موافق ہو گا نصف مہر میں اس کا قول معتبر ہو گا۔ جامع کبیر کی روایت طرفین کے قول کے مطابق ہے۔ کیونکہ جس طرح طلاق سے پہلے مہر مثل موجب نکاح ہے اسی طرح طلاق قبل الدخول کے بعد متعہ موجب نکاح ہے۔ پس جس طرح مہر مثل حکم تھا۔ اسی طرح متعہ مثل بھی حکم ہونا چاہئے ۔ طرفین کا ذکر خاص طور سے اسلئے کیا گیا ہے کہ ابو یوسف کے نزدیک تمام صورتوں میں شوہر کا قول معتبر ہے۔ وجه التوفیق سے صاحب ہدایہ اس تعارض کو دور فرما رہے ہیں۔ فرماتے ہیں کہ مبسوط میں مسئلہ کی وضع ایک ہزار اور دو ہزار میں تھی ۔ یعنی شوہر مدعی تھا ایک ہزار کا اور عورت دعوی کر رہی ہے دو ہزار کا۔ اور متعہ بالعموم پانچ سوروپیہ کی مقدار کو نہیں پہنچتا ہے۔ اس وجہ سے متعہ کوحکم بنانے میں کوئی فائدہ نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ شوہر نصف مسمی یعنی پانچ سو کا پہلے ہی سے معترف ہے لہذا عورت کو پانچ سو درہم دے دیئے جائیں گے متعہ کو حکم بنانے کی چنداں ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ اور جامع کبیر میں مسئلہ وضع سو اور دس درہم میں ہے ۔ یعنی شوہر کا دعویٰ ہے کہ مہر دس درہم ہیں اور عورت کا دعوی ہے کہ مہر سو درہم ہیں۔ اور متعد مثل بالعموم ہیں درہم کا ہوتا ہے۔ پس اب متعہ کو حکم بنانا مفید ہوگا۔ چنانچہ اس صورت میں متعہ عورت کی جانب کیلئے مؤید ہے اور جامع صغیر میں مقدار مہر کا ذکر نہیں کیا گیا۔ بلکہ اس سلسلہ میں جامع صغیر ساکت ہے۔ لہذا جامع صغیر کی روایت کو اس پر محمول کیا جائے گا جو مبسوط میں مذکور ہے۔ کیونکہ امام محمد کی تمام کتابوں میں مبسوط ہی اصل ہے۔ اور بعض لوگ یہ بھی کہتے ہیں کہ مبسوط پہلے تصنیف کی گئی۔ اسکے بعد جامع صغیر تصنیف کی گئی ہے لہذا مبسوط میں جو مذکور ہو گا وہ متعارف کے مانند ہے۔ وشرح قولھما سے طرفین کے قول کی تشریح فرمارہے ہیں۔ تشریح یہ ہے کہ جب زوجین نے مقدار مبر قبل الطلاق میں اختلاف
The reason is that Imam Muhammad in al-Mabsut hypothesized the case with one thousand and two thousand, and mut'ah customarily does not reach that amount. So making mut'ah the governing factor would be useless. In al-Jami' al-Kabir, the case was set with one hundred and ten. And that woman's mut'ah al-mithl is not like that. So making mut'ah the governing factor would be useful. What is mentioned in al-Jami' al-Saghir is silent about the amount. Therefore, it will be carried on the amount mentioned in al-Mabsut. Explanation of the statement of the two (companions) in this case: when the dispute occurs at the time of the marriage contract, if the husband claims one thousand and the wife claims two thousand, then if the wife's mahr al-mithl is one thousand or less, the husband's statement (is accepted). If the mahr al-mithl is two thousand or more, the wife's statement (is accepted). If either establishes clear evidence, it will be accepted in both cases. If both present evidence, in the first case the wife's evidence is accepted because it proves the increase, and in the second case the husband's evidence because he proves the decrease. If the mahr al-mithl is one thousand five hundred, both take oaths, and when both have taken oaths, one thousand five hundred becomes obligatory. This is the derivation of Imam Abu Bakr al-Jassas al-Razi. Imam al-Karkhi said: Both take oaths in all three cases, then after that mahr al-mithl is made the governing factor. Explanation: This issue has several forms: the dispute between the spouses occurs during their lifetimes, or after both deaths their heirs dispute, or after the death of one spouse. If during their lifetimes they dispute, then there are two forms: this dispute occurs after divorce or before divorce. Then each of those has two forms: the dispute is about the original or about the named amount. The author first described the case where the spouses dispute about the amount of the dower at the time of the marriage contract, or after separation after consummation, or after the death of one spouse. For example, the husband claims the mahr is one thousand and the wife says two thousand. Regarding this, the school of the two (companions) is that the wife's statement is accepted up to the amount of mahr al-mithl, and the husband's statement is accepted for the excess over mahr al-mithl. If divorce occurred before consummation, regarding half the mahr only the husband's statement is accepted, not the wife's. Imam Abu Yusuf's school is that whether the dispute occurs after divorce or before divorce, in both cases the husband's statement is accepted, unless the husband mentions a trifling thing, then his statement is not accepted. There is disagreement among jurists about the meaning of a trifling thing. Some jurists hold that a trifling thing means less than ten dirhams. Summary: if the husband claims less than ten dirhams, his statement is not accepted; from ten dirhams and above, Abu Yusuf holds the husband's statement is accepted. The author of al-Hidayah says that the correct position is that in Abu Yusuf's view, a trifling thing means an unfamiliar mahr, meaning the husband mentions such a small amount that a woman of her like would not normally marry for that amount. Abu Yusuf's proof is that the wife is the claimant of the increase and the husband is the denier of the increase, and the rule is that in the absence of evidence from the claimant, the statement of the denier with an oath is accepted. Therefore, the husband, who denies the increase, his statement with an oath is accepted. But if the husband mentions such a trifling amount that apparent circumstances belie it, then his statement in that trifling amount is not accepted. The gist of Abu Yusuf's mentioned proof is that the usufruct of the vulva is not considered property, because the vulva is not wealth. However, to manifest the greatness of the vulva or for the purpose of procreation, the usufruct of the vulva is made considered property by necessity. So as long as it is possible to make the named mahr (which is the original) obligatory, one does not resort to mahr al-mithl (which is established by necessity). Therefore, Abu Yusuf says that regarding the named mahr, the husband's statement is accepted; mahr al-mithl will not be made the governing factor. The gist of the proof of the two (companions) is that if the claimant has no evidence, the statement of the defendant with an oath is accepted, and the defendant is the person whose statement agrees with the apparent circumstances. Since in marriage the original cause is mahr al-mithl, therefore the one whose statement agrees with mahr al-mithl, his statement will be called agreeing with the apparent circumstances. Summary: According to the two (companions), mahr al-mithl is the governing factor. So if mahr al-mithl is one thousand or less, the husband's statement is accepted. If mahr al-mithl is two thousand or more, the wife's statement is accepted. If mahr al-mithl is between one thousand and two thousand, mahr al-mithl becomes obligatory. An example: a dyer and a cloth-owner dispute the amount of wages. The cloth-owner says the dyeing wage is one dirham, the dyer says two dirhams. In this case, the value of the dyeing is made the governing factor. The method: first determine the value of the un-dyed cloth, then the value of the dyed cloth. For instance, the un-dyed cloth value is ten dirhams, the dyed cloth value is twelve dirhams. Thus the increase due to dyeing is two dirhams, which is the value of the dyeing. So that value is made the governing factor. Accordingly, if the dyer's statement agrees with this value, the cloth-owner's statement is accepted. Then, here, the author of al-Hidayah stated a contradiction in Imam Muhammad's statements. The contradiction is that Imam Muhammad in al-Jami' al-Saghir and al-Mabsut stated that after divorce before consummation, if the spouses dispute the amount of mahr, the husband's statement is accepted regarding half the mahr, and mut'ah al-mithl is not made the governing factor. But in al-Jami' al-Kabir, he stated that mut'ah al-mithl is made the governing factor, and whichever of the spouses has a statement agreeing with mut'ah al-mithl, his statement regarding half the mahr is accepted. The narration of al-Jami' al-Kabir agrees with the statement of the two (companions). Because just as before divorce mahr al-mithl is the cause of marriage, similarly after divorce before consummation mut'ah is the cause of marriage. So as mahr al-mithl was the governing factor, similarly mut'ah al-mithl should be the governing factor. The two (companions) are mentioned specifically because according to Abu Yusuf the husband's statement is accepted in all cases. The author of al-Hidayah removes this contradiction through reconciliation. He says: In al-Mabsut the case was set with one thousand and two thousand, meaning the husband claimed one thousand and the wife claimed two thousand, and mut'ah generally does not reach the amount of five hundred. Therefore, making mut'ah the governing factor is not beneficial because the husband already admits half the named mahr, i.e., five hundred, so the wife will be given five hundred dirhams; there is no need to make mut'ah the governing factor. In al-Jami' al-Kabir the case was set with one hundred and ten dirhams, meaning the husband claims the mahr is ten dirhams and the wife claims one hundred dirhams, and mut'ah al-mithl is generally ten dirhams. So here making mut'ah the governing factor is beneficial. In that case, mut'ah supports the wife's side. In al-Jami' al-Saghir the amount of mahr is not mentioned; rather, it is silent on this matter. Therefore, the narration of al-Jami' al-Saghir is carried on what is mentioned in al-Mabsut, because among all Imam Muhammad's books, al-Mabsut is the original. Some also say that al-Mabsut was composed first; then al-Jami' al-Saghir was composed later, so what is mentioned in al-Mabsut is like the customary. And the explanation of the statement of the two (companions): He (the author) is explaining the statement of the two (companions). The explanation is that when the spouses dispute the amount of mahr before divorce...

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute resolution and ruling statement from the Urdu sharh of al-Hidayah. It addresses the scenario where spouses disagree on the amount of mahr (dower), either during marriage or after divorce (before or after consummation). The text first explains the apparent contradiction in Imam Muhammad's statements across his works (al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir) regarding whether mut'ah al-mithl (the dower of the like for divorce before consummation) should be used as a governing factor. The reconciliation is based on different hypothetical amounts: in al-Mabsut, the amounts are large (1000 and 2000) where mut'ah al-mithl is less than half of the smaller claim, so it is not needed; in al-Jami' al-Kabir, the amounts are small (10 and 100) where mut'ah al-mithl is comparable, so it becomes relevant. The author then presents the ruling of the two companions (Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad, though contextually 'al-tarafayn' here likely refers to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad as opposed to Abu Yusuf) that the statement of the spouse whose claimed amount matches the mahr al-mithl (or mut'ah al-mithl) is accepted. Specifically, the wife's statement is accepted up to mahr al-mithl, and the husband's statement is accepted for any excess. For divorce before consummation, only the husband's statement is accepted regarding half the mahr. Imam Abu Yusuf's separate opinion is also detailed: he holds the husband's statement is always accepted unless he claims a trifling amount (shay' qalil), which is defined as an amount so low that a woman of her status would not normally marry for it. Abu Yusuf's reasoning is that the usufruct of the vulva is not inherently valuable, but by necessity it becomes considered property; therefore, the named mahr (original) takes precedence over mahr al-mithl. The passage concludes with a qiyas (analogy) to a dispute between a dyer and a cloth-owner to illustrate how mahr al-mithl is determined. This is a thorough explanation of the Hanafi positions on mahr disputes.

Key Terms
متعہ مثل (mut'ah al-mithl): The gift of consolation for a divorced woman before consummation, measured by the mahr al-mithl of a similar woman.
تعارض (ta'arud): Apparent contradiction between two narrations from the same authority.
محمل (mahmal): The contextual interpretation that resolves an apparent contradiction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does al-Hidayah state that in al-Mabsut, mut'ah al-mithl is not made the governing factor?
A) Because al-Mabsut is a less reliable text.
B) Because the hypothetical mahr amounts are large, so mut'ah al-mithl is too small to be beneficial.
C) Because Imam Muhammad changed his mind later.
D) Because the wife's claim was lower than mut'ah al-mithl.

Key Takeaway
Apparent contradictions within Imam Muhammad's narrations are resolved by considering the different hypothetical amounts assumed in each work.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
8 min
Mahr al-Mithl as the Arbiter in Mahr Disputes
General principle of mahr al-mithl as arbiter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the principle that mahr al-mithl is the arbiter in mahr disputes and apply it to determine which spouse's claim is accepted with oath.

Core Idea
Mahr al-mithl is the benchmark: the spouse whose claim matches it is the defendant, and their word prevails with oath.

This lesson explains the foundational Hanafi rule for resolving disputes over the amount of mahr. You will learn how mahr al-mithl functions as a legal arbiter, and see the analogy with the dyer and cloth owner that underpins the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal problem
The spouses disagree on the amount of mahr after marriage or divorce. No evidence is available.
2
Recognize mahr al-mithl as the asl
In marriage, the original basis (asl) is mahr al-mithl (the dower of a similar woman). The named mahr is a specification (tasmiyah).
3
Determine whose claim matches mahr al-mithl
Compare each spouse's claim to the market-determined mahr al-mithl. The spouse whose claim is closer to or matches mahr al-mithl is considered the defendant (mudda'a alayh) because the apparent situation supports them.
4
Apply the procedural rule
If mahr al-mithl ≤ husband's claim, husband's word with oath is accepted. If mahr al-mithl ≥ wife's claim, wife's word with oath is accepted. If mahr al-mithl is between both claims, it becomes wajib itself and no one's claim is taken; the procedure shifts to oaths from both.
This is the rule before evidence is considered.

Source Text
