تھا۔ اسی طرح متعہ مثل بھی حکم ہونا چاہئے ۔ طرفین کا ذکر خاص طور سے اسلئے کیا گیا ہے کہ ابو یوسف کے نزدیک تمام صورتوں میں شوہر کا قول معتبر ہے۔ وجه التوفیق سے صاحب ہدایہ اس تعارض کو دور فرما رہے ہیں۔ فرماتے ہیں کہ مبسوط میں مسئلہ کی وضع ایک ہزار اور دو ہزار میں تھی ۔ یعنی شوہر مدعی تھا ایک ہزار کا اور عورت دعوی کر رہی ہے دو ہزار کا۔ اور متعہ بالعموم پانچ سوروپیہ کی مقدار کو نہیں پہنچتا ہے۔ اس وجہ سے متعہ کوحکم بنانے میں کوئی فائدہ نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ شوہر نصف مسمی یعنی پانچ سو کا پہلے ہی سے معترف ہے لہذا عورت کو پانچ سو درہم دے دیئے جائیں گے متعہ کو حکم بنانے کی چنداں ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ اور جامع کبیر میں مسئلہ وضع سو اور دس درہم میں ہے ۔ یعنی شوہر کا دعویٰ ہے کہ مہر دس درہم ہیں اور عورت کا دعوی ہے کہ مہر سو درہم ہیں۔ اور متعد مثل بالعموم ہیں درہم کا ہوتا ہے۔ پس اب متعہ کو حکم بنانا مفید ہوگا۔ چنانچہ اس صورت میں متعہ عورت کی جانب کیلئے مؤید ہے اور جامع صغیر میں مقدار مہر کا ذکر نہیں کیا گیا۔ بلکہ اس سلسلہ میں جامع صغیر ساکت ہے۔ لہذا جامع صغیر کی روایت کو اس پر محمول کیا جائے گا جو مبسوط میں مذکور ہے۔ کیونکہ امام محمد کی تمام کتابوں میں مبسوط ہی اصل ہے۔ اور بعض لوگ یہ بھی کہتے ہیں کہ مبسوط پہلے تصنیف کی گئی۔ اسکے بعد جامع صغیر تصنیف کی گئی ہے لہذا مبسوط میں جو مذکور ہو گا وہ متعارف کے مانند ہے۔ وشرح قولھما سے طرفین کے قول کی تشریح فرمارہے ہیں۔ تشریح یہ ہے کہ جب زوجین نے مقدار مبر قبل الطلاق میں اختلاف کیا ۔ مثلا شوہر نے دعوی کیا کہ مہر ایک ہزار درہم ہے اور عورت دو ہزار کا دعوی کرتی ہے۔ تو اب اگر مہر مثل ایک ہزار یا اس سے کم ہے تو وبہ کا قول مع الیمین معتبر ہوگا۔ کیونکہ ظاہر حال شوہر کے قول کے موافق ہے۔ اور ظاہر حال جس کے قول کے موافق ہوتا ہے وہی مدعی مل یہ ہوگا۔ اور دعوی میں اگر مدعی کے پاس بینہ موجود نہ ہو تو مدعی علیہ کا قول مع الیمین معتبر ہوتا ہے۔ اور اگر مہر مثل دو ہزار یا اس سے زائد ب و عورت کا قول مع اسمیں معتبر ہوگا۔
اور اگر زوجین میں سے کسی ایک نے بینہ قائم کر دیا تو دونوں صورتوں میں ( مہر مثل شوہر کے قول کا شاہد ہو یا عورت کے قول کا ) اس کا بینہ قبول کر لیا جائے گا۔ اور اگر دونوں نے بینہ پیش کر دیا تو پہلی صورت ( جس وقت مہر مثل شوہر کے قول کا شاہد ہے ) میں عورت کا بینہ قبول کیا جائے گا۔ اور دوسری صورت ( جس وقت مہر مثل عورت کا شاہد ہے) میں شوہر کا بینہ قبول کیا جائے گا۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ بعینہ اس چیز کو ثابت کرتا ہے جو ظاہرا ثابت نہ ہو اور چونکہ پہلی صورت میں عورت کا قول خلاف ظاہر سے لہذا اس کا بینہ قبول ہوگا اور دوسری صورت میں شوہر کا قول خلاف ظاہر ہے۔ اس وجہ سے دوسری صورت میں شوہر کا بینہ قبول کیا جائے گا۔ اور اگر مہر مثل ڈیڑھ ہزار درہم ہے تو دونوں سے قسمیں لی جائیں گی کیونکہ زوجین میں سے ہر ایک مدعی بھی ہے اور منکر اور مدنی علیہ بھی ۔ اس لئے کہ شوہر دعوی کر رہا ہے کہ مسمی مہر مثل سے کم ہے اور عورت اس کی منکر ہے اور عورت کا دعویٰ مہر مثل سے زیادہ کا ہے۔ اور شوہر اس کا منکر ہے پس جب دونوں منکر ہیں تو دونوں سے قسمیں لی جائیں کیونکہ بینہ نہ ہونے کی صورت میں منکر پر قتسم واجب ہوتی ہے۔ رہی یہ بات کہ قسم کی ابتدا کون کرے گا، تو اس بارے میں قاضی خان میں مذکور ہے کہ قاضی ابتداء بالحلف کے سلسلہ میں قرعہ اندازی کرے اور یہ قرعہ اندازی مستحب ہے۔ ورنہ قاضی جس سے چاہے ابتدا کرائے۔ پس اگر شوہر نے قسم کھانے سے انکار کر دیا تو عورت کا قول معتبر ہو گا۔ اور دو ہزار درہم واجب ہوں گے۔ اور اگر عورت نے قسم سے انکار کر دیا تو شوہر کا قول معتبر ہو گا۔ اور ایک ہزار سمی واجب ہوگا اور اگر دونوں نے قسم کھالی تو ڈیڑھ ہزار درہم واجب ہوں گے۔ ایک ہزار بطریق تسمیہ کیونکہ ایک ہزار پر دونوں متفق ہیں۔ اور پانچ سو بطریق مہر مثل اور اگر ان دونوں میں سے کسی ایک نے بینہ پیش کر دیا تو اس کا بینہ قبول کر لیا جائے گا اور اگر دونوں نے پیش کر دیا تو مہر مشل ڈیڑھ ہزار درہم واجب ہوں گے۔ اور تعارض کی وجہ سے دونوں بہنیں باطل ہو جائیں گے۔ یہ امام ابو بکر جصاص رازی کی تخریج ہے اور امام کرخی نے فرمایا کہ تینوں صورتوں میں زوجین سے قسم لی جائے مہر شل زوج کے موافق ہو یا عورت کے موافق ہو یا کسی کے موافق نہ ہو قسم کے بعد مہر مثل کو حکم بنایا جائے گا۔ اسلئے کہ اصل تسمیہ پر تو دونوں متفق ہیں۔ اور تسمیہ صحیحہ مہر مثل کی طرف رجوع کو منع کرتا ہے۔ لیکن جب دونوں نے قسمیں کھا لی تو تسمیہ متعد ر ہو گیا۔ پس مہر شل کو حکم بنایا جائے۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب
(معینی شرح بداید )
اگر مہر مقرر میں اختلاف ہو تو بالا جماع مہر مثل واجب ہے
ولو كان الاختلاف في اصل المسمى يجب مهر المثل بالاجماع لانه هو الاصل عندهما وعنده تعذر القضاء بالمسمى قيصار اليه
ترجمہ اور اگر اختلاف اصل مسمی میں ہے تو مہر مثل واجب ہوگا بالا تفاق۔ اس لئے کہ مہر مثل ہی اصل ہے طرفین کے نزدیک اور یوسف کے نزدیک مسمی کے ساتھ فیصلہ متعذر ہو گیا لہذ امہر مثل کی طرف رجوع کیا جائے گا۔
Book of Nikah. The summary of the argument of the two parties is that if the claimant does not have evidence, the statement of the defendant with oath is accepted, and the defendant is the person whose statement is in accordance with the apparent situation. Since in marriage the original basis is mahr al-mithl, whoever's statement agrees with mahr al-mithl, his statement is deemed in accordance with the apparent situation. In summary, according to the two parties, mahr al-mithl is the arbiter. So if mahr al-mithl is one thousand or less, the husband's word is accepted. If mahr al-mithl is two thousand or more, the wife's word is accepted. If mahr al-mithl is between one thousand and two thousand, then mahr al-mithl is obligatory. An example of this is the dispute between the dyer and the cloth owner over the amount of wages: e.g., the cloth owner says the dyeing wage is one dirham, and the dyer says it is two dirhams. In this case, the value of the dyeing is made the arbiter. The procedure: first find the price of the un-dyed cloth, then find the price of the dyed cloth. E.g., the un-dyed cloth price is ten dirhams, the dyed is twelve dirhams. The increase of two dirhams is due to dyeing, so those two dirhams are the dye price. Then that price is made the arbiter. If the dyer's claim agrees with this price, the cloth owner's claim is accepted. Then the author of al-Hidayah mentions a contradiction in the statements of Imam Muhammad: In al-Jami' al-Saghir and al-Mabsut, he stated that after divorce before consummation, if the spouses disagree on the amount of mahr, the husband's word regarding half the mahr is accepted, and mut'ah al-mithl is not made the arbiter. In al-Jami' al-Kabir, he stated that mut'ah al-mithl is made the arbiter, and whichever spouse's statement agrees with it, his/her word regarding half the mahr is accepted. The narration of al-Jami' al-Kabir agrees with the statement of the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) because just as before divorce mahr al-mithl is the basis of marriage, similarly after divorce before consummation, mut'ah is the basis of marriage. So just as mahr al-mithl was the arbiter, so mut'ah al-mithl should also be the arbiter. The mention of the two is specifically because according to Abu Yusuf, in all cases the husband's word is accepted. The author of al-Hidayah resolves this contradiction via reconciliation. He says: In al-Mabsut, the case was set at one thousand and two thousand: the husband claimed one thousand, the wife claimed two thousand. Mut'ah normally does not reach five hundred. So making mut'ah the arbiter would be of no benefit because the husband already admits half the named sum, i.e., five hundred. Therefore the wife is given five hundred dirhams; there is no need to make mut'ah the arbiter. In al-Jami' al-Kabir, the case was set at one hundred and ten dirhams: the husband claimed the mahr is ten dirhams, the wife claimed it is one hundred dirhams. Mut'ah al-mithl is normally ten dirhams. So here making mut'ah the arbiter is beneficial. In this case, mut'ah supports the wife's side. In al-Jami' al-Saghir, the amount of mahr is not mentioned; it is silent on this. So its narration is interpreted according to what is in al-Mabsut, because among all of Imam Muhammad's books, al-Mabsut is the foundation. Some also say that al-Mabsut was written first, then al-Jami' al-Saghir, so what is mentioned in al-Mabsut is like the established practice. And the commentary on 'qaulihima' explains the statement of the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). The explanation: When the spouses disagree on the amount of mahr before divorce — e.g., the husband claims the mahr is one thousand dirhams, the wife claims two thousand — then if mahr al-mithl is one thousand or less, the husband's word with oath is accepted, because the apparent situation supports his word. And the person whose word is supported by the apparent situation is the defendant. In a claim, if the claimant has no evidence, the defendant's word with oath is accepted. If mahr al-mithl is two thousand or more, the wife's word with oath is accepted. If one of the spouses produces evidence, then in both cases (whether mahr al-mithl supports the husband or the wife), that evidence is accepted. If both produce evidence, then in the first case (where mahr al-mithl supports the husband), the wife's evidence is accepted; in the second case (where mahr al-mithl supports the wife), the husband's evidence is accepted. The reason is that evidence establishes what is not apparent. In the first case, the wife's statement is contrary to the apparent, so her evidence is accepted. In the second case, the husband's statement is contrary to the apparent, so his evidence is accepted. If mahr al-mithl is one thousand five hundred dirhams, then oaths are taken from both, because each spouse is both claimant and defendant. The husband claims the named mahr is less than mahr al-mithl, and the wife denies that; the wife claims more than mahr al-mithl, and the husband denies that. Since both are deniers, oaths are taken from both because in the absence of evidence, the oath is obligatory upon the denier. As to who begins the oath, it is mentioned in Qadikhan that the judge should do a lottery (qur'ah) regarding the initiation, and this lottery is recommended (mustahab). Otherwise, the judge may start with whomever he wishes. If the husband refuses to swear, the wife's word is accepted and two thousand dirhams become wajib. If the wife refuses, the husband's word is accepted and one thousand named mahr becomes wajib. If both swear, then one thousand five hundred dirhams become wajib: one thousand as the named mahr (since both agree on that), and five hundred as mahr al-mithl. If one of them produces evidence, that evidence is accepted. If both produce evidence, then mahr al-mithl of one thousand five hundred becomes wajib, and due to contradiction, both evidences become invalid. This is the deduction of Imam Abu Bakr al-Jassas al-Razi. Imam al-Karkhi said: In all three cases, oaths are taken from the spouses, whether mahr al-mithl agrees with the husband, the wife, or neither. After the oaths, mahr al-mithl is made the arbiter, because both agreed on the original specification (tasmiyah). A valid specification prevents recourse to mahr al-mithl. But when both take oaths, the specification becomes nullified, so mahr al-mithl is made the arbiter. And Allah knows best. (Mu'ini Sharh Bidayah). If there is a dispute over the fixed mahr, then by consensus mahr al-mithl is wajib. And if the dispute is over the original named mahr, mahr al-mithl is wajib by consensus because it is the original (basis) according to the two, and according to Abu Yusuf, since judgment by the named amount is impossible, recourse is made to mahr al-mithl.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah deals with the Hanafi rules for resolving disputes between husband and wife over the amount of mahr (dower). It is a commentary on al-Hidayah, expanding on the legal reasoning. The passage can be divided into several sections: first, the general principle that when spouses disagree on mahr, mahr al-mithl (dower of the like) is the benchmark. The author explains that the party whose claim matches mahr al-mithl is considered the defendant (mudda'a alayh) because apparent circumstances support them. Thus, if mahr al-mithl is lower, the husband's word is accepted; if higher, the wife's; if in between, mahr al-mithl itself becomes wajib. An analogy is made with a dispute between a dyer and cloth owner over wages, where the market value of dyeing dictates. Second, the passage addresses a seeming contradiction in Imam Muhammad's statements across his books regarding divorce before consummation. In al-Mabsut and al-Jami' al-Saghir, he said the husband's word is taken for half the mahr without considering mut'ah al-mithl; but in al-Jami' al-Kabir, he said mut'ah al-mithl is the arbiter. The reconciliation (tawfiq) offered by the commentator is that the cases differ in the amounts involved: in the first case the amounts are large (1000 vs 2000) so mut'ah is negligible; in the second case (10 vs 100) mut'ah is significant. Al-Jami' al-Saghir is silent on amounts, so it follows al-Mabsut as the foundational book. Third, the passage discusses rules of evidence and oaths when mahr al-mithl is exactly between the claims (1500). Both spouses are considered both claimant and denier, so oaths are taken from both. The procedure for starting oaths is by lottery or judge's choice. Consequences of oath refusal or swearing are detailed. Fourth, the views of two later Hanafi scholars, al-Jassas and al-Karkhi, are cited, with al-Karkhi preferring to always take oaths and then apply mahr al-mithl after the specification is nullified. Finally, a brief note reiterates that if the dispute is over the original mahr (i.e., whether any mahr was specified at all), mahr al-mithl is wajib by consensus.

Key Terms
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The dower of a woman similar to the wife in status, considering factors like family, beauty, and social standing.
بينة (bayyinah): Legal evidence, typically testimony of two male witnesses or one male and two females.
يمين (yamin): Oath taken by a defendant in the absence of evidence, required to be sworn by Allah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a mahr dispute without evidence, if mahr al-mithl is 1500, husband claims 1000, wife claims 2000, what is the ruling?
A) Husband's word accepted.
B) Wife's word accepted.
C) Both swear oaths and mahr al-mithl becomes wajib.
D) Evidence is required from both.

Key Takeaway
Mahr al-mithl is the legal benchmark; the spouse whose claim matches it is the defendant and their statement with oath is accepted.

Nikah — Marriage
advanced
10 min
Reconciling Imam Muhammad's Contradictory Narrations on Mut'ah al-Mithl
Resolution of apparent contradiction in Imam Muhammad's narrations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the apparent contradiction in Imam Muhammad's statements regarding mut'ah al-mithl and describe the reconciliation (tawfiq) based on the amounts in dispute.

Core Idea
Imam Muhammad's contradictory narrations are reconciled by the context: when mut'ah is negligible, ignore it; when significant, use it as arbiter.

In his various books, Imam Muhammad appears to contradict himself on whether mut'ah al-mithl (consolatory gift) should be used as an arbiter in mahr disputes after divorce before consummation. This lesson unpacks the reconciliation (tawfiq) provided by the commentator, showing that the apparent conflict arises from different factual scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conflicting narrations
In al-Mabsut and al-Jami' al-Saghir, Imam Muhammad does not apply mut'ah al-mithl. In al-Jami' al-Kabir, he applies it as arbiter.
The third book, al-Jami' al-Saghir, is silent on amounts, so it is interpreted via al-Mabsut.
2
Note the amounts involved in each narration
In al-Mabsut, the dispute is over 1000 vs 2000 dirhams. Mut'ah is normally around 500 dirhams, negligible compared to 500 half? Actually mut'ah max is 500, half the mahr is 1000 or 500? Wait: mut'ah al-mithl is typically up to 500, so in a 1000 vs 2000 dispute, half the mahr is 500 (if husband's claim is taken) or 1000 (if wife's). Mut'ah of 500 is not negligible compared to 500, but the commentator says mut'ah normally does not reach 500. Actually the text: 'متعہ بالعموم پانچ سوروپیہ کی مقدار کو نہیں پہنچتا ہے' meaning mut'ah normally does not reach 500. So in a 1000 vs 2000 case, half the mahr (500) is already equal to or more than mut'ah, so using mut'ah adds no benefit.
3
Understand the reconciliation
In al-Jami' al-Kabir, the dispute is over 10 vs 100 dirhams. Mut'ah is normally 10 dirhams. Here mut'ah is significant relative to the claims, so using it as arbiter is beneficial.
4
Realize that al-Mabsut is the foundational book
Imam Muhammad's al-Mabsut was written first, and al-Jami' al-Saghir follows it. The silent narration is interpreted based on al-Mabsut.

كتاب النكاح
طرفین کی دلیل کا حاصل یہ ہے مدعی کے پاس اگر بینہ موجود نہ ہو ت مدعی علیہ کا قول مع الیمین معتبر ہوتا ہے اور مدعی علیہ وہ شخص کہلاتا ہے جس کا قول ظاہر حال کے موافق ہو۔ اور چونکہ نکاح میں موجب اصلی مہر مثل ہے۔ لہذا جس کا قول مہر مثل کے موافق ہو گا اس کا قول ظاہر حال کے موافق کہلائے گا۔
خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ طرفین کے نزدیک مہر مثل حکم ہے۔ چنانچہ اگر مہر مثل ایک ہزار یا اس سے کم ہے تو شوہر کا قول معتبر ہوگا۔ اور اگر مبر مثل دو ہزار یا اس سے زائد ہے تو عورت کا قول معتبر ہوگا اور اگر مہر مثل ایک ہزار اور دو ہزار کے درمیان ہے تو مہر مثل واجب ہو گا۔ اسکی مثال ایسی ہے کہ انگریز اور صاحب ثوب کے درمیان اجرت کی مقدار میں اختلاف ہوا مثلاً صاحب ثوب کہتا ہے کہ رنگنے کی اجرت ایک درہم ہے اور انگریز کہتا ہے کہ اجرت دو درہم ہیں تو اس صورت میں رنگ کی قیمت کو حکم بنایا جائے گا۔ اس کی صورت یہ ہوگی کہ پہلے بغیر رنگے کپڑے کی قیمت معلوم کرے۔ پھر رنگے ہوئے کی قیمت معلوم کرے۔ مثلاً بغیر رنگے کپڑے کی قیمت ہے دس درہم اور رنگے ہوئے کپڑے کی قیمت بارہ درہم ہیں۔ پس رنگ کی وجہ سے دو درہم کا اضافہ ہوا ہے تو یہ دو درہم رنگ کی قیمت ہوں گے ۔ لہذا اس قیمت کو حکم بنایا جائے گا۔ چنانچہ رنگریز کا قول اس قیمت کے موافق ہے تو صاحب ثوب کا قول معتبر ہوگا۔
ثم ذكر ههنا الح سے صاحب ہدایہ نے امام محمد کے اقوال میں تعارض بیان فرمایا ہے تعارض یہ ہے کہ امام محمد نے جامع صغیر اور مبسوط میں ذکر فرمایا کہ طلاق قبل الدخول کے بعد اگر مقدار مہر میں زوجین نے اختلاف کیا تو نصف مہر میں شوہر کا قول معتبر مانا جائے گا۔ اور متعہ مثل کو حکم نہیں بنایا جائے گا۔ اور جامع کبیر میں ذکر کیا ہے کہ متعہ مثل کو حکم بنایا جائے گا۔ متعہ مثل زوجین میں سے جس کے قول کے موافق ہو گا نصف مہر میں اس کا قول معتبر ہو گا۔ جامع کبیر کی روایت طرفین کے قول کے مطابق ہے۔ کیونکہ جس طرح طلاق سے پہلے مہر مثل موجب نکاح ہے اسی طرح طلاق قبل الدخول کے بعد متعہ موجب نکاح ہے۔ پس جس طرح مہر مثل حکم تھا۔ اسی طرح متعہ مثل بھی حکم ہونا چاہئے ۔ طرفین کا ذکر خاص طور سے اسلئے کیا گیا ہے کہ ابو یوسف کے نزدیک تمام صورتوں میں شوہر کا قول معتبر ہے۔ وجه التوفیق سے صاحب ہدایہ اس تعارض کو دور فرما رہے ہیں۔ فرماتے ہیں کہ مبسوط میں مسئلہ کی وضع ایک ہزار اور دو ہزار میں تھی ۔ یعنی شوہر مدعی تھا ایک ہزار کا اور عورت دعوی کر رہی ہے دو ہزار کا۔ اور متعہ بالعموم پانچ سوروپیہ کی مقدار کو نہیں پہنچتا ہے۔ اس وجہ سے متعہ کوحکم بنانے میں کوئی فائدہ نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ شوہر نصف مسمی یعنی پانچ سو کا پہلے ہی سے معترف ہے لہذا عورت کو پانچ سو درہم دے دیئے جائیں گے متعہ کو حکم بنانے کی چنداں ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ اور جامع کبیر میں مسئلہ وضع سو اور دس درہم میں ہے ۔ یعنی شوہر کا دعویٰ ہے کہ مہر دس درہم ہیں اور عورت کا دعوی ہے کہ مہر سو درہم ہیں۔ اور متعد مثل بالعموم ہیں درہم کا ہوتا ہے۔ پس اب متعہ کو حکم بنانا مفید ہوگا۔ چنانچہ اس صورت میں متعہ عورت کی جانب کیلئے مؤید ہے اور جامع صغیر میں مقدار مہر کا ذکر نہیں کیا گیا۔ بلکہ اس سلسلہ میں جامع صغیر ساکت ہے۔ لہذا جامع صغیر کی روایت کو اس پر محمول کیا جائے گا جو مبسوط میں مذکور ہے۔ کیونکہ امام محمد کی تمام کتابوں میں مبسوط ہی اصل ہے۔ اور بعض لوگ یہ بھی کہتے ہیں کہ مبسوط پہلے تصنیف کی گئی۔ اسکے بعد جامع صغیر تصنیف کی گئی ہے لہذا مبسوط میں جو مذکور ہو گا وہ متعارف کے مانند ہے۔ وشرح قولھما سے طرفین کے قول کی تشریح فرمارہے ہیں۔ تشریح یہ ہے کہ جب زوجین نے مقدار مبر قبل الطلاق میں اختلاف کیا ۔ مثلا شوہر نے دعوی کیا کہ مہر ایک ہزار درہم ہے اور عورت دو ہزار کا دعوی کرتی ہے۔ تو اب اگر مہر مثل ایک ہزار یا اس سے کم ہے تو وبہ کا قول مع الیمین معتبر ہوگا۔ کیونکہ ظاہر حال شوہر کے قول کے موافق ہے۔ اور ظاہر حال جس کے قول کے موافق ہوتا ہے وہی مدعی مل یہ ہوگا۔ اور دعوی میں اگر مدعی کے پاس بینہ موجود نہ ہو تو مدعی علیہ کا قول مع الیمین معتبر ہوتا ہے۔ اور اگر مہر مثل دو ہزار یا اس سے زائد ب و عورت کا قول مع اسمیں معتبر ہوگا۔
اور اگر زوجین میں سے کسی ایک نے بینہ قائم کر دیا تو دونوں صورتوں میں ( مہر مثل شوہر کے قول کا شاہد ہو یا عورت کے قول کا ) اس کا بینہ قبول کر لیا جائے گا۔ اور اگر دونوں نے بینہ پیش کر دیا تو پہلی صورت ( جس وقت مہر مثل شوہر کے قول کا شاہد ہے ) میں عورت کا بینہ قبول کیا جائے گا۔ اور دوسری صورت ( جس وقت مہر مثل عورت کا شاہد ہے) میں شوہر کا بینہ قبول کیا جائے گا۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ بعینہ اس چیز کو ثابت کرتا ہے جو ظاہرا ثابت نہ ہو اور چونکہ پہلی صورت میں عورت کا قول خلاف ظاہر سے لہذا اس کا بینہ قبول ہوگا اور دوسری صورت میں شوہر کا قول خلاف ظاہر ہے۔ اس وجہ سے دوسری صورت میں شوہر کا بینہ قبول کیا جائے گا۔ اور اگر مہر مثل ڈیڑھ ہزار درہم ہے تو دونوں سے قسمیں لی جائیں گی کیونکہ زوجین میں سے ہر ایک مدعی بھی ہے اور منکر اور مدنی علیہ بھی ۔ اس لئے کہ شوہر دعوی کر رہا ہے کہ مسمی مہر مثل سے کم ہے اور عورت اس کی منکر ہے اور عورت کا دعویٰ مہر مثل سے زیادہ کا ہے۔ اور شوہر اس کا منکر ہے پس جب دونوں منکر ہیں تو دونوں سے قسمیں لی جائیں کیونکہ بینہ نہ ہونے کی صورت میں منکر پر قتسم واجب ہوتی ہے۔ رہی یہ بات کہ قسم کی ابتدا کون کرے گا، تو اس بارے میں قاضی خان میں مذکور ہے کہ قاضی ابتداء بالحلف کے سلسلہ میں قرعہ اندازی کرے اور یہ قرعہ اندازی مستحب ہے۔ ورنہ قاضی جس سے چاہے ابتدا کرائے۔ پس اگر شوہر نے قسم کھانے سے انکار کر دیا تو عورت کا قول معتبر ہو گا۔ اور دو ہزار درہم واجب ہوں گے۔ اور اگر عورت نے قسم سے انکار کر دیا تو شوہر کا قول معتبر ہو گا۔ اور ایک ہزار سمی واجب ہوگا اور اگر دونوں نے قسم کھالی تو ڈیڑھ ہزار درہم واجب ہوں گے۔ ایک ہزار بطریق تسمیہ کیونکہ ایک ہزار پر دونوں متفق ہیں۔ اور پانچ سو بطریق مہر مثل اور اگر ان دونوں میں سے کسی ایک نے بینہ پیش کر دیا تو اس کا بینہ قبول کر لیا جائے گا اور اگر دونوں نے پیش کر دیا تو مہر مشل ڈیڑھ ہزار درہم واجب ہوں گے۔ اور تعارض کی وجہ سے دونوں بہنیں باطل ہو جائیں گے۔ یہ امام ابو بکر جصاص رازی کی تخریج ہے اور امام کرخی نے فرمایا کہ تینوں صورتوں میں زوجین سے قسم لی جائے مہر شل زوج کے موافق ہو یا عورت کے موافق ہو یا کسی کے موافق نہ ہو قسم کے بعد مہر مثل کو حکم بنایا جائے گا۔ اسلئے کہ اصل تسمیہ پر تو دونوں متفق ہیں۔ اور تسمیہ صحیحہ مہر مثل کی طرف رجوع کو منع کرتا ہے۔ لیکن جب دونوں نے قسمیں کھا لی تو تسمیہ متعد ر ہو گیا۔ پس مہر شل کو حکم بنایا جائے۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب
(معینی شرح بداید )
اگر مہر مقرر میں اختلاف ہو تو بالا جماع مہر مثل واجب ہے
ولو كان الاختلاف في اصل المسمى يجب مهر المثل بالاجماع لانه هو الاصل عندهما وعنده تعذر القضاء بالمسمى قيصار اليه
ترجمہ اور اگر اختلاف اصل مسمی میں ہے تو مہر مثل واجب ہوگا بالا تفاق۔ اس لئے کہ مہر مثل ہی اصل ہے طرفین کے نزدیک اور یوسف کے نزدیک مسمی کے ساتھ فیصلہ متعذر ہو گیا لہذ امہر مثل کی طرف رجوع کیا جائے گا۔
Book of Nikah. The summary of the argument of the two parties is that if the claimant does not have evidence, the statement of the defendant with oath is accepted, and the defendant is the person whose statement is in accordance with the apparent situation. Since in marriage the original basis is mahr al-mithl, whoever's statement agrees with mahr al-mithl, his statement is deemed in accordance with the apparent situation. In summary, according to the two parties, mahr al-mithl is the arbiter. So if mahr al-mithl is one thousand or less, the husband's word is accepted. If mahr al-mithl is two thousand or more, the wife's word is accepted. If mahr al-mithl is between one thousand and two thousand, then mahr al-mithl is obligatory. An example of this is the dispute between the dyer and the cloth owner over the amount of wages: e.g., the cloth owner says the dyeing wage is one dirham, and the dyer says it is two dirhams. In this case, the value of the dyeing is made the arbiter. The procedure: first find the price of the un-dyed cloth, then find the price of the dyed cloth. E.g., the un-dyed cloth price is ten dirhams, the dyed is twelve dirhams. The increase of two dirhams is due to dyeing, so those two dirhams are the dye price. Then that price is made the arbiter. If the dyer's claim agrees with this price, the cloth owner's claim is accepted. Then the author of al-Hidayah mentions a contradiction in the statements of Imam Muhammad: In al-Jami' al-Saghir and al-Mabsut, he stated that after divorce before consummation, if the spouses disagree on the amount of mahr, the husband's word regarding half the mahr is accepted, and mut'ah al-mithl is not made the arbiter. In al-Jami' al-Kabir, he stated that mut'ah al-mithl is made the arbiter, and whichever spouse's statement agrees with it, his/her word regarding half the mahr is accepted. The narration of al-Jami' al-Kabir agrees with the statement of the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) because just as before divorce mahr al-mithl is the basis of marriage, similarly after divorce before consummation, mut'ah is the basis of marriage. So just as mahr al-mithl was the arbiter, so mut'ah al-mithl should also be the arbiter. The mention of the two is specifically because according to Abu Yusuf, in all cases the husband's word is accepted. The author of al-Hidayah resolves this contradiction via reconciliation. He says: In al-Mabsut, the case was set at one thousand and two thousand: the husband claimed one thousand, the wife claimed two thousand. Mut'ah normally does not reach five hundred. So making mut'ah the arbiter would be of no benefit because the husband already admits half the named sum, i.e., five hundred. Therefore the wife is given five hundred dirhams; there is no need to make mut'ah the arbiter. In al-Jami' al-Kabir, the case was set at one hundred and ten dirhams: the husband claimed the mahr is ten dirhams, the wife claimed it is one hundred dirhams. Mut'ah al-mithl is normally ten dirhams. So here making mut'ah the arbiter is beneficial. In this case, mut'ah supports the wife's side. In al-Jami' al-Saghir, the amount of mahr is not mentioned; it is silent on this. So its narration is interpreted according to what is in al-Mabsut, because among all of Imam Muhammad's books, al-Mabsut is the foundation. Some also say that al-Mabsut was written first, then al-Jami' al-Saghir, so what is mentioned in al-Mabsut is like the established practice. And the commentary on 'qaulihima' explains the statement of the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). The explanation: When the spouses disagree on the amount of mahr before divorce — e.g., the husband claims the mahr is one thousand dirhams, the wife claims two thousand — then if mahr al-mithl is one thousand or less, the husband's word with oath is accepted, because the apparent situation supports his word. And the person whose word is supported by the apparent situation is the defendant. In a claim, if the claimant has no evidence, the defendant's word with oath is accepted. If mahr al-mithl is two thousand or more, the wife's word with oath is accepted. If one of the spouses produces evidence, then in both cases (whether mahr al-mithl supports the husband or the wife), that evidence is accepted. If both produce evidence, then in the first case (where mahr al-mithl supports the husband), the wife's evidence is accepted; in the second case (where mahr al-mithl supports the wife), the husband's evidence is accepted. The reason is that evidence establishes what is not apparent. In the first case, the wife's statement is contrary to the apparent, so her evidence is accepted. In the second case, the husband's statement is contrary to the apparent, so his evidence is accepted. If mahr al-mithl is one thousand five hundred dirhams, then oaths are taken from both, because each spouse is both claimant and defendant. The husband claims the named mahr is less than mahr al-mithl, and the wife denies that; the wife claims more than mahr al-mithl, and the husband denies that. Since both are deniers, oaths are taken from both because in the absence of evidence, the oath is obligatory upon the denier. As to who begins the oath, it is mentioned in Qadikhan that the judge should do a lottery (qur'ah) regarding the initiation, and this lottery is recommended (mustahab). Otherwise, the judge may start with whomever he wishes. If the husband refuses to swear, the wife's word is accepted and two thousand dirhams become wajib. If the wife refuses, the husband's word is accepted and one thousand named mahr becomes wajib. If both swear, then one thousand five hundred dirhams become wajib: one thousand as the named mahr (since both agree on that), and five hundred as mahr al-mithl. If one of them produces evidence, that evidence is accepted. If both produce evidence, then mahr al-mithl of one thousand five hundred becomes wajib, and due to contradiction, both evidences become invalid. This is the deduction of Imam Abu Bakr al-Jassas al-Razi. Imam al-Karkhi said: In all three cases, oaths are taken from the spouses, whether mahr al-mithl agrees with the husband, the wife, or neither. After the oaths, mahr al-mithl is made the arbiter, because both agreed on the original specification (tasmiyah). A valid specification prevents recourse to mahr al-mithl. But when both take oaths, the specification becomes nullified, so mahr al-mithl is made the arbiter. And Allah knows best. (Mu'ini Sharh Bidayah). If there is a dispute over the fixed mahr, then by consensus mahr al-mithl is wajib. And if the dispute is over the original named mahr, mahr al-mithl is wajib by consensus because it is the original (basis) according to the two, and according to Abu Yusuf, since judgment by the named amount is impossible, recourse is made to mahr al-mithl.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah deals with the Hanafi rules for resolving disputes between husband and wife over the amount of mahr (dower). It is a commentary on al-Hidayah, expanding on the legal reasoning. The passage can be divided into several sections: first, the general principle that when spouses disagree on mahr, mahr al-mithl (dower of the like) is the benchmark. The author explains that the party whose claim matches mahr al-mithl is considered the defendant (mudda'a alayh) because apparent circumstances support them. Thus, if mahr al-mithl is lower, the husband's word is accepted; if higher, the wife's; if in between, mahr al-mithl itself becomes wajib. An analogy is made with a dispute between a dyer and cloth owner over wages, where the market value of dyeing dictates. Second, the passage addresses a seeming contradiction in Imam Muhammad's statements across his books regarding divorce before consummation. In al-Mabsut and al-Jami' al-Saghir, he said the husband's word is taken for half the mahr without considering mut'ah al-mithl; but in al-Jami' al-Kabir, he said mut'ah al-mithl is the arbiter. The reconciliation (tawfiq) offered by the commentator is that the cases differ in the amounts involved: in the first case the amounts are large (1000 vs 2000) so mut'ah is negligible; in the second case (10 vs 100) mut'ah is significant. Al-Jami' al-Saghir is silent on amounts, so it follows al-Mabsut as the foundational book. Third, the passage discusses rules of evidence and oaths when mahr al-mithl is exactly between the claims (1500). Both spouses are considered both claimant and denier, so oaths are taken from both. The procedure for starting oaths is by lottery or judge's choice. Consequences of oath refusal or swearing are detailed. Fourth, the views of two later Hanafi scholars, al-Jassas and al-Karkhi, are cited, with al-Karkhi preferring to always take oaths and then apply mahr al-mithl after the specification is nullified. Finally, a brief note reiterates that if the dispute is over the original mahr (i.e., whether any mahr was specified at all), mahr al-mithl is wajib by consensus.

Key Terms
متعة المثل (mut'ah al-mithl): A consolatory gift given to a divorced woman before consummation, valued according to the husband's status.
توفیق (tawfiq): Reconciliation of apparently contradictory texts or rulings by showing they apply to different contexts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did Imam Muhammad apply mut'ah al-mithl in one narration but not in another?
A) He changed his mind and the later narration abrogates the earlier.
B) The narrations are from different teachers and are both weak.
C) The cases had different amounts; in the first mut'ah was negligible, in the second it was significant.
D) The earlier narration was a mistake corrected later.

Key Takeaway
Imam Muhammad's different rulings on mut'ah al-mithl are reconciled by context: mut'ah is used when it has a significant relative impact on the outcome.

10 min
Procedures for Oaths and Evidence When Mahr al-Mithl is Between Claims
Oath and evidence rules when mahr al-mithl is the midpoint

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi procedure for taking oaths from both spouses and determine the outcome when mahr al-mithl is exactly between their claims and no evidence is presented.

Core Idea
When mahr al-mithl lies exactly between the claims, both spouses are both claimant and defendant; oaths are taken from both, and after oaths mahr al-mithl becomes wajib.

This lesson delves into the specific scenario where the spouses' claims are symmetric around mahr al-mithl, e.g., husband claims 1000, wife claims 2000, and mahr al-mithl is 1500. In this case, neither spouse's claim matches the benchmark, so a special procedure involving mutual oaths is triggered.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The spouses disagree on mahr. No evidence. Mahr al-mithl is exactly the midpoint between their claims.
2
Determine the legal positions
Each spouse is both a claimant (against the other's higher/lower claim) and a defendant (against the other's claim). The husband claims less than mahr al-mithl, so he denies the excess; the wife claims more, so she denies the shortfall.
3
Apply the oath procedure
Since both are defendants (and also claimants), oaths are taken from both. The judge may start with a lottery or choose whom to begin. If one refuses to swear, the other's claim is accepted. If both swear, the specification (tasmiyah) is nullified and mahr al-mithl becomes wajib.
This procedure is from al-Jassas's takhrij; al-Karkhi differs (see next lesson).
4
Consider the effect of evidence
If one spouse produces evidence, that evidence is accepted. If both produce evidence, both evidences cancel each other and mahr al-mithl becomes wajib.

دونوں نے پیش کر دیا تو مہر مشل ڈیڑھ ہزار درہم واجب ہوں گے۔ اور تعارض کی وجہ سے دونوں بہنیں باطل ہو جائیں گے۔ یہ امام ابو بکر جصاص رازی کی تخریج ہے اور امام کرخی نے فرمایا کہ تینوں صورتوں میں زوجین سے (معینی شرح بداید )
اگر مہر مقرر میں اختلاف ہو تو بالا جماع مہر مثل واجب ہے
ولو كان الاختلاف في اصل المسمى يجب مهر المثل بالاجماع لانه هو الاصل عندهما وعنده تعذر القضاء بالمسمى قيصار اليه
ترجمہ اور اگر اختلاف اصل مسمی میں ہے تو مہر مثل واجب ہوگا بالا تفاق۔ اس لئے کہ مہر مثل ہی اصل ہے طرفین کے نزدیک اور یوسف کے نزدیک مسمی کے ساتھ فیصلہ متعذر ہو گیا لہذ امہر مثل کی طرف رجوع کیا جائے گا۔
Book of Nikah. The summary of the argument of the two parties is that if the claimant does not have evidence, the statement of the defendant with oath is accepted, and the defendant is the person whose statement is in accordance with the apparent situation. Since in marriage the original basis is mahr al-mithl, whoever's statement agrees with mahr al-mithl, his statement is deemed in accordance with the apparent situation. In summary, according to the two parties, mahr al-mithl is the arbiter. So if mahr al-mithl is one thousand or less, the husband's word is accepted. If mahr al-mithl is two thousand or more, the wife's word is accepted. If mahr al-mithl is between one thousand and two thousand, then mahr al-mithl is obligatory. An example of this is the dispute between the dyer and the cloth owner over the amount of wages: e.g., the cloth owner says the dyeing wage is one dirham, and the dyer says it is two dirhams. In this case, the value of the dyeing is made the arbiter. The procedure: first find the price of the un-dyed cloth, then find the price of the dyed cloth. E.g., the un-dyed cloth price is ten dirhams, the dyed is twelve dirhams. The increase of two dirhams is due to dyeing, so those two dirhams are the dye price. Then that price is made the arbiter. If the dyer's claim agrees with this price, the cloth owner's claim is accepted. Then the author of al-Hidayah mentions a contradiction in the statements of Imam Muhammad: In al-Jami' al-Saghir and al-Mabsut, he stated that after divorce before consummation, if the spouses disagree on the amount of mahr, the husband's word regarding half the mahr is accepted, and mut'ah al-mithl is not made the arbiter. In al-Jami' al-Kabir, he stated that mut'ah al-mithl is made the arbiter, and whichever spouse's statement agrees with it, his/her word regarding half the mahr is accepted. The narration of al-Jami' al-Kabir agrees with the statement of the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) because just as before divorce mahr al-mithl is the basis of marriage, similarly after divorce before consummation, mut'ah is the basis of marriage. So just as mahr al-mithl was the arbiter, so mut'ah al-mithl should also be the arbiter. The mention of the two is specifically because according to Abu Yusuf, in all cases the husband's word is accepted. The author of al-Hidayah resolves this contradiction via reconciliation. He says: In al-Mabsut, the case was set at one thousand and two thousand: the husband claimed one thousand, the wife claimed two thousand. Mut'ah normally does not reach five hundred. So making mut'ah the arbiter would be of no benefit because the husband already admits half the named sum, i.e., five hundred. Therefore the wife is given five hundred dirhams; there is no need to make mut'ah the arbiter. In al-Jami' al-Kabir, the case was set at one hundred and ten dirhams: the husband claimed the mahr is ten dirhams, the wife claimed it is one hundred dirhams. Mut'ah al-mithl is normally ten dirhams. So here making mut'ah the arbiter is beneficial. In this case, mut'ah supports the wife's side. In al-Jami' al-Saghir, the amount of mahr is not mentioned; it is silent on this. So its narration is interpreted according to what is in al-Mabsut, because among all of Imam Muhammad's books, al-Mabsut is the foundation. Some also say that al-Mabsut was written first, then al-Jami' al-Saghir, so what is mentioned in al-Mabsut is like the established practice. And the commentary on 'qaulihima' explains the statement of the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). The explanation: When the spouses disagree on the amount of mahr before divorce — e.g., the husband claims the mahr is one thousand dirhams, the wife claims two thousand — then if mahr al-mithl is one thousand or less, the husband's word with oath is accepted, because the apparent situation supports his word. And the person whose word is supported by the apparent situation is the defendant. In a claim, if the claimant has no evidence, the defendant's word with oath is accepted. If mahr al-mithl is two thousand or more, the wife's word with oath is accepted. If one of the spouses produces evidence, then in both cases (whether mahr al-mithl supports the husband or the wife), that evidence is accepted. If both produce evidence, then in the first case (where mahr al-mithl supports the husband), the wife's evidence is accepted; in the second case (where mahr al-mithl supports the wife), the husband's evidence is accepted. The reason is that evidence establishes what is not apparent. In the first case, the wife's statement is contrary to the apparent, so her evidence is accepted. In the second case, the husband's statement is contrary to the apparent, so his evidence is accepted. If mahr al-mithl is one thousand five hundred dirhams, then oaths are taken from both, because each spouse is both claimant and defendant. The husband claims the named mahr is less than mahr al-mithl, and the wife denies that; the wife claims more than mahr al-mithl, and the husband denies that. Since both are deniers, oaths are taken from both because in the absence of evidence, the oath is obligatory upon the denier. As to who begins the oath, it is mentioned in Qadikhan that the judge should do a lottery (qur'ah) regarding the initiation, and this lottery is recommended (mustahab). Otherwise, the judge may start with whomever he wishes. If the husband refuses to swear, the wife's word is accepted and two thousand dirhams become wajib. If the wife refuses, the husband's word is accepted and one thousand named mahr becomes wajib. If both swear, then one thousand five hundred dirhams become wajib: one thousand as the named mahr (since both agree on that), and five hundred as mahr al-mithl. If one of them produces evidence, that evidence is accepted. If both produce evidence, then mahr al-mithl of one thousand five hundred becomes wajib, and due to contradiction, both evidences become invalid. This is the deduction of Imam Abu Bakr al-Jassas al-Razi. Imam al-Karkhi said: In all three cases, oaths are taken from the spouses, whether mahr al-mithl agrees with the husband, the wife, or neither. After the oaths, mahr al-mithl is made the arbiter, because both agreed on the original specification (tasmiyah). A valid specification prevents recourse to mahr al-mithl. But when both take oaths, the specification becomes nullified, so mahr al-mithl is made the arbiter. And Allah knows best. (Mu'ini Sharh Bidayah). If there is a dispute over the fixed mahr, then by consensus mahr al-mithl is wajib. And if the dispute is over the original named mahr, mahr al-mithl is wajib by consensus because it is the original (basis) according to the two, and according to Abu Yusuf, since judgment by the named amount is impossible, recourse is made to mahr al-mithl.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah deals with the Hanafi rules for resolving disputes between husband and wife over the amount of mahr (dower). It is a commentary on al-Hidayah, expanding on the legal reasoning. The passage can be divided into several sections: first, the general principle that when spouses disagree on mahr, mahr al-mithl (dower of the like) is the benchmark. The author explains that the party whose claim matches mahr al-mithl is considered the defendant (mudda'a alayh) because apparent circumstances support them. Thus, if mahr al-mithl is lower, the husband's word is accepted; if higher, the wife's; if in between, mahr al-mithl itself becomes wajib. An analogy is made with a dispute between a dyer and cloth owner over wages, where the market value of dyeing dictates. Second, the passage addresses a seeming contradiction in Imam Muhammad's statements across his books regarding divorce before consummation. In al-Mabsut and al-Jami' al-Saghir, he said the husband's word is taken for half the mahr without considering mut'ah al-mithl; but in al-Jami' al-Kabir, he said mut'ah al-mithl is the arbiter. The reconciliation (tawfiq) offered by the commentator is that the cases differ in the amounts involved: in the first case the amounts are large (1000 vs 2000) so mut'ah is negligible; in the second case (10 vs 100) mut'ah is significant. Al-Jami' al-Saghir is silent on amounts, so it follows al-Mabsut as the foundational book. Third, the passage discusses rules of evidence and oaths when mahr al-mithl is exactly between the claims (1500). Both spouses are considered both claimant and denier, so oaths are taken from both. The procedure for starting oaths is by lottery or judge's choice. Consequences of oath refusal or swearing are detailed. Fourth, the views of two later Hanafi scholars, al-Jassas and al-Karkhi, are cited, with al-Karkhi preferring to always take oaths and then apply mahr al-mithl after the specification is nullified. Finally, a brief note reiterates that if the dispute is over the original mahr (i.e., whether any mahr was specified at all), mahr al-mithl is wajib by consensus.

Key Terms
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The dower of a woman similar to the wife in status, considering factors like family, beauty, and social standing.
متعة المثل (mut'ah al-mithl): A consolatory gift given to a divorced woman before consummation, valued according to the husband's status.
بينة (bayyinah): Legal evidence, typically testimony of two male witnesses or one male and two females.
يمين (yamin): Oath taken by a defendant in the absence of evidence, required to be sworn by Allah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If husband claims 500, wife claims 1500, and mahr al-mithl is 1000, what is the first procedural step if no evidence is presented?
A) Accept husband's claim because 500 is less than 1000.
B) Accept wife's claim because 1500 is more than 1000.
C) Take oaths from both spouses.
D) Order a calculation of mahr al-mithl.

Key Takeaway
When mahr al-mithl is the midpoint, mutual oaths are required; after both swear, mahr al-mithl becomes wajib, nullifying the specification.

Nikah — Marriage

Later Scholarly Differences: Al-Jassas vs Al-Karkhi on Oath Procedure
Later Hanafi ikhtilaf on mutual oaths in mahr disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to differentiate between the takhrij of Imam Abu Bakr al-Jassas and the view of Imam al-Karkhi regarding the use of oaths in all mahr disputes, and identify which view is more widely adopted.

Core Idea
Al-Jassas restricts mutual oaths to the midpoint case; al-Karkhi extends it to all cases where mahr al-mithl is known, making oaths the universal procedure before imposing mahr al-mithl.

Beyond the classical narrations, later Hanafi scholars developed further refinements. This lesson examines the difference between Imam Abu Bakr al-Jassas al-Razi and Imam al-Karkhi on whether oaths should be taken from both spouses in every mahr dispute (not just the midpoint) before resorting to mahr al-mithl.

Guided Path
1
Recall the three scenarios
Scenario 1: mahr al-mithl supports husband (≤ his claim). Scenario 2: supports wife (≥ her claim). Scenario 3: between the claims.
2
State al-Jassas's takhrij
Al-Jassas follows the procedure described in the main text: only in Scenario 3 are oaths taken from both; in Scenarios 1 and 2, the one with matching claim is defendant and swears alone.
3
State al-Karkhi's view
Al-Karkhi holds that in all three scenarios, oaths should be taken from both spouses. His reasoning: the specification (tasmiyah) is valid and prevents recourse to mahr al-mithl; only when both swear does the specification become nullified, allowing mahr al-mithl.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
Under al-Jassas, in Scenario 1, husband's word is accepted without oath (just his oath as defendant). Under al-Karkhi, both must swear; if both swear, mahr al-mithl replaces the named mahr, which could change the outcome if mahr al-mithl differs.

(معینی شرح بداید )
اگر مہر مقرر میں اختلاف ہو تو بالا جماع مہر مثل واجب ہے
ولو كان الاختلاف في اصل المسمى يجب مهر المثل بالاجماع لانه هو الاصل عندهما وعنده تعذر القضاء بالمسمى قيصار اليه
ترجمہ اور اگر اختلاف اصل مسمی میں ہے تو مہر مثل واجب ہوگا بالا تفاق۔ اس لئے کہ مہر مثل ہی اصل ہے طرفین کے نزدیک اور یوسف کے نزدیک مسمی کے ساتھ فیصلہ متعذر ہو گیا لہذ امہر مثل کی طرف رجوع کیا جائے گا۔
Book of Nikah. The summary of the argument of the two parties is that if the claimant does not have evidence, the statement of the defendant with oath is accepted, and the defendant is the person whose statement is in accordance with the apparent situation. Since in marriage the original basis is mahr al-mithl, whoever's statement agrees with mahr al-mithl, his statement is deemed in accordance with the apparent situation. In summary, according to the two parties, mahr al-mithl is the arbiter. So if mahr al-mithl is one thousand or less, the husband's word is accepted. If mahr al-mithl is two thousand or more, the wife's word is accepted. If mahr al-mithl is between one thousand and two thousand, then mahr al-mithl is obligatory. An example of this is the dispute between the dyer and the cloth owner over the amount of wages: e.g., the cloth owner says the dyeing wage is one dirham, and the dyer says it is two dirhams. In this case, the value of the dyeing is made the arbiter. The procedure: first find the price of the un-dyed cloth, then find the price of the dyed cloth. E.g., the un-dyed cloth price is ten dirhams, the dyed is twelve dirhams. The increase of two dirhams is due to dyeing, so those two dirhams are the dye price. Then that price is made the arbiter. If the dyer's claim agrees with this price, the cloth owner's claim is accepted. Then the author of al-Hidayah mentions a contradiction in the statements of Imam Muhammad: In al-Jami' al-Saghir and al-Mabsut, he stated that after divorce before consummation, if the spouses disagree on the amount of mahr, the husband's word regarding half the mahr is accepted, and mut'ah al-mithl is not made the arbiter. In al-Jami' al-Kabir, he stated that mut'ah al-mithl is made the arbiter, and whichever spouse's statement agrees with it, his/her word regarding half the mahr is accepted. The narration of al-Jami' al-Kabir agrees with the statement of the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) because just as before divorce mahr al-mithl is the basis of marriage, similarly after divorce before consummation, mut'ah is the basis of marriage. So just as mahr al-mithl was the arbiter, so mut'ah al-mithl should also be the arbiter. The mention of the two is specifically because according to Abu Yusuf, in all cases the husband's word is accepted. The author of al-Hidayah resolves this contradiction via reconciliation. He says: In al-Mabsut, the case was set at one thousand and two thousand: the husband claimed one thousand, the wife claimed two thousand. Mut'ah normally does not reach five hundred. So making mut'ah the arbiter would be of no benefit because the husband already admits half the named sum, i.e., five hundred. Therefore the wife is given five hundred dirhams; there is no need to make mut'ah the arbiter. In al-Jami' al-Kabir, the case was set at one hundred and ten dirhams: the husband claimed the mahr is ten dirhams, the wife claimed it is one hundred dirhams. Mut'ah al-mithl is normally ten dirhams. So here making mut'ah the arbiter is beneficial. In this case, mut'ah supports the wife's side. In al-Jami' al-Saghir, the amount of mahr is not mentioned; it is silent on this. So its narration is interpreted according to what is in al-Mabsut, because among all of Imam Muhammad's books, al-Mabsut is the foundation. Some also say that al-Mabsut was written first, then al-Jami' al-Saghir, so what is mentioned in al-Mabsut is like the established practice. And the commentary on 'qaulihima' explains the statement of the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). The explanation: When the spouses disagree on the amount of mahr before divorce — e.g., the husband claims the mahr is one thousand dirhams, the wife claims two thousand — then if mahr al-mithl is one thousand or less, the husband's word with oath is accepted, because the apparent situation supports his word. And the person whose word is supported by the apparent situation is the defendant. In a claim, if the claimant has no evidence, the defendant's word with oath is accepted. If mahr al-mithl is two thousand or more, the wife's word with oath is accepted. If one of the spouses produces evidence, then in both cases (whether mahr al-mithl supports the husband or the wife), that evidence is accepted. If both produce evidence, then in the first case (where mahr al-mithl supports the husband), the wife's evidence is accepted; in the second case (where mahr al-mithl supports the wife), the husband's evidence is accepted. The reason is that evidence establishes what is not apparent. In the first case, the wife's statement is contrary to the apparent, so her evidence is accepted. In the second case, the husband's statement is contrary to the apparent, so his evidence is accepted. If mahr al-mithl is one thousand five hundred dirhams, then oaths are taken from both, because each spouse is both claimant and defendant. The husband claims the named mahr is less than mahr al-mithl, and the wife denies that; the wife claims more than mahr al-mithl, and the husband denies that. Since both are deniers, oaths are taken from both because in the absence of evidence, the oath is obligatory upon the denier. As to who begins the oath, it is mentioned in Qadikhan that the judge should do a lottery (qur'ah) regarding the initiation, and this lottery is recommended (mustahab). Otherwise, the judge may start with whomever he wishes. If the husband refuses to swear, the wife's word is accepted and two thousand dirhams become wajib. If the wife refuses, the husband's word is accepted and one thousand named mahr becomes wajib. If both swear, then one thousand five hundred dirhams become wajib: one thousand as the named mahr (since both agree on that), and five hundred as mahr al-mithl. If one of them produces evidence, that evidence is accepted. If both produce evidence, then mahr al-mithl of one thousand five hundred becomes wajib, and due to contradiction, both evidences become invalid. This is the deduction of Imam Abu Bakr al-Jassas al-Razi. Imam al-Karkhi said: In all three cases, oaths are taken from the spouses, whether mahr al-mithl agrees with the husband, the wife, or neither. After the oaths, mahr al-mithl is made the arbiter, because both agreed on the original specification (tasmiyah). A valid specification prevents recourse to mahr al-mithl. But when both take oaths, the specification becomes nullified, so mahr al-mithl is made the arbiter. And Allah knows best. (Mu'ini Sharh Bidayah). If there is a dispute over the fixed mahr, then by consensus mahr al-mithl is wajib. And if the dispute is over the original named mahr, mahr al-mithl is wajib by consensus because it is the original (basis) according to the two, and according to Abu Yusuf, since judgment by the named amount is impossible, recourse is made to mahr al-mithl.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah deals with the Hanafi rules for resolving disputes between husband and wife over the amount of mahr (dower). It is a commentary on al-Hidayah, expanding on the legal reasoning. The passage can be divided into several sections: first, the general principle that when spouses disagree on mahr, mahr al-mithl (dower of the like) is the benchmark. The author explains that the party whose claim matches mahr al-mithl is considered the defendant (mudda'a alayh) because apparent circumstances support them. Thus, if mahr al-mithl is lower, the husband's word is accepted; if higher, the wife's; if in between, mahr al-mithl itself becomes wajib. An analogy is made with a dispute between a dyer and cloth owner over wages, where the market value of dyeing dictates. Second, the passage addresses a seeming contradiction in Imam Muhammad's statements across his books regarding divorce before consummation. In al-Mabsut and al-Jami' al-Saghir, he said the husband's word is taken for half the mahr without considering mut'ah al-mithl; but in al-Jami' al-Kabir, he said mut'ah al-mithl is the arbiter. The reconciliation (tawfiq) offered by the commentator is that the cases differ in the amounts involved: in the first case the amounts are large (1000 vs 2000) so mut'ah is negligible; in the second case (10 vs 100) mut'ah is significant. Al-Jami' al-Saghir is silent on amounts, so it follows al-Mabsut as the foundational book. Third, the passage discusses rules of evidence and oaths when mahr al-mithl is exactly between the claims (1500). Both spouses are considered both claimant and denier, so oaths are taken from both. The procedure for starting oaths is by lottery or judge's choice. Consequences of oath refusal or swearing are detailed. Fourth, the views of two later Hanafi scholars, al-Jassas and al-Karkhi, are cited, with al-Karkhi preferring to always take oaths and then apply mahr al-mithl after the specification is nullified. Finally, a brief note reiterates that if the dispute is over the original mahr (i.e., whether any mahr was specified at all), mahr al-mithl is wajib by consensus.

Key Terms
تخریج (takhrij): A derivation or deduction of a ruling from the principles of the school, often used for later scholars' opinions.
تسمیہ (tasmiyah): The specification of mahr in the marriage contract, i.e., the named dower.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Karkhi, why should oaths be taken from both spouses even when mahr al-mithl supports one spouse?
A) Because the supported spouse might be lying.
B) Because the specification (tasmiyah) must be nullified by mutual oaths before resorting to mahr al-mithl.
C) Because the judge must always hear from both parties under oath.
D) Because the unsupported spouse has a right to swear.

Key Takeaway
Al-Jassas restricts mutual oaths to the midpoint case; al-Karkhi extends it universally; the mufta bihi follows al-Jassas.

Nikah — Marriage
beginner
5 min
Consensus Rule: Dispute Over Original Mahr (Asl al-Mahr)
Consensus ruling when mahr specification is disputed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a dispute over the amount of mahr and a dispute over whether any mahr was specified at all, and apply the consensus rule that mahr al-mithl becomes wajib in the latter case.

Core Idea
If spouses disagree on whether a mahr was specified (asl al-musamma), mahr al-mithl is wajib by consensus.

The earlier lessons dealt with disputes over the amount of a mahr that both acknowledge was specified. This lesson covers a different scenario: the spouses disagree on the very existence of a specified mahr. For example, the husband claims no mahr was specified, the wife claims it was. In such cases, mahr al-mithl becomes wajib by unanimous agreement (ijma') among the Hanafi scholars.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish between dispute over amount vs. dispute over existence
Previous lesson: both agree that some mahr was specified, but disagree how much. This lesson: one spouse (usually husband) denies any specification; the wife claims there was a specified mahr.
2
Identify the consensus
The text states: 'If there is a dispute over the original named mahr, mahr al-mithl is wajib by consensus (bil-ijma').' This is because the basis (asl) of marriage is mahr al-mithl; when the named amount is in doubt, the asl prevails.
3
Understand why Abu Yusuf's view aligns
Even Abu Yusuf, who normally favors the husband's word, agrees here: since the very existence of the specification is contested, neither party has a clear claim, so mahr al-mithl is default.

منع کرتا ہے۔ لیکن جب دونوں نے قسمیں کھا لی تو تسمیہ متعد ر ہو گیا۔ پس مہر شل کو حکم بنایا جائے۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب
(معینی شرح بداید )
اگر مہر مقرر میں اختلاف ہو تو بالا جماع مہر مثل واجب ہے
ولو كان الاختلاف في اصل المسمى يجب مهر المثل بالاجماع لانه هو الاصل عندهما وعنده تعذر القضاء بالمسمى قيصار اليه
ترجمہ اور اگر اختلاف اصل مسمی میں ہے تو مہر مثل واجب ہوگا بالا تفاق۔ اس لئے کہ مہر مثل ہی اصل ہے طرفین کے نزدیک اور یوسف کے نزدیک مسمی کے ساتھ فیصلہ متعذر ہو گیا لہذ امہر مثل کی طرف رجوع کیا جائے گا۔
Book of Nikah. The summary of the argument of the two parties is that if the claimant does not have evidence, the statement of the defendant with oath is accepted, and the defendant is the person whose statement is in accordance with the apparent situation. Since in marriage the original basis is mahr al-mithl, whoever's statement agrees with mahr al-mithl, his statement is deemed in accordance with the apparent situation. In summary, according to the two parties, mahr al-mithl is the arbiter. So if mahr al-mithl is one thousand or less, the husband's word is accepted. If mahr al-mithl is two thousand or more, the wife's word is accepted. If mahr al-mithl is between one thousand and two thousand, then mahr al-mithl is obligatory. An example of this is the dispute between the dyer and the cloth owner over the amount of wages: e.g., the cloth owner says the dyeing wage is one dirham, and the dyer says it is two dirhams. In this case, the value of the dyeing is made the arbiter. The procedure: first find the price of the un-dyed cloth, then find the price of the dyed cloth. E.g., the un-dyed cloth price is ten dirhams, the dyed is twelve dirhams. The increase of two dirhams is due to dyeing, so those two dirhams are the dye price. Then that price is made the arbiter. If the dyer's claim agrees with this price, the cloth owner's claim is accepted. Then the author of al-Hidayah mentions a contradiction in the statements of Imam Muhammad: In al-Jami' al-Saghir and al-Mabsut, he stated that after divorce before consummation, if the spouses disagree on the amount of mahr, the husband's word regarding half the mahr is accepted, and mut'ah al-mithl is not made the arbiter. In al-Jami' al-Kabir, he stated that mut'ah al-mithl is made the arbiter, and whichever spouse's statement agrees with it, his/her word regarding half the mahr is accepted. The narration of al-Jami' al-Kabir agrees with the statement of the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) because just as before divorce mahr al-mithl is the basis of marriage, similarly after divorce before consummation, mut'ah is the basis of marriage. So just as mahr al-mithl was the arbiter, so mut'ah al-mithl should also be the arbiter. The mention of the two is specifically because according to Abu Yusuf, in all cases the husband's word is accepted. The author of al-Hidayah resolves this contradiction via reconciliation. He says: In al-Mabsut, the case was set at one thousand and two thousand: the husband claimed one thousand, the wife claimed two thousand. Mut'ah normally does not reach five hundred. So making mut'ah the arbiter would be of no benefit because the husband already admits half the named sum, i.e., five hundred. Therefore the wife is given five hundred dirhams; there is no need to make mut'ah the arbiter. In al-Jami' al-Kabir, the case was set at one hundred and ten dirhams: the husband claimed the mahr is ten dirhams, the wife claimed it is one hundred dirhams. Mut'ah al-mithl is normally ten dirhams. So here making mut'ah the arbiter is beneficial. In this case, mut'ah supports the wife's side. In al-Jami' al-Saghir, the amount of mahr is not mentioned; it is silent on this. So its narration is interpreted according to what is in al-Mabsut, because among all of Imam Muhammad's books, al-Mabsut is the foundation. Some also say that al-Mabsut was written first, then al-Jami' al-Saghir, so what is mentioned in al-Mabsut is like the established practice. And the commentary on 'qaulihima' explains the statement of the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). The explanation: When the spouses disagree on the amount of mahr before divorce — e.g., the husband claims the mahr is one thousand dirhams, the wife claims two thousand — then if mahr al-mithl is one thousand or less, the husband's word with oath is accepted, because the apparent situation supports his word. And the person whose word is supported by the apparent situation is the defendant. In a claim, if the claimant has no evidence, the defendant's word with oath is accepted. If mahr al-mithl is two thousand or more, the wife's word with oath is accepted. If one of the spouses produces evidence, then in both cases (whether mahr al-mithl supports the husband or the wife), that evidence is accepted. If both produce evidence, then in the first case (where mahr al-mithl supports the husband), the wife's evidence is accepted; in the second case (where mahr al-mithl supports the wife), the husband's evidence is accepted. The reason is that evidence establishes what is not apparent. In the first case, the wife's statement is contrary to the apparent, so her evidence is accepted. In the second case, the husband's statement is contrary to the apparent, so his evidence is accepted. If mahr al-mithl is one thousand five hundred dirhams, then oaths are taken from both, because each spouse is both claimant and defendant. The husband claims the named mahr is less than mahr al-mithl, and the wife denies that; the wife claims more than mahr al-mithl, and the husband denies that. Since both are deniers, oaths are taken from both because in the absence of evidence, the oath is obligatory upon the denier. As to who begins the oath, it is mentioned in Qadikhan that the judge should do a lottery (qur'ah) regarding the initiation, and this lottery is recommended (mustahab). Otherwise, the judge may start with whomever he wishes. If the husband refuses to swear, the wife's word is accepted and two thousand dirhams become wajib. If the wife refuses, the husband's word is accepted and one thousand named mahr becomes wajib. If both swear, then one thousand five hundred dirhams become wajib: one thousand as the named mahr (since both agree on that), and five hundred as mahr al-mithl. If one of them produces evidence, that evidence is accepted. If both produce evidence, then mahr al-mithl of one thousand five hundred becomes wajib, and due to contradiction, both evidences become invalid. This is the deduction of Imam Abu Bakr al-Jassas al-Razi. Imam al-Karkhi said: In all three cases, oaths are taken from the spouses, whether mahr al-mithl agrees with the husband, the wife, or neither. After the oaths, mahr al-mithl is made the arbiter, because both agreed on the original specification (tasmiyah). A valid specification prevents recourse to mahr al-mithl. But when both take oaths, the specification becomes nullified, so mahr al-mithl is made the arbiter. And Allah knows best. (Mu'ini Sharh Bidayah). If there is a dispute over the fixed mahr, then by consensus mahr al-mithl is wajib. And if the dispute is over the original named mahr, mahr al-mithl is wajib by consensus because it is the original (basis) according to the two, and according to Abu Yusuf, since judgment by the named amount is impossible, recourse is made to mahr al-mithl.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah deals with the Hanafi rules for resolving disputes between husband and wife over the amount of mahr (dower). It is a commentary on al-Hidayah, expanding on the legal reasoning. The passage can be divided into several sections: first, the general principle that when spouses disagree on mahr, mahr al-mithl (dower of the like) is the benchmark. The author explains that the party whose claim matches mahr al-mithl is considered the defendant (mudda'a alayh) because apparent circumstances support them. Thus, if mahr al-mithl is lower, the husband's word is accepted; if higher, the wife's; if in between, mahr al-mithl itself becomes wajib. An analogy is made with a dispute between a dyer and cloth owner over wages, where the market value of dyeing dictates. Second, the passage addresses a seeming contradiction in Imam Muhammad's statements across his books regarding divorce before consummation. In al-Mabsut and al-Jami' al-Saghir, he said the husband's word is taken for half the mahr without considering mut'ah al-mithl; but in al-Jami' al-Kabir, he said mut'ah al-mithl is the arbiter. The reconciliation (tawfiq) offered by the commentator is that the cases differ in the amounts involved: in the first case the amounts are large (1000 vs 2000) so mut'ah is negligible; in the second case (10 vs 100) mut'ah is significant. Al-Jami' al-Saghir is silent on amounts, so it follows al-Mabsut as the foundational book. Third, the passage discusses rules of evidence and oaths when mahr al-mithl is exactly between the claims (1500). Both spouses are considered both claimant and denier, so oaths are taken from both. The procedure for starting oaths is by lottery or judge's choice. Consequences of oath refusal or swearing are detailed. Fourth, the views of two later Hanafi scholars, al-Jassas and al-Karkhi, are cited, with al-Karkhi preferring to always take oaths and then apply mahr al-mithl after the specification is nullified. Finally, a brief note reiterates that if the dispute is over the original mahr (i.e., whether any mahr was specified at all), mahr al-mithl is wajib by consensus.

Key Terms
أصل المسمى (asl al-musamma): The original named mahr; i.e., the existence of a specified mahr in the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When spouses disagree on whether any mahr was specified in the marriage contract, what is the default ruling?
A) The husband's word is accepted because he would have specified it.
B) The wife's word is accepted because she is the recipient.
C) Mahr al-mithl becomes wajib by consensus.
D) The marriage is invalid due to uncertainty.

Key Takeaway
If the very existence of a specified mahr is disputed, mahr al-mithl is wajib by consensus, regardless of the normal procedural rules.

Resolving Mahr Disputes: The Role of Mahr al-Mithl and Evidence
Explains which spouse's claim prevails when they dispute mahr amount, based on mahr al-mithl and evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rules for which spouse's claim is accepted in a mahr dispute and apply them to scenarios involving mahr al-mithl and evidence.

Core Idea
In a mahr dispute, the spouse whose claim aligns with mahr al-mithl is the defendant; if mahr al-mithl is between, both are plaintiffs-defendants.

When spouses disagree on the agreed mahr amount after consummation, the court must decide whose word to accept. The Hanafi school provides detailed rules based on the fair dowry (mahr al-mithl) and the principles of evidence. This passage from al-Hidayah walks through multiple scenarios, showing how the interplay of claims, mahr al-mithl, and evidence determines the outcome. It also presents a subtle intra-madhhab disagreement on when oaths are required.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claims and mahr al-mithl
Note the amount each spouse claims and the mahr al-mithl (fair dowry) for the wife.
Mahr al-mithl is the baseline; it represents what a woman of similar status would receive.
2
Determine which claim is supported by the apparent situation (zahir al-hal)
The claim that matches or is closer to mahr al-mithl is deemed the apparent truth. The spouse making that claim becomes the defendant.
The defendant's statement with an oath is accepted if no evidence is provided.
3
Analyze evidence if presented
If one spouse presents evidence, it is accepted regardless of mahr al-mithl. If both present evidence, the evidence of the spouse whose claim contradicts the apparent (i.e., whose claim differs from mahr al-mithl) is accepted, because it establishes what is not apparently true.
This preference for the 'contradicting' evidence is based on the principle that evidence confirms the truth when the default assumption is the opposite.
4
Handle the intermediate mahr al-mithl scenario
When mahr al-mithl falls exactly between the two claims (e.g., 1500 when husband claims 1000 and wife claims 2000), both spouses are both plaintiffs and defendants. In the absence of evidence, oaths are taken from both. If both swear, mahr al-mithl is imposed.
This follows the view of Imam al-Jassas. Imam al-Karkhi holds that oaths are required in all cases, not just this one.

رہا ہے کہ مسمی مہر مثل سے کم ہے اور عورت اس کی منکر ہے اور عورت کا دعویٰ مہر مثل سے زیادہ کا ہے۔ اور شوہر اس کا منکر ہے پس جب دونوں منکر ہیں تو دونوں سے قسمیں لی جائیں کیونکہ بینہ نہ ہونے کی صورت میں واجب ہوگا اور اگر دونوں نے قسم کھا لی تو ڈیڑھ ہزار درہم واجب ہوں گے۔ ایک ہزار بطریق تسمیہ کیونکہ ایک ہزار پر دونوں متفق ہیں۔ اور پانچ سو بطریق مہر مثل اور اگر ان دونوں میں سے کسی ایک نے بینہ پیش کر That is, for example, the husband claims that the dowry is one thousand dirhams, and the wife claims two thousand. So if the fair dowry (mahr al-mithl) is one thousand or less, then the husband's statement accompanied by an oath is accepted. Because the apparent situation agrees with the husband's statement. And the one whose statement the apparent situation agrees with is the defendant. And in a claim, if the plaintiff does not have evidence, then the defendant's statement with an oath is accepted. And if the fair dowry is two thousand or more, then the wife's statement with an oath is accepted. And if either spouse establishes evidence, then in both cases (whether the fair dowry supports the husband's statement or the wife's statement) that evidence is accepted. And if both present evidence, then in the first case (when the fair dowry supports the husband's statement) the wife's evidence is accepted. And in the second case (when the fair dowry supports the wife's statement) the husband's evidence is accepted. The proof is that it precisely establishes what is not apparently established, and since in the first case the wife's statement contradicts the apparent, her evidence is accepted, and in the second case the husband's statement contradicts the apparent, so his evidence is accepted. And if the fair dowry is one thousand five hundred dirhams, then oaths are taken from both because each spouse is both a plaintiff and a defendant. Because the husband claims that the named dowry is less than the fair dowry, and the wife denies that, and the wife claims more than the fair dowry, and the husband denies that. So when both are deniers, oaths are taken from both because in the absence of evidence, the oath is obligatory on the denier. As for who begins the oath, it is mentioned in Qadikhan that the judge should draw lots in the matter of initiating the oath, and this drawing of lots is recommendable. Otherwise, the judge may start with whomever he wishes. So if the husband refuses to swear, the wife's statement is accepted, and two thousand dirhams become obligatory. And if the wife refuses to swear, the husband's statement is accepted, and one thousand dirhams become obligatory. And if both swear, then one thousand five hundred dirhams become obligatory—one thousand by way of naming (since both agree on one thousand) and five hundred by way of the fair dowry. And if either of them presents evidence, that evidence is accepted. And if both present evidence, then the fair dowry of one thousand five hundred dirhams becomes obligatory, and both pieces of evidence become void due to contradiction. This is the deduction of Imam Abu Bakr al-Jassas al-Razi. And Imam al-Karkhi said that in all three cases, oaths are taken from the spouses, whether the fair dowry agrees with the husband or the wife or agrees with neither; after the oath, the fair dowry is adjudged. Because both agree on the original naming, and a valid naming prevents reference to the fair dowry. But when both have sworn, the naming becomes impossible, so the fair dowry is adjudged. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage discusses the rules when spouses dispute the amount of mahr (dower) after the marriage has been consummated. The author presents a series of scenarios based on the value of mahr al-mithl (fair dowry) relative to the amounts claimed by each party. The key principle is that the claim which aligns with the apparent situation (zahir al-hal) is given preference, meaning the one whose claim is supported by mahr al-mithl is considered the defendant (mudda'a alayh) and their statement with an oath is accepted. If mahr al-mithl equals the husband's claim, his word is taken; if it equals the wife's claim, hers is taken. If mahr al-mithl falls between the two claims (e.g., 1500 when husband claims 1000 and wife claims 2000), then both are considered both plaintiff and defendant, and oaths are required from both. The passage then discusses scenarios with evidence (bayyinah): if only one party has evidence, it is accepted regardless of mahr al-mithl; if both have evidence, the evidence of the party whose claim contradicts the apparent is accepted (since it establishes what is not apparently true). If both have evidence and mahr al-mithl is exactly between, both evidences are void and mahr al-mithl is imposed. The author then presents two different views: Imam al-Jassas's approach (as described) and Imam al-Karkhi's view that oaths are taken from both in all cases and then mahr al-mithl is applied, because the naming (tasmiyah) becomes impossible after oaths. This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf, but the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is generally that of the majority of the madhhab.

Key Terms
مهر مثل (mahr al-mithl): The fair dowry for a woman of similar status, determined by her family and social standing. Used as a default when the named mahr is disputed or absent.
قول مع اليمين (qawl ma'a al-yamin): The statement of a party accepted only if accompanied by an oath. Typically applies to the defendant when the plaintiff has no evidence.
بينة (bayyinah): Evidence, usually two male witnesses or one male and two females, that establishes a fact in court.
ظاهر حال (zahir al-hal): The apparent situation or default assumption, determined by mahr al-mithl in this context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When mahr al-mithl is exactly between the two claims (e.g., 1500 when husband says 1000 and wife says 2000), and neither spouse has evidence, what is the correct Hanafi procedure?
A) The husband's statement with an oath is accepted because he is the defendant.
B) The wife's statement with an oath is accepted because she is the defendant.
C) Oaths are taken from both; if both swear, mahr al-mithl (1500) is imposed.
D) The judge picks the midpoint arbitrarily.

Key Takeaway
In a mahr dispute, the spouse whose claim matches mahr al-mithl is the defendant; if mahr al-mithl is between, both are defendants, and oaths determine the mahr.
