Dispute Over the Existence of a Named Mahr (Asl al-Musamma)
Ruling with proof on dispute over existence of named mahr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when spouses dispute whether any mahr was named, and explain the Hanafi imams' differing reasoning behind that ruling.

Core Idea
When spouses dispute the very existence of a named mahr, mahr al-mithl is wajib by consensus, but the imams differ on the underlying principle.

In marriage, the mahr is a key obligation. What happens when one spouse claims a specific mahr was agreed upon, and the other denies any mahr was named at all? This lesson addresses that precise scenario. The ruling is agreed upon, but the reasoning reveals a subtle intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf that affects related rulings, such as the obligation of mut'ah upon divorce before consummation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
The passage describes a dispute between spouses about whether any mahr was named (asl al-musamma) at the time of the marriage contract. One claims it was named; the other denies it.
This is distinct from a dispute about the amount or type of mahr.
2
State the ruling by ijma
Both the matn and commentary affirm that mahr al-mithl (the customary mahr for a woman of her status) is wajib by consensus, and the denier's statement (with an oath) is accepted.
Ijma here covers the final ruling, even though the reasoning differs.
3
Distinguish the two reasoning approaches
Abu Hanifa and (according to the author's correction) Muhammad hold that mahr al-mithl is the principle (asl) in marriage – it applies when no mahr is proven. Abu Yusuf holds that the named mahr is the principle, but because of the dispute it cannot be enforced, so mahr al-mithl is resorted to as a substitute.
This difference is not merely academic; it affects whether mut'ah is wajib on divorce before consummation.
4
Note the correction about Imam Muhammad's position
The author of the Hidayah claimed that Muhammad agreed with Abu Hanifa, but the commentator corrects this, stating that Muhammad actually agrees with Abu Yusuf. Therefore, the majority (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the named mahr is the principle.
This correction is important for understanding the weight of the opinions.
5
Apply to a scenario
Consider: Husband says 'I named a mahr of 500 dirhams'; wife says 'No mahr was mentioned.' The wife's denial is accepted, so no named mahr is established. Mahr al-mithl becomes wajib. If divorce occurs before consummation, is mut'ah also wajib? According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the majority), since the named mahr is the principle but unenforceable, mut'ah is not required because mahr al-mithl already compensates. According to Abu Hanifa, mahr al-mithl is the principle, so mut'ah is also wajib.
The mufta bihi position is that mahr al-mithl is wajib, and the ruling on mut'ah follows the majority view (no additional mut'ah).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اگر مہر مقرر میں اختلاف ہو تو بالا جماع مہر مثل واجب ہے
ولو كان الاختلاف في اصل المسمى يجب مهر المثل بالاجماع لانه هو الاصل عندهما وعنده تعذر القضاء بالمسمى قيصار اليه
ترجمہ اور اگر اختلاف اصل مسمی میں ہے تو مہر مثل واجب ہوگا بالا تفاق۔ اس لئے کہ مہر مثل ہی اصل ہے طرفین کے نزدیک اور یوسف کے نزدیک مسمی کے ساتھ فیصلہ متعذر ہو گیا لہذ امہر مثل کی طرف رجوع کیا جائے گا۔
تشریح مذکورہ مسئلہ کی دوسری صورت یہ ہے کہ حالت حیات میں زوجین نے اصل مسمی میں اختلاف کیا۔ مثلاً ایک کہتا ہے کہ عقد نکاح کے وقت مہر کو ذکر کیا گیا تھا دوسرا اس کا منکر ہے تو اس صورت میں منکر کا قول معتبر ہو گا ۔ اور مہر مثل واجب ہوگا۔ طرفین کی دلیل تو یہ ہے کہ مہر مثل ہی اصل ہے۔ لہذا اسی کو اب کر دیا گیا ہے۔ اور ابو یوسف فرماتے ہیں کہ اصل تو مہر سمی ہے۔ لیکن چونکہ اختلاف کی وجہ سے مسمی کا فیصلہ متعذر ہو گیا اس لیئے مہر مثل واجب ہو گا۔ اور اس صورت میں اگر طلاق قبل الدخول ہے تو متعہ واجب ہوگا۔
اس جگہ بھی صاحب ہدایہ سے سہو ہو گیا۔ کیونکہ یہاں صاحب ہدایہ فرمارہے ہیں کہ مہر مثل کے اصل ہونے میں امام محمد ، امام ابو حنیفہ کے ساتھ ہیں ۔ حالانکہ ماقبل ص ۱۹ اپر اذا تزوجها على هذا العبد أو على هذا اعبد واحدهما او کس کے ذیل میں صراحت کی گئی ہے کہ امام محمد ابو یوسنت کے ساتھ ہیں۔ اور امام محمد کے نزدیک مہر مثل اصل نہیں ہے بلکہ مہر سمی اصل ہے۔ چنانچہ وہاں دیکھ لیا جائے۔
If there is disagreement over the fixed dower, then by consensus mahr al-mithl is obligatory.
And if the disagreement is over the existence of the named dower (asl al-musamma), mahr al-mithl is obligatory by consensus because it is the principle (asl) according to them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad?), and according to him (Abu Yusuf) the ruling by the named dower is impossible, so recourse is taken to mahr al-mithl.
Translation: And if the disagreement is over the existence of the named dower, then mahr al-mithl is obligatory by agreement. Because mahr al-mithl is the principle for both parties, and according to Abu Yusuf, judgment by the named dower has become impossible, so recourse is taken to mahr al-mithl.
Commentary: The second scenario of the mentioned issue is that during their lifetime, the spouses disagree over the existence of the named dower. For example, one says that the dower was mentioned at the time of the marriage contract, and the other denies it. In this case, the statement of the denier is accepted with an oath, and mahr al-mithl is obligatory. The proof of the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad?) is that mahr al-mithl is the principle, so it is adopted. And Abu Yusuf says that the principle is the named dower, but because of the dispute, judgment by the named dower has become impossible, so mahr al-mithl becomes obligatory. And in this case, if divorce occurs before consummation, then mut'ah (consolatory gift) is obligatory.
Here also there is an error by the author of the Hidayah. Because here the author of the Hidayah says that regarding mahr al-mithl being the principle, Imam Muhammad is with Imam Abu Hanifa. Whereas previously on page 19, under the discussion of 'idha tazawwajaha 'ala hadha al-'abd aw 'ala hadha al-'abd wahidahuma..., it was explicitly stated that Imam Muhammad is with Abu Yusuf. And according to Imam Muhammad, mahr al-mithl is not the principle, but the named dower is the principle. So look there.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage addresses the issue when the spouses disagree not about the amount of mahr but about whether any mahr was stipulated at all in the marriage contract. The author presents the matn (original text) saying that by consensus (ijma) mahr al-mithl is wajib in this case. The commentary then explains that during their lifetime, if one claims a mahr was named and the other denies it, the denier's statement (with an oath) is accepted, and mahr al-mithl becomes due. The disagreement among the Hanafi imams is about the underlying reasoning: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (according to the author's correction) hold that mahr al-mithl is the principle (asl) in marriage, so it is applied when the named mahr cannot be established. Abu Yusuf holds that the named mahr is the principle, but because of the dispute it cannot be enforced, so mahr al-mithl is applied as a secondary measure. The author also notes an error in Al-Hidayah regarding Imam Muhammad's position: the Hidayah claims Muhammad agrees with Abu Hanifa, but the author clarifies that, based on earlier discussions, Muhammad actually agrees with Abu Yusuf that the named mahr is the principle. This intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf has practical implications: for example, if divorce occurs before consummation, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad would hold that mut'ah (a consolatory gift) is wajib in this case as well, while Abu Yusuf's position may differ. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is that mahr al-mithl is wajib regardless, but the reasoning affects other related rulings.

Key Terms
اصل المسمى (asl al-musamma): The existence or fact of a named dower in the marriage contract.
متعہ (mut'ah): A consolatory gift given to a wife divorced before consummation when no mahr was named.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When spouses dispute whether a mahr was named in the marriage contract, who is believed with an oath?
A) The husband, because he is the one giving the mahr.
B) The wife, because she is entitled to a mahr.
C) The denier (the one who says no mahr was named).
D) The claimant (the one who says a mahr was named).

Key Takeaway
When spouses dispute the existence of a named mahr, the denier's oath is accepted and mahr al-mithl becomes wajib, despite intra-Hanafi differences on the underlying principle.

Mahr Dispute After Death of One Spouse
Ruling with proof and intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mahr dispute after the death of one spouse and apply the analogy (qiyas) to a marriage without mahr.

Core Idea
Death of one spouse does not extinguish the obligation of mahr al-mithl; the dispute is resolved as during their lifetimes.

This passage addresses an important nuance: if a dispute over mahr arises after one spouse has died, does the ruling change? The author clarifies that the same principles apply, because death does not negate the consideration of mahr al-mithl. The proof is an analogy (qiyas) to a marriage contracted without any mahr where one spouse dies. This lesson will walk through the scenario, the ruling, and the intra-Hanafi disagreement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Post-Death Scenario
The dispute occurs between the surviving spouse and the heirs of the deceased. The disagreement can be over the amount of mahr or over the existence of a named mahr.
2
Recall the Pre-Death Ruling
During their lifetimes, if spouses dispute over mahr amount, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold that mahr al-mithl is the standard; Abu Yusuf holds that the husband's statement (with oath) is accepted. If the dispute is over the existence of a named mahr, after consummation mahr al-mithl is wajib by consensus; before consummation mut'ah is wajib.
These details are from earlier in the text.
3
Recognize the Qiyas to Marriage Without Mahr
The author analogizes to a woman who marries without any mahr and then one spouse dies – in that case mahr al-mithl becomes wajib. Similarly, death does not drop the obligation of mahr al-mithl here.
The analogy is based on the shared illa (cause): death does not extinguish the right to mahr al-mithl.
4
Note the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf differs: he accepts the husband's claim as the payer. The mufta bihi (operative position) is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, i.e., mahr al-mithl is wajib.
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) is the amount paid to the wife/heirs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اگر اختلاف زوجین میں سے کسی ایک کی موت کے بعد ہوا تو کیا حکم ہے
ولو كان الاختلاف بعد موت احدهما فالجواب فيه كالجواب فى حياتهما لان اعتبار مهر المثل لا يسقط بموت احدهما
ترجمہ اور اگر اختلاف احد الزوجین کی موت کے بعد ہے تو اس صورت میں وہی حکم ہے جو حکم ان دونوں کی حیات میں تھا۔ اسلئے کہ مہر مثل کا اعتبار احد الزوجین کی موت سے ساقط نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ تشریح یہ مسئلہ مذکورہ کی تیسری صورت ہے۔ صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ زوجین میں سے جو زندہ ہے اس نے میت کے ورثہ کے ساتھ اختلاف کیا۔ مہر کی مقدار میں اختلاف کیا ہو یا اصل مسمی ہیں۔ دونوں صورتوں میں وہی حکم ہو گا جو حکم دونوں کی حیات میں اختلاف کی صورت میں تھا۔ یعنی اگر مقدار میں اختلاف ہے تو طرفین کے نزدیک مہر مثل حکم ہوگا اور امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک شوہر کا قول معتبر ہوگا۔ اور اگر اصل مسمی میں اختلاف ہے تو دخول کے بعد بالاتفاق مہر مثل واجب ہوگا اور دخول سے پہلے متعہ واجب ہوگا۔ تفصیل ماقبل میں گذر چکی ۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ احد الزوجین کی موت سے مہر مثل کا اعتبار ساقط نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ جیسے کسی عورت نے بغیر مہر کے کسی مرد سے نکاح کیا۔ پھر احد الزوجین کا انتقال ہو گیا تو اس صورت میں مہر مثل واجب ہوگا۔ اسی طرح یہاں بھی احد الزوجین کے انتقال سے مہر مثل ساقط نہیں ہو گا۔
What is the ruling if the disagreement occurs after the death of one of the spouses?
And if the disagreement is after the death of one of them, the answer is the same as the answer during their lifetimes, because the consideration of mahr al-mithl is not dropped by the death of one of them.
Translation: And if the disagreement is after the death of one of the spouses, then the ruling is the same as the ruling during their lifetimes. Because the consideration of mahr al-mithl is not dropped by the death of one of them.
Commentary: This issue is the third scenario. The scenario is that the surviving spouse disputes with the heirs of the deceased. Whether the dispute is over the amount of mahr or over the existence of the named mahr, in both cases the ruling is the same as in the case of dispute during their lifetimes. That is, if the dispute is over the amount, then according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) mahr al-mithl is the ruling, and according to Imam Abu Yusuf, the husband's statement is accepted. And if the dispute is over the existence of the named mahr, then after consummation mahr al-mithl is wajib by agreement, and before consummation mut'ah is wajib. The details have passed before. The proof is that the consideration of mahr al-mithl is not dropped by the death of one of them. For example, if a woman marries a man without a mahr, then one of them dies, in that case mahr al-mithl is wajib. Similarly here, mahr al-mithl is not dropped by the death of one.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage deals with the situation where one spouse dies before a dispute over mahr is resolved. The surviving spouse disputes with the heirs of the deceased. The author rules that the same principles apply as during the lifetimes of both spouses. The proof is by analogy (qiyas) to a marriage contracted without any mahr: if one spouse dies, mahr al-mithl is wajib. So here, the death does not invalidate the obligation of mahr al-mithl. The passage reiterates the earlier ikhtilaf: in a dispute over the amount, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold that mahr al-mithl is the standard, while Abu Yusuf holds that the husband's statement (with oath) is accepted. In a dispute over the existence of a named mahr, if consummation occurred, mahr al-mithl is wajib by consensus; if no consummation, mut'ah is wajib. The intra-Hanafi dispute remains relevant, and the mufta bihi is as previously stated.

Key Terms
ورثہ (warathah): Heirs of the deceased spouse who are parties to the dispute.
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The mahr customary for a woman of similar status.
قِياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning – applying a ruling from an original case to a new case due to shared effective cause (illa).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) No mahr is due because the marriage ends with death.
B) The husband's statement with oath is accepted.
C) The wife's statement with oath is accepted.
D) Mahr al-mithl is wajib.

Key Takeaway
Death of a spouse does not terminate the obligation of mahr al-mithl; the same rulings apply as during their lifetimes, based on analogy to a marriage without mahr.

Disagreement Over Mahr After Death of Both Spouses
Intra-Hanafi dispute on mahr after both spouses die

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on mahr disputes after both spouses' deaths and explain the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) of each view.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa: heirs' word rules; Abu Yusuf: except trivial claims; Muhammad: same as during life.

When both spouses are deceased, their heirs may dispute the mahr amount or its very existence. The Hanafi school has three distinct positions on whose statement is accepted. Understanding this ikhtilaf clarifies how evidentiary rules shift after death and why mahr al-mithl may or may not apply.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Recognize that the dispute occurs after both spouses have died – neither can testify. The heirs of each side claim different facts about the mahr.
2
State each imam's position
For amount dispute: Abu Hanifa accepts husband's heirs' statement; Abu Yusuf accepts heirs' statement unless trivial; Muhammad applies same rule as during life (mahr al-mithl). For existence dispute: Abu Hanifa accepts the denier's statement.
3
Identify the basis (dalil)
Abu Hanifa: after death, the spouses could not prove mahr al-mithl, so weight is given to heirs' statements. Muhammad: qiyas to the situation when alive. Abu Yusuf: balance – accept heirs' word but exclude implausibly low claims.
The source text does not elaborate the dala'il beyond these hints.
4
Determine the practical difference
Under Abu Hanifa, a very low claim by husband's heirs is accepted; under Abu Yusuf, it is rejected; under Muhammad, mahr al-mithl becomes wajib regardless of claims.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf.
5
Note the mu'tamad
Later Hanafi fatwa manuals often rely on Abu Hanifa's view for after-death disputes, but Muhammad's view is also strong and may be preferred in some contexts.
Consult reliable sources like Radd al-Muhtar for the final tarjih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اگر ورثہ میں اختلاف زوجین کی موت کے بعد ہوا تو شوہر کے ورثہ کا قول معتبر ہوگا۔ اقوال فقہاء
ولو كان الاختلاف بعد موتهما في المقدار فالقول قول ورثة الزوج عند ابي حنيفة ولا يستثنى القليل وعند ابي يوسف القول قول الورثة الا ان ياتوا بشئ قليل وعند محمد الجواب فيه كالجواب في حالة الحيوة و ان كان في اصل المسمى فعند ابي حنيفة القول قول من انكره فالحاصل انه لاحكم لمهر المثل عنده بعد موتهما على ما نبينه من بعد ان شاء الله
If the dispute occurs between the heirs after the death of the spouses, then the statement of the husband's heirs is accepted. Statements of the jurists:
And if the dispute over the amount occurs after both their deaths, then the statement of the husband's heirs is accepted according to Abu Hanifa, and no exception is made for a small amount. According to Abu Yusuf, the statement of the (wife's?) heirs is accepted, unless they bring a small amount. According to Muhammad, the answer is the same as during their lifetimes. And if the dispute is over the existence of the named mahr, then according to Abu Hanifa, the statement of the denier is accepted. The conclusion is that mahr al-mithl has no ruling according to him (Abu Hanifa?) after their deaths, as we will explain later, insha Allah.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage presents the most complex scenario: both spouses have died, and their heirs dispute the mahr. The author summarizes the positions of the three Hanafi imams.
- Abu Hanifa: In a dispute over the amount, the statement of the husband's heirs (with oath) is accepted, even if they claim a very small amount. In a dispute over the existence of the named mahr, the statement of the denier (whoever denies that a mahr was named) is accepted. For Abu Hanifa, after the death of both, the concept of mahr al-mithl is not applied; instead, the statement of the heirs is taken.
- Abu Yusuf: In a dispute over the amount, the statement of the heirs (likely the wife's heirs, or both? The text says 'qaul al-wuratha' but needs clarification) is accepted unless they claim a very small amount (presumably indicating dishonesty).
- Muhammad: The ruling is the same as during the lifetimes of the spouses. So if the dispute is over the amount, mahr al-mithl is wajib; if over the existence, the denier's statement is accepted, etc.
The passage notes that Abu Hanifa does not give weight to mahr al-mithl after the death of both spouses. This is a significant intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf. The relied-upon position for fatwa is typically that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, but there is variation.

Key Terms
ورثة الزوج (wurathat al-zawj): Heirs of the husband.
منكر (munkir): The person who denies the claim; in this context, the heir who denies that a mahr was named.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Mahr al-mithl is wajib.
B) The husband's heirs' statement with oath is accepted.
C) The wife's heirs' statement is accepted.
D) The judge divides the difference equally.

Key Takeaway
After both spouses die, the Hanafi school's primary view (Abu Hanifa) gives the husband's heirs' word decisive weight in mahr disputes, suspending mahr al-mithl.

Dispute Over Specified Mahr During Marriage: Ruling and Ikhtilaf
Explains ruling and intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on dispute about original mahr during lifetime

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when spouses dispute the specified mahr during marriage and explain the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the underlying principle (mahr al-mithl as original vs. substitute).

Core Idea
When spouses dispute the mahr, the denier's word is taken and mahr al-mithl is wajib—but imams differ on whether it is the original or a substitute.

In this passage, we examine a scenario where a married couple disagrees about the mahr that was specified at the time of marriage. The ruling is clear: the one who denies the specified mahr (usually the husband) has the say, and mahr al-mithl becomes obligatory. However, the Hanafi masters differ in their reasoning—Abu Hanifa considers mahr al-mithl the original, while Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad see it as a substitute when the specified mahr cannot be determined. The text also corrects a common misconception about Imam Muhammad's position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the ruling
The passage describes a dispute during the spouses' lifetime about the mahr that was specified at the time of marriage. The ruling: the denier's word is taken (the one who denies that any specific mahr was agreed upon), and mahr al-mithl becomes wajib.
The ruling applies regardless of which spouse is the denier, though typically the husband denies.
2
Understand the ikhtilaf between the imams
Abu Hanifa says mahr al-mithl is the original (asl). Abu Yusuf says the original is the specified mahr, but because the dispute makes it impossible to enforce, mahr al-mithl becomes wajib as a substitute. Both agree on the outcome but differ on the legal basis.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf about talil (reasoning), not the hukm itself.
3
Correct the error in Hidayah regarding Imam Muhammad
The author of Hidayah claimed Imam Muhammad agreed with Abu Hanifa. The passage clarifies that, based on earlier text, Imam Muhammad actually agrees with Abu Yusuf (specified mahr is original, mahr al-mithl is substitute).
This shows the importance of cross-referencing within the Hanafi corpus.
4
Note the special case of divorce before consummation
If divorce occurs before consummation in this disputed mahr scenario, the wife is entitled to mut'ah (a consolatory gift) instead of the full mahr al-mithl.
Mut'ah is wajib in Hanafi fiqh for pre-consummation divorce when no mahr was specified or when the specified mahr is disputed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تشریح مذکورہ مسئلہ کی دوسری صورت یہ ہے کہ حالت حیات میں زوجین نے اصل مسمی میں اختلاف کیا۔ مثلاً ایک کہتا ہے کہ عقد نکاح کے وقت مہر کو ذکر کیا گیا تھا دوسرا اس کا منکر ہے تو اس صورت میں منکر کا قول معتبر ہو گا۔ اور مہر مثل واجب ہوگا۔ طرفین کی دلیل تو یہ ہے کہ مہر مثل ہی اصل ہے۔ لہذا اسی کو حکم کر دیا گیا ہے۔ اور ابو یوسف فرماتے ہیں کہ اصل تو مہر سمی ہے۔ لیکن چونکہ اختلاف کی وجہ سے مسمی کا فیصلہ متعذر ہو گیا اس لیئے مہر مثل واجب ہو گا۔ اور اس صورت میں اگر طلاق قبل الدخول ہے تو متعہ واجب ہوگا۔ اس جگہ بھی صاحب ہدایہ سے سہو ہو گیا۔ کیونکہ یہاں صاحب ہدایہ فرمارہے ہیں کہ مہر مثل کے اصل ہونے میں امام محمد، امام ابو حنیفہ کے ساتھ ہیں۔ حالانکہ ماقبل ص ۱۹ پر "اذا تزوجها على هذا العبد أو على هذا العبد واحدهما..." کے ذیل میں صراحت کی گئی ہے کہ امام محمد ابو یوسف کے ساتھ ہیں۔ اور امام محمد کے نزدیک مہر مثل اصل ہے نہ کہ مہر سمی۔ چنانچہ وہاں دیکھ لیا جائے۔
Explanation of the second scenario of the mentioned issue: that during lifetime the spouses dispute the specified mahr. For example, one says that at the time of marriage the mahr was mentioned, the other denies it. In this case the say of the denier is reliable, and mahr al-mithl becomes obligatory. The proof of the two parties (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) is that mahr al-mithl is the origin, so that is taken as the ruling. And Abu Yusuf says: the origin is the specified mahr, but because due to the dispute a decision on the specified mahr is impossible, therefore mahr al-mithl becomes obligatory. And in this case if divorce occurs before consummation, mut'ah becomes obligatory. At this place also there is an error from the author of Hidayah. Because here the author of Hidayah says that regarding mahr al-mithl being the origin, Imam Muhammad is with Abu Hanifa. Whereas in the preceding page 19 under "when he marries her on this slave or this slave..." it is clearly stated that Imam Muhammad is with Abu Yusuf. And according to Imam Muhammad, mahr al-mithl is the origin, not the specified mahr. So refer there.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about a specific scenario: when a married couple disputes the amount of mahr that was specified at the time of marriage. The ruling presented is that during the lifetime of both spouses, if they disagree about whether a mahr was specified, the one who denies it (the husband) has the say, and the wife is entitled to mahr al-mithl (the mahr of her peers). The text notes a distinction: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf actually agree on the result (mahr al-mithl becomes wajib) but differ in their reasoning. Abu Hanifa says mahr al-mithl is the original/default, while Abu Yusuf says the original is the specified mahr but since agreement on it is impossible due to dispute, mahr al-mithl becomes the substitute. The passage also points out a correction: the author of Hidayah claimed Imam Muhammad agrees with Abu Hanifa on this, but the text clarifies that Imam Muhammad actually agrees with Abu Yusuf. The ruling also mentions that if divorce occurs before consummation, mut'ah (a consolatory gift) is wajib instead of the full mahr.

Key Terms
مہر مثل (mahr al-mithl): The mahr of a woman similar in status, determined by her family's social standing and personal attributes, used when no mahr is specified or when the specified mahr is disputed.
مہر مسمی (mahr musamma): The specific mahr that is mentioned and agreed upon at the time of marriage.
متعة (mut'ah): A consolatory gift given to the wife in case of divorce before consummation when no mahr was specified.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling when spouses dispute the specified mahr during their lifetime?
A) The husband's claim is accepted and the specified mahr is enforced.
B) The denier's word is taken and mahr al-mithl becomes wajib.
C) The wife's claim is accepted and she gets what she claims.
D) The judge decides based on evidence.

Key Takeaway
When spouses dispute the specified mahr during marriage, the denier's word is taken and mahr al-mithl becomes wajib, with an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on whether mahr al-mithl is the original or a substitute.

Dispute After Both Deaths: Mahr Al-Mithl in Intra-Hanafi Ruling
Intra-Hanafi dispute on mahr after death of both spouses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the intra-Hanafi positions on mahr disputes after both spouses die and identify the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
After both spouses die, mahr al-mithl is imposed by Sahibayn and the majority, overriding Abu Hanifa's view.

This passage presents a unique intra-Hanafi dispute where both spouses have died and their heirs argue over the mahr. The disagreement centers on whether mahr al-mithl can still be imposed when the original mahr is denied. Understanding this scenario helps clarify the Hanafi approach to debts that survive death.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of dispute
Discerning whether the dispute is about the amount (miqdar) of the mahr or about the original specification (asl al-musamma) is crucial, as each leads to different rulings.
The text clearly separates 'al-miqdar' and 'asl al-musamma'.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position for each type
For amount: husband's heirs' word is taken, even if they claim a small amount. For original mahr: the denier's word is taken, and no mahr al-mithl is imposed.
Abu Hanifa argues that death extinguishes the possibility of determining mahr al-mithl.
3
State Sahibayn's positions
Abu Yusuf accepts the husband's heirs' word except if they claim a small amount; Muhammad equates the post-death scenario to the lifetime scenario, thus mahr al-mithl applies.
Muhammad uses qiyas to the lifetime case.
4
Recognize the fatwa position for original mahr dispute
According to Sahibayn and the other three imams, mahr al-mithl is wajib from the husband's estate. This is the mufta bihi ruling.
The text explicitly says 'the fatwa is also according to their statement'.
5
Note the sub-ikhtilaf with Shafi'i regarding tahluf
Imam Shafi'i requires mutual oath-taking (tahluf) before imposing mahr al-mithl, while Sahibayn, Malik, and Ahmad do not.
This difference affects procedure but not the core ruling of wajib.

If the dispute occurs among the heirs after the death of both spouses, then the word of the husband's heirs is reliable. Statements of jurists: And if the dispute is after their death regarding the amount, then the word is that of the husband's heirs according to Abu Hanifa, and he does not make an exception for a small amount. According to Abu Yusuf, the word is that of the heirs (husband's) unless they bring a small amount. According to Muhammad, the answer in this case is the same as the answer in the state of lifetime. And if it is about the original specified [mahr], then according to Abu Hanifa the word is of the one who denies the specification. So the conclusion is that according to Abu Hanifa, there is no ruling of mahr al-mithl after their death, as we will explain later if Allah wills. Explanation: This is the fourth scenario of the mentioned issue. The scenario is that after the death of both spouses, their heirs dispute about the specified amount. The Hanafis differ on its ruling. Abu Hanifa says the word of the husband's heirs with the oath is reliable, and he does not except even a small amount. Even if they claim a small amount, their word is accepted. Abu Yusuf also says the husband's heirs' word is reliable, but he excepts a small amount. So if the husband's heirs claim a small amount, it is not acceptable according to Abu Yusuf. Imam Muhammad says the ruling is the same as in the lifetime scenario. That is, just as in lifetime mahr al-mithl was made the ruling, similarly after both deaths mahr al-mithl is the ruling. Muhammad analogizes the post-death state to the pre-death state. The proof of Abu Yusuf has passed in the previous issue. The summary of Abu Hanifa's proof is that the husband's heirs deny an increase in the mahr, and in the absence of evidence, the word of the denier with the oath is reliable. So the word of the husband's heirs with the oath is reliable. And if the heirs dispute about the original specified mahr, Abu Hanifa considers the word of the one who denies the specification reliable, but nothing becomes wajib on the husband's heirs. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), in this case mahr al-mithl is decreed. Imam Malik, Imam Shafi'i, and Imam Ahmad also hold this view, and the fatwa is also according to their statement. But Imam Shafi'i makes mahr al-mithl wajib after tahluf (oath-swearing), while according to the two, Imam Malik, and Imam Ahmad, tahluf is not wajib. The proofs of all have been stated in the next issue. Wait a little. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage details the intra-Hanafi disagreement on the ruling after both spouses have died and their heirs dispute the mahr. Two types of dispute are considered: one about the amount (miqdar) and one about the original specification (al-musamma). For the amount dispute, Abu Hanifa gives full weight to the husband's heirs' statement, even if they claim a small amount, because they are the deniers of an extra claim. Abu Yusuf agrees but excepts a small amount (i.e., if they claim an unusually low amount, it is not accepted). Imam Muhammad equates the situation to the lifetime scenario, so mahr al-mithl is imposed. For the original mahr dispute, Abu Hanifa does not impose mahr al-mithl at all, while Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) impose mahr al-mithl, and this view is supported by the other three imams (Malik, Shafi'i, Ahmad) and is the basis for fatwa. The text also notes a sub-difference: Shafi'i requires tahluf (mutual oath-taking) before mahr al-mithl, while the others do not.

Key Terms
مقدار (miqdar): The amount or quantum of the specified mahr that is being disputed.
تحالف (tahluf): Mutual oath-swearing between the parties when evidence is lacking, used to resolve disputes.
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The mahr of an equivalent woman in social status, used when the original mahr is unspecified or disputed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which view is followed in fatwa regarding dispute after both deaths?
A) Abu Hanifa's view that husband's heirs' word is taken.
B) Sahibayn's view that mahr al-mithl is wajib.
C) Imam Shafi'i's view requiring tahluf.
D) Imam Muhammad's view that it is like the lifetime case.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fatwa, after both spouses die, mahr al-mithl is imposed on the husband's estate if the original mahr is disputed, adopting the view of Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and the majority.

Inheritance of Mahr When Both Spouses Die
Ruling on inheritance of mahr when both die, with intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on inheritance of mahr when both spouses die, distinguish between specified and unspecified mahr, and explain Abu Hanifa's argument of inqiraḍ aqrān.

Core Idea
When both spouses die, specified mahr is inherited; unspecified mahr is not due according to Abu Hanifa due to extinction of peers.

This passage addresses a unique scenario in marriage law: both spouses have died, and the question is whether the wife's heirs can claim mahr from the husband's estate. The ruling depends on whether a mahr was specified or not, and the Hanafi school itself is divided. Understanding this ikhtilaf reveals how the school balances debt priority with the practical difficulty of determining mahr al-mithl after both parties are gone.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage first considers whether a mahr was specified or not. List both scenarios.
2
State the ruling for specified mahr
The wife's heirs take the specified mahr from the husband's estate, unless she died first.
3
State the ruling for unspecified mahr
Abu Hanifa says nothing is due; Sahibayn say mahr al-mithl is due.
4
Analyze the proof of Sahibayn
They use qiyas: mahr al-mithl becomes a debt like specified mahr and is not dropped by death, analogous to when one spouse dies.
5
Analyze the proof of Abu Hanifa
He argues that the death of both indicates extinction of peers (inqiraḍ aqrān), making it impossible for the judge to estimate mahr al-mithl.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
زوجین فوت ہو گئے اور مہر مقرر تھا تو عورت کے ورثہ اس کی میراث سے لیس اور اگر مہر مقرر نہیں تھا تو ورثہ کیلئے کچھ بھی نہیں ہے... اقوال فقہاء
واذا مات الزوجان قد سمى لها مهرا فلورثتها ان ياخذوا ذلك من ميراثه وان لم يسم لها مهرا فلا شئ لورثتها عند ابي حنيفة وقالا لورثتها المهر على الوجهين معناه المسمى في الوجه الاول و مهر المثل في الثاني اما الاول فلان المسمى دين في ذمته وقد تأكد بالموت فيقضى من تركته الا اذا علم انها ماتت اولا فيسقط نصيبه من ذلك و اما الثاني فوجه قولهما ان مهر المثل صار دينا في ذمته كالمسمى فلا يسقط بالموت كما اذا مات احد هما ولابي حنيفة ان موتهما يدل على انقراض اقرانهما فبمهر من يقدر القاضي مهر المثل
ترجمہ اور جب دونوں زوجین فوت ہو جائیں اور اس نے عورت کے لئے مہر مقرر کیا تھا تو اس کے ورثہ کے لئے (حق ہے کہ) وہ اس کی میراث سے لیں۔ اور اگر اس نے عورت کے لئے مہر مقرر نہیں کیا تھا تو اس کے ورثہ کے لئے کچھ نہیں ہے امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک۔ اور صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ عورت کے ورثہ کے لئے مہر ہے دونوں صورتوں میں۔ مطلب یہ ہے کہ پہلی صورت میں مہر مسمی اور دوسری صورت میں مہر مثل۔ پہلی صورت کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ مہر مسمی شوہر کے ذمہ قرض ہے اور وہ مرنے سے مقرر ہو گیا ہے تو اس کی ترکہ سے ادا کیا جائے گا مگر جب یہ معلوم ہو کہ عورت پہلے مر گئی تو اس کا حصہ ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ اور دوسری صورت میں صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مہر مثل بھی شوہر کے ذمہ واجب ہو گیا ہے جیسے مہر مسمی تو اس لئے مرنے سے ساقط نہیں ہوتا جیسے کہ جب دونوں میں سے ایک مر گیا (تو ساقط نہیں ہوا) اور ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ دونوں کا مرنا اس بات پر دلالت کرتا ہے کہ ان کے ہم عصر منقرض ہو گئے ہیں تو کس مہر کے ساتھ قاضی مہر مثل کا اندازہ کرے گا؟
The spouses died and the mahr was specified, so the wife's heirs take it from his inheritance. And if the mahr was not specified, then there is nothing for her heirs according to Abu Hanifa. Statements of jurists: And when both spouses die and he had specified for her a mahr, then her heirs have the right to take that from his inheritance. And if he did not specify a mahr for her, then there is nothing for her heirs according to Abu Hanifa. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say: for her heirs, there is mahr in both cases; meaning the specified mahr in the first case and mahr al-mithl in the second. As for the first, because the specified mahr is a debt in his liability and it is confirmed by death, so it is paid from his estate, except when it is known that she died first, then her share drops. As for the second, the proof of the two is that mahr al-mithl becomes a debt in his liability like the specified mahr, so it is not dropped by death, just as when one of them dies. And for Abu Hanifa, that their death indicates the extinction of their peers, so based on whose mahr will the judge estimate mahr al-mithl?
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage deals with the inheritance of mahr when both spouses have died. The key question: do the wife's heirs get anything from the husband's estate? If a mahr was specified, it is a debt on the husband's estate and the wife's heirs inherit it (unless she died first, in which case it drops). If no mahr was specified, Abu Hanifa says nothing is due to her heirs because the death of both makes it impossible to determine mahr al-mithl (no peers to compare). The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree: they say mahr al-mithl becomes a debt like the specified mahr and is not extinguished by death, analogizing to the case of one spouse dying. The rational proof for Abu Hanifa is that with both dead, there is no basis to determine mahr al-mithl—the 'peers' are extinct. The text also mentions that if the wife died first, her share of the specified mahr drops because her right to inheritance ceased.

Key Terms
ترکہ (tarkah): The estate left by the deceased husband, from which debts including mahr are paid before inheritance.
انقراض اقران (inqirāḍ aqrān): The extinction of peers, meaning no comparable women exist to determine mahr al-mithl when both spouses have died.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is Abu Hanifa's reason for saying that no mahr is due to the wife's heirs if both spouses die without a specified mahr?
A) Mahr al-mithl is not a debt.
B) The death of both indicates the extinction of peers, making estimation impossible.
C) The wife's heirs have no standing to claim.
D) Mahr al-mithl was already paid.

Key Takeaway
Specified mahr is a debt inherited by wife's heirs upon husband's death; unspecified mahr, according to Abu Hanifa, is not due because peers are extinct, but Sahibayn hold it remains a debt.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Heirs' Disagreement After Death Over Dower
Intra-Hanafi dispute on post-death dower disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on dower disputes after both spouses' death and identify the mufta bihi view.

Core Idea
After death, the husband's heirs may deny extra dower — but the fatwa favors mahr al-mithl.

When both spouses die and their heirs dispute the amount of dower, or whether it was specified at all, Hanafi imams differ. This lesson unpacks the reasoning of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad, and shows how the later fatwa aligns with the Sahibayn and other schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenarios
There are two sub-issues: dispute over the amount of the specified dower (miqdar al-musamma), and dispute over whether any dower was specified at all (asl al-musamma). Recognize that the passage covers both.
2
State each imam's position
For the amount dispute: Abu Hanifa accepts the husband's heirs' word with oath unconditionally; Abu Yusuf accepts it except when they claim a trivial amount; Muhammad holds that mahr al-mithl applies (as during life). For the specification dispute: Abu Hanifa again accepts the denier's word (husband's heirs), while Sahibayn rule for mahr al-mithl.
Trivial amount (shay' qalil) is defined by custom.
3
Analyze the proofs
Abu Hanifa relies on the general principle: the denier's word with oath is accepted in absence of evidence. Abu Yusuf excepts trivial claims based on a separate reasoning. Muhammad uses qiyas to the life-state. Note that the text mentions proofs are detailed in a later issue.
This is a procedural ruling, not a categorical obligation.
4
Identify the tarjih (preferred view)
The passage explicitly states that the fatwa is according to the Sahibayn and the three other imams (Malik, Shafi'i, Ahmad). Thus, mahr al-mithl is due in both sub-issues, though Shafi'i requires an additional oath procedure (tahaluf).
Tarjih authority: the text itself states 'fatwa is according to these scholars'.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
Under Abu Hanifa's view, the husband's heirs can deny any extra dower and owe nothing; under the relied-upon view, mahr al-mithl must be paid. This affects how judges decide actual inheritance cases.
The mufta bihi view protects the wife's heirs from potential injustice.

Translation: And if after the death of the spouses there is a dispute regarding the amount of the specified dower, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the statement of the husband's heirs will be accepted. And Imam Abu Hanifa does not make an exception for a small amount. And according to Abu Yusuf, the statement of the husband's heirs is accepted unless they mention a small amount. And according to Imam Muhammad, in this case the same ruling applies as in the case of life. And if there is a dispute regarding the actual specification, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the statement of the denier of specification will be accepted. The summary is that according to Imam Sahab, after the death of the spouses, mahr al-mithl will not be ruled. Based on evidence which we will mention later, God willing. Elaboration: This is the fourth scenario of the mentioned issue. The scenario is that after the death of the spouses, their heirs dispute regarding the amount of the specified dower. Regarding its ruling, there is disagreement among the Hanafis. Imam Abu Hanifa says: The statement of the husband's heirs with oath will be accepted. And Imam Abu Hanifa does not exclude a small amount. Rather, according to Imam Sahab, in any case the statement of the husband's heirs will be accepted, even if they claim a small amount. And according to Imam Abu Yusuf also, the statement of the husband's heirs will be accepted, but Abu Yusuf excludes a small amount. The summary is that if the husband's heirs claim a small amount, then according to Abu Yusuf it will not be accepted. And Imam Muhammad says that in this case the same ruling applies as was in the case of dispute during life. That is, just as during life mahr al-mithl was made the ruling, so after the death of both, mahr al-mithl will be the ruling. Imam Muhammad analogized the post-death state to the life state. And the proof of Abu Yusuf has already passed in the previous issue. The summary of Imam Abu Hanifa's proof is that the husband's heirs are deniers of extra dower. And in the absence of evidence, the statement of the denier with oath is accepted. Therefore, the statement of the husband's heirs with oath will be accepted. And if the spouses' heirs dispute regarding the actual specification, then Imam Sahab considers the statement of the denier of specification with oath as acceptable. But nothing will be obligatory upon the husband's heirs. And according to the Sahibayn, in this case mahr al-mithl will be adjudicated. Imam Malik, Imam Shafi'i, and Imam Ahmad are also of this view. And the fatwa is also according to these scholars. But Imam Shafi'i makes mahr al-mithl obligatory after tahaluf, while according to the Sahibayn, Imam Malik, and Imam Ahmad, tahaluf is not obligatory. The proofs of all have been mentioned in the next issue. Wait a little. And God knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the ruling when both spouses have died and their heirs disagree over the amount of the dower that was specified (mahr musamma). The discussion also covers the sub-case where the heirs dispute whether any dower was specified at all. The author first summarizes the positions: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the word of the husband's heirs is accepted with an oath, without any exception for a trivial amount. Imam Abu Yusuf agrees but excludes the case where the husband's heirs claim a trivial amount—such a claim is not accepted. Imam Muhammad likens the post-death scenario to the situation during the spouses' lifetimes, thus mahr al-mithl (proper dower) applies. The elaboration clarifies that this is the fourth scenario of a broader issue. The reasoning: Imam Abu Hanifa's basis is the general legal principle that the denier's word with oath is accepted in the absence of evidence; here, the husband's heirs are denying any increase in the dower. Regarding the dispute over whether a dower was specified, Imam Abu Hanifa again accepts the word of the one who denies the specification (i.e., the husband's heirs), and nothing is due from them. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) rule that mahr al-mithl is obligatory in both sub-cases. The passage notes that the great imams—Malik, Shafi'i, and Ahmad—agree with the Sahibayn, and the fatwa is based on their view. However, a difference remains: Shafi'i requires an oath-swearing procedure (tahaluf) before mahr al-mithl becomes due, while the others do not.

Key Terms
مقدار سمی (miqdar al-musamma): the specified amount of dower mentioned in the marriage contract
مہر مثل (mahr al-mithl): the proper dower, determined by the dower of female relatives of equal standing
شیء قلیل (shay' qalil): a trivial amount, specifically what is considered negligible in custom
منکر (munkir): the one who denies a claim; here, the husband's heirs denying a larger dower
قول مع الیمین (qawl ma'a al-yamin): the statement of the defendant supported by an oath

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what is the ruling when the heirs of the spouses dispute the amount of the specified dower after both have died?
A) The wife's heirs' word is accepted with oath.
B) The husband's heirs' word is accepted with oath, without any exception for a trivial amount.
C) The husband's heirs' word is accepted only if they do not claim a trivial amount.
D) Mahr al-mithl is determined by the judge.

Key Takeaway
After both spouses die, the mufta bihi Hanafi view is that mahr al-mithl is due when heirs dispute the dower, overriding Abu Hanifa's unconditional acceptance of the husband's heirs' word.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
10 min
Ruling on Dower When Both Spouses Die: Specified vs Unspecified
Intra-Hanafi dispute on mahr when both spouses die

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on dower when both spouses die, distinguish between specified and unspecified dower, and state the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf with its practical consequence.

Core Idea
When both spouses die without a specified dower, the wife's heirs get nothing according to Abu Hanifa, but the Sahibayn hold that mahr al-mithl is still due.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in marriage law (nikah): the fate of the dower (mahr) when both husband and wife die. The ruling depends critically on whether a dower was specified in the contract or not. While there is consensus on the specified dower becoming a confirmed debt, an intra-Hanafi dispute arises when no dower was agreed upon. We will explore the proofs of Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples (Sahibayn), and see which position is relied upon for fatwa today.

Guided Path
1
Identify the agreed ruling for specified dower
When a dower was specified (mahr musamma) and both spouses die, the wife's heirs take the full specified dower from the husband's estate, subject to adjustments if the wife died first.
This is agreed upon by all Hanafi imams.
2
Isolate the disputed scenario: no specified dower
If no dower was specified (mahr al-mithl), there is disagreement. First, clearly state Abu Hanifa's position and his proof.
3
State Abu Hanifa's position and proof
Abu Hanifa: No mahr al-mithl is due because the death of both spouses extinguishes their contemporaries (mu'asirin). The judge cannot estimate mahr al-mithl without a reference group, so obligation ceases.
Key argument: qiyas with impossibility of estimation.
4
State the Sahibayn's position and proof
Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): Mahr al-mithl is due as a debt in the husband's liability, analogous to the specified dower. Death does not cancel it, just as the death of one spouse does not cancel it.
They use two analogies: to specified dower and to the death of one spouse.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
Practical consequence: Under Abu Hanifa, wife's heirs get nothing; under Sahibayn, they receive mahr al-mithl. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of the Sahibayn.
The text mentions that the fatwa is according to Sahibayn and other imams.

جا سکتا ہے تو اس کا وجوب بھی نہیں ہو سکے گا۔
The spouses died and a dower was specified, so for the wife's heirs it is permissible to take that from his inheritance. If no dower was specified, then there is nothing for the wife's heirs according to Abu Hanifa. And the Sahibayn said: For the wife's heirs, in both cases there is a dower. Its meaning is: in the first case the specified dower, and in the second case mahr al-mithl. The first case: because the specified dower is a debt in the husband's liability, and due to death it becomes confirmed. So the specified dower will be paid from the husband's estate. The second case: the reason for the Sahibayn's statement is that mahr al-mithl becomes a debt in the husband's liability, like the specified dower. Therefore, it will not be cancelled due to death, just as when one of the two dies. And the proof of Abu Hanifa is that the death of both spouses indicates the extinction of their contemporaries. So with which woman's mahr will the judge estimate mahr al-mithl? Elaboration: The scenario is that both husband and wife have died. Now it is to be seen whether a specified dower existed for the wife or not. If a specified dower existed, then by agreement the wife's heirs will receive the dower from the husband's estate. And if there was no specified dower, then in this case, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, there is nothing for the wife's heirs. And according to the Sahibayn, in this case mahr al-mithl will be given. The summary is that according to the Sahibayn, in both cases there is a dower: in the case of specification, the specified dower; in the case of no specification, mahr al-mithl. The proof for the agreed-upon case is that the specified dower is a debt in the husband's liability. The proof of this debt would have been established by evidence or by mutual agreement of the spouses. In any case, the specified dower is a debt in the husband's liability. And due to death, the specified dower becomes confirmed because before death there was a possibility that the husband might give a divorce before consummation, and due to that the dower would be reduced to half. But after death, this possibility no longer remains. So when the specified dower becomes confirmed due to death, it will be paid from the husband's estate. However, if it is known that the wife died before the husband, then in this case the husband's share in this specified dower will be deducted, and the remainder will be given to the wife's heirs. The husband's share is: if the wife has children, the husband gets one-fourth of the estate; if the wife has no children, the husband gets one-half. In reality, there are four scenarios: First, both spouses died at the same time and this is known. Second, it is not known who died first. Third, it is known that the husband died first. In these three scenarios, the wife's heirs will be given the entire specified dower from the husband's estate. Fourth, it is known that the wife died first. Then in this case, the husband's share of inheritance from this specified dower is deducted and the remainder is given to the wife's heirs. In the disputed case, the Sahibayn's proof is that just as the specified dower is a debt in the husband's liability, similarly mahr al-mithl is also a debt in the husband's liability. Therefore, just as the specified dower is not cancelled due to death, similarly mahr al-mithl will not be cancelled due to death. The Sahibayn made a second analogy: The validity of mahr al-mithl is not cancelled by the death of one of the spouses; similarly, it will not be cancelled by the death of both. Imam Sahab's proof is that the death of both spouses indicates the extinction of their contemporaries. And the judge estimates mahr al-mithl based on the dower of women of her age and time. So when the judge does not find any of her contemporary women, how can he estimate her mahr al-mithl? And when mahr al-mithl cannot be estimated, its obligation cannot occur.
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on the dower (mahr) when both spouses die. It is divided into two cases: (1) where a dower was specified (mahr musamma) and (2) where no dower was specified. In the first case, there is consensus (ittifaq) that the wife's heirs take the specified dower from the husband's estate, as it becomes a confirmed debt upon death. However, careful consideration is given to the order of death: if the wife died first, the husband's inheritance share (e.g., one-fourth if she had children, one-half if not) is deducted from the specified dower before the wife's heirs receive it. In the second case, an intra-Hanafi dispute arises. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the wife's heirs receive nothing because the death of both spouses indicates the extinction of their contemporaries (mu'asirin); without any contemporary women to serve as reference, the judge cannot estimate mahr al-mithl, and therefore its obligation ceases. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue that mahr al-mithl, like the specified dower, is a debt in the husband's liability and is not cancelled by death. They analogize to the case where only one spouse dies, which does not cancel mahr al-mithl. The commentary elaborates on the logic of both positions and notes the practical consequences.

Key Terms
مہر سمی (mahr musamma): the dower explicitly specified in the marriage contract
مہر مثل (mahr al-mithl): the proper dower estimated by the dower of equivalent women
دین (dayn): debt; the dower becomes a debt in the husband's liability
موکد (mu'akkad): confirmed; the specified dower becomes confirmed upon death
معاصرین (mu'asirin): contemporaries; women of the same age and time for estimating mahr al-mithl

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi view in the Hanafi school, what do the wife's heirs receive when both spouses die without a specified dower?
A) Nothing
B) Mahr al-mithl (the proper dower)
C) Half of the estimated dower
D) The marriage is nullified

Key Takeaway
When both spouses die without a specified dower, the relied-upon Hanafi position (Sahibayn) is that mahr al-mithl is due from the husband's estate.

Specified Mahr When Both Spouses Die: The Agreed Ruling
Ruling with proof on specified mahr after both spouses die

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on specified mahr when both spouses die and explain the four scenarios affecting its distribution.

Core Idea
Specified mahr is a debt that survives both deaths; only the wife dying first reduces it.

When both spouses die, the specified mahr (mahr musamma) remains a debt on the husband's estate. This lesson clarifies the agreed Hanafi position that the wife's heirs are entitled to the full mahr unless the wife died first, in which case the husband's inheritance share is deducted. We will examine the four scenarios of death timing.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the debt status of specified mahr
Understand that specified mahr is a debt on the husband, proved by evidence or mutual agreement. Death makes it binding beyond possibility of reduction.
Before death, husband could divorce before consummation and pay only half.
2
Identify the four scenarios of death timing
List the four possibilities: both die simultaneously, unknown order, husband dies first, wife dies first.
The first three result in full payment to wife's heirs.
3
Apply the deduction rule when wife dies first
When wife dies first, the husband inherits a share from her estate (1/4 if she has children, 1/2 if not). This share is deducted from the specified mahr before handing the rest to her heirs.
This mirrors the rule for inheritance of mahr when the wife predeceases.
4
Explain why death affirms the mahr
Death removes the possibility of divorce before consummation, which would halve the mahr. Thus, the mahr becomes fully owed.
This is the reason given in the text: 'بسبب الموت يتأكد'.
5
State the agreed ruling concisely
Unless the wife dies first, the wife's heirs receive the full specified mahr from the husband's estate. If she dies first, the husband's inheritance share is subtracted.
This is the unanimous position of the Hanafi school.

And when both spouses have died while the woman's mahr was specified, it is permissible for the woman's heirs to take that mahr from the husband's inheritance. If the mahr was not specified, then according to Abu Hanifa there is nothing for the woman's heirs. The Sahibayn said that in both cases there is mahr for the woman's heirs. Meaning: in the first case it is the specified mahr, and in the second case it is the mahr of the like. In the first case, because the specified mahr is a debt owed by the husband, and due to death it becomes affirmed. So the specified mahr will be decreed from the husband's estate. In the second case, the Sahibayn's argument is that the mahr of the like becomes a debt on the husband, similar to the specified mahr, so it is not dropped due to death, just as when one of them dies. Abu Hanifa's evidence is that the death of both spouses indicates the end of their contemporaries. With whose mahr will the judge estimate the mahr of the like? Explanation: The case is that both husband and wife have died. It is then examined whether the woman had a specified mahr or not. If she had a specified mahr, then by agreement the woman's heirs will collect the mahr from the husband's estate. If she had no specified mahr, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa there is nothing for the woman's heirs; according to the Sahibayn, in this case there is a mahr of the like. In short, according to the Sahibayn, in both cases there is mahr: if specified it is the specified mahr, if unspecified it is the mahr of the like. The evidence for the agreed-upon issue: The specified mahr is a debt owed by the husband. This debt is proven either by evidence or by mutual agreement. In any case, the specified mahr is a debt on the husband, and death makes it affirmed because before death there was the possibility that the husband might divorce before consummation, leaving half the mahr, but after death this possibility no longer exists. So when the specified mahr is affirmed by death, it will be decreed from the husband's estate. However, if it is known that the wife died before the husband, then the husband's share from the specified mahr is dropped. The husband's share is: if the wife has children, the husband gets one-fourth; if the wife has no children, the husband gets one-half. In fact, there are four scenarios: (1) Both died at the same time and this is known. (2) It is not known who died first. (3) It is known that the husband died first. In these three cases, the woman's heirs are given the full specified mahr from the husband's estate. (4) It is known that the wife died first. In this case, the husband's share of inheritance is taken out from the specified mahr, and the rest is given to the woman's heirs. In the disputed case, the Sahibayn's evidence: Just as the specified mahr is a debt on the husband, similarly the mahr of the like is a debt on the husband. So just as the specified mahr is not dropped due to death, the mahr of the like is also not dropped due to death. The Sahibayn made another analogy: The death of one spouse does not invalidate the mahr of the like, so the death of both also does not invalidate it. Imam Sahib's evidence: The death of both spouses indicates the end of their contemporaries. And the judge estimates the mahr of the like based on the mahr of women of her age and time. When the judge does not find any of her contemporaries, how can he estimate her mahr of the like? And when it cannot be estimated, its obligation cannot exist. However, if the era is not old and much time has not passed, then the mahr of the like will be decreed. Some mashayikh have stated a fine point on behalf of Imam Sahib: They say that the mahr of the like is the price of the vulva, so it resembles the specified mahr because the specified mahr is also the price of the vulva. And since the mahr of the like is in exchange for non-property (usufruct of the vulva), it resembles a gift (silah). For example, maintenance (nafaqah) is a gift from the husband. The specified mahr is not dropped by the death of both spouses nor by the death of one. The gift (maintenance) is dropped by the death of both spouses and also by the death of one. Now if in the mahr of the like only the resemblance to the specified mahr is considered, then it should not drop in either case—neither by death of both nor by death of one. If only the resemblance to maintenance is considered, then it should drop in both cases. But we, considering both resemblances, say: Since the mahr of the like resembles the specified mahr, it is not dropped by the death of one spouse; and since it resembles a gift (maintenance), it is dropped by the death of both spouses. And Allah knows best (Fath al-Qadir).
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the ruling of mahr when both spouses die. It first states the agreed position: if a specified mahr (mahr musamma) was fixed, it is a debt on the husband and must be paid to the wife's heirs from his estate. Death affirms it because the possibility of divorce before consummation (which would halve it) is removed. The nuance is that if the wife dies first, the husband's share of inheritance (as heir) is deducted from that mahr. Four scenarios are delineated: simultaneous death, unknown order, husband first, wife first—in the first three the full mahr goes to wife's heirs; in the last, husband's share is subtracted. The dispute arises when no mahr was specified. Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the wife's heirs are entitled to mahr mithl (mahr of the like), just as in the specified case, because mahr mithl also becomes a debt. They analogize to the case where one spouse dies—there mahr mithl is due, so when both die it should also be due. Abu Hanifa argues that when both die, there are no contemporaries of the wife left to estimate mahr mithl, so it cannot be determined and thus is not owed. He considers the practical impossibility of estimation. Some later scholars refine this: if the time is recent, estimation is still possible, so mahr mithl is due. A sophisticated note from some mashayikh synthesizes two resemblances: mahr mithl is like specified mahr in being the price of vulva (so not dropped by one spouse's death) and like maintenance (nafaqah) in being for usufruct (so dropped by both deaths). Hence the compromise: mahr mithl is not dropped when one dies (like specified mahr) but is dropped when both die (like maintenance). This is the relied-upon view. The passage ends with 'Wallahu a'lam' and a reference to Fath al-Qadir indicating the tarjih.

Key Terms
مهر مسمى (mahr musamma): The mahr explicitly agreed upon and specified at the time of marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which scenario does the husband's inheritance share get deducted from the specified mahr?
A) When both die simultaneously.
B) When it is unknown who died first.
C) When the wife dies first.
D) When the husband dies first.

Key Takeaway
Specified mahr is a debt that survives the death of both spouses; only the wife predeceasing the husband triggers a deduction of his inheritance share.

Mahr Mithl When Both Spouses Die: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute with qiyas reasoning on mahr mithl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding mahr mithl when both spouses die and state the compromise view that became mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Mahr mithl resembles both specified mahr and nafaqah; thus it drops only when both die.

When no mahr was specified and both spouses die, the Hanafi school is divided. Abu Hanifa denies any mahr, citing the impossibility of estimating mahr mithl without contemporaries. The Sahibayn analogize to specified mahr, arguing it is a debt that should not drop. Later mashayikh reconcile by considering two resemblances: mahr mithl is like specified mahr (not dropped by one death) and like nafaqah (dropped by both deaths). This lesson unpacks that reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and the two positions
The issue is whether mahr mithl is due when both spouses die without specifying a mahr. Abu Hanifa says no; Sahibayn say yes.
The dispute is only about mahr mithl, not specified mahr (which is agreed).
2
Analyze Abu Hanifa's evidence
He argues that both spouses' deaths eliminate their contemporaries, making estimation of mahr mithl impossible. Without estimation, obligation cannot arise.
The text mentions 'انقطاع المعاصرين' (cessation of contemporaries).
3
Analyze the Sahibayn's evidence using qiyas
They analogize mahr mithl to specified mahr: both are debts on the husband. Just as specified mahr does not drop by death, mahr mithl should not drop. They also analogize to the case where one spouse dies (mahr mithl is due there).
Two analogies are used: with specified mahr and with the case of one death.
4
Understand the reconciliation by later mashayikh
They note that mahr mithl has two aspects: as a price for the vulva (like specified mahr) and as a gift/exchange for usufruct (like nafaqah). Specified mahr does not drop on one death; nafaqah drops on both deaths. So mahr mithl drops only when both die.
This is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position.
5
State the mufta bihi ruling
If only one spouse dies, mahr mithl is due. If both die, it is not due. This balances the two resemblances.
Also, if time is recent and contemporaries still exist, some authorities say mahr mithl may still be due even if both die.

ہوگا اور چونکہ صلہ یعنی نفقہ کے ساتھ مشابہت رکھتا ہے اسلئے زوجین کی موت سے مہر مثل ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب (فتح القدير)
And when both spouses have died while the woman's mahr was specified, it is permissible for the woman's heirs to take that mahr from the husband's inheritance. If the mahr was not specified, then according to Abu Hanifa there is nothing for the woman's heirs. The Sahibayn said that in both cases there is mahr for the woman's heirs. Meaning: in the first case it is the specified mahr, and in the second case it is the mahr of the like. In the first case, because the specified mahr is a debt owed by the husband, and due to death it becomes affirmed. So the specified mahr will be decreed from the husband's estate. In the second case, the Sahibayn's argument is that the mahr of the like becomes a debt on the husband, similar to the specified mahr, so it is not dropped due to death, just as when one of them dies. Abu Hanifa's evidence is that the death of both spouses indicates the end of their contemporaries. With whose mahr will the judge estimate the mahr of the like? Explanation: The case is that both husband and wife have died. It is then examined whether the woman had a specified mahr or not. If she had a specified mahr, then by agreement the woman's heirs will collect the mahr from the husband's estate. If she had no specified mahr, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa there is nothing for the woman's heirs; according to the Sahibayn, in this case there is a mahr of the like. In short, according to the Sahibayn, in both cases there is mahr: if specified it is the specified mahr, if unspecified it is the mahr of the like. The evidence for the agreed-upon issue: The specified mahr is a debt owed by the husband. This debt is proven either by evidence or by mutual agreement. In any case, the specified mahr is a debt on the husband, and death makes it affirmed because before death there was the possibility that the husband might divorce before consummation, leaving half the mahr, but after death this possibility no longer exists. So when the specified mahr is affirmed by death, it will be decreed from the husband's estate. However, if it is known that the wife died before the husband, then the husband's share from the specified mahr is dropped. The husband's share is: if the wife has children, the husband gets one-fourth; if the wife has no children, the husband gets one-half. In fact, there are four scenarios: (1) Both died at the same time and this is known. (2) It is not known who died first. (3) It is known that the husband died first. In these three cases, the woman's heirs are given the full specified mahr from the husband's estate. (4) It is known that the wife died first. In this case, the husband's share of inheritance is taken out from the specified mahr, and the rest is given to the woman's heirs. In the disputed case, the Sahibayn's evidence: Just as the specified mahr is a debt on the husband, similarly the mahr of the like is a debt on the husband. So just as the specified mahr is not dropped due to death, the mahr of the like is also not dropped due to death. The Sahibayn made another analogy: The death of one spouse does not invalidate the mahr of the like, so the death of both also does not invalidate it. Imam Sahib's evidence: The death of both spouses indicates the end of their contemporaries. And the judge estimates the mahr of the like based on the mahr of women of her age and time. When the judge does not find any of her contemporaries, how can he estimate her mahr of the like? And when it cannot be estimated, its obligation cannot exist. However, if the era is not old and much time has not passed, then the mahr of the like will be decreed. Some mashayikh have stated a fine point on behalf of Imam Sahib: They say that the mahr of the like is the price of the vulva, so it resembles the specified mahr because the specified mahr is also the price of the vulva. And since the mahr of the like is in exchange for non-property (usufruct of the vulva), it resembles a gift (silah). For example, maintenance (nafaqah) is a gift from the husband. The specified mahr is not dropped by the death of both spouses nor by the death of one. The gift (maintenance) is dropped by the death of both spouses and also by the death of one. Now if in the mahr of the like only the resemblance to the specified mahr is considered, then it should not drop in either case—neither by death of both nor by death of one. If only the resemblance to maintenance is considered, then it should drop in both cases. But we, considering both resemblances, say: Since the mahr of the like resembles the specified mahr, it is not dropped by the death of one spouse; and since it resembles a gift (maintenance), it is dropped by the death of both spouses. And Allah knows best (Fath al-Qadir).
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the ruling of mahr when both spouses die. It first states the agreed position: if a specified mahr (mahr musamma) was fixed, it is a debt on the husband and must be paid to the wife's heirs from his estate. Death affirms it because the possibility of divorce before consummation (which would halve it) is removed. The nuance is that if the wife dies first, the husband's share of inheritance (as heir) is deducted from that mahr. Four scenarios are delineated: simultaneous death, unknown order, husband first, wife first—in the first three the full mahr goes to wife's heirs; in the last, husband's share is subtracted. The dispute arises when no mahr was specified. Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the wife's heirs are entitled to mahr mithl (mahr of the like), just as in the specified case, because mahr mithl also becomes a debt. They analogize to the case where one spouse dies—there mahr mithl is due, so when both die it should also be due. Abu Hanifa argues that when both die, there are no contemporaries of the wife left to estimate mahr mithl, so it cannot be determined and thus is not owed. He considers the practical impossibility of estimation. Some later scholars refine this: if the time is recent, estimation is still possible, so mahr mithl is due. A sophisticated note from some mashayikh synthesizes two resemblances: mahr mithl is like specified mahr in being the price of vulva (so not dropped by one spouse's death) and like maintenance (nafaqah) in being for usufruct (so dropped by both deaths). Hence the compromise: mahr mithl is not dropped when one dies (like specified mahr) but is dropped when both die (like maintenance). This is the relied-upon view. The passage ends with 'Wallahu a'lam' and a reference to Fath al-Qadir indicating the tarjih.

Key Terms
مهر مثل (mahr mithl): The mahr of a woman similar in status to the wife, used when no mahr was specified.
صاحبين (Sahibayn): Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, the two chief disciples of Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the compromise view, what happens to mahr mithl when both spouses die?
A) It is due because it resembles specified mahr.
B) It is dropped because it resembles nafaqah.
C) It is divided between the heirs.
D) It is due only if the wife died first.

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi view on mahr mithl when both spouses die is that it drops because of its resemblance to nafaqah, but it remains due if only one spouse dies.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
6 min
Dispute Over Goods: Mahr or Gift?
Ruling with proof on dispute over goods sent to wife.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the default evidentiary rule and its exception in a dispute over whether goods sent to the wife are mahr or gift, and apply the Hanafi principle of mumallik.

Core Idea
Husband's word prevails as mumallik, except for ready-to-eat food where custom gives wife's word weight.

When a husband sends goods to his wife, and they later dispute whether these were mahr or a gift, the Hanafi school provides a clear rule based on the principle that the one who transfers ownership (mumallik) knows his intention best. However, an important exception arises for perishable food items, where custom (urf) shifts the credibility to the wife. This lesson unpacks the default rule, its reasoning, and the role of custom in overriding the presumption.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default rule
When the husband sends goods and a dispute arises, the husband's word (with oath) is taken over the wife's. Understand that this is an evidentiary rule for resolving disputes.
The rule is based on the husband being the mumallik.
2
Understand the reasoning (mumallik principle)
The husband is the one who made the wife owner of the goods. He knows best whether he intended a gift or payment of mahr. Additionally, the natural tendency is to discharge a wajib (mahr) before giving voluntary gifts.
This parallels the principle 'al-qaulu li-man huwa al-mumallik'.
3
Recognize the exception for food
For food that is ready to be eaten (e.g., cooked meat, perishable fruits), the wife's word is accepted. The reason is that custom (urf) treats such items as gifts, so the presumption flips.
This exception is from Imam Muhammad in al-Jami' al-Saghir.
4
Apply the custom distinction
Distinguish between ready-to-eat food (wife's word) and staple grains like wheat and barley (husband's word). The ruling depends on prevalent custom.
If custom changes in a different time or place, the ruling may shift accordingly.
5
Note the sub-rule on obligatory items
The husband cannot count obligatory maintenance items (e.g., khimar, dir') as part of the mahr, because the apparent purpose contradicts claiming them as mahr.
This sub-rule reinforces that the husband's claim is subject to contextual reasonableness.
